# docs/canon/glossary.yml

```yml
# Canonical glossary. Schema: docs/canon/README.md#glossaryyml
#
# Stage: canonical-decision pass complete (2026-04-26).
# Every entry has `canonical:` set to one of its `aliases:` (the spelling
# every artifact should prefer), `definition:` filled with a formal
# 1–3-sentence statement suitable for citation, and `notes:` recording
# the rationale of the canonical choice plus any usage guidance for
# non-canonical aliases that remain valid in specific contexts.
#
# Note on `type_hash:` fields (T2.a, 2026-05-25):
#   The canonical source for cell-type identity is now
#   `cartridges/<cartridge>/cartridge.json` `cellTypes[]` entries.
#   `type_hash` values in this file were regenerated by computing
#   `sha256(s1:s2:s3:s4)` over the manifest triple — D11/D12 unified
#   shape, .v1 suffix dropped.  The OLD-format hashes used by
#   `runtime/legacy-ingest` (`whatPath:howSlug:instPath` with `.v1`/`.v2`)
#   are pinned for drift-detection in
#   `core/experience-cartridge/src/__tests__/typehash-parity.test.ts`
#   (Q11-C).  See `docs/design/STRUCTURED-TYPEHASH-CANONICAL.md` for full
#   context.  `canonical:` / `aliases:` / `definition:` fields below
#   still use `.v1` suffixes — incremental cleanup per D12 in a follow-up
#   doc pass; the `type_hash:` hex is authoritative.
#
# Decision principles:
#   1. Codebase usage in production paths is the strongest signal.
#   2. Whitepaper v3 + paper A1 usage is the secondary signal.
#   3. Conciseness wins ties; descriptive wins over generic.
#   4. Initialisms (BRC-100, MFP, SIR, OIR) are canonical for the short
#      form; the expanded name is acceptable on first introduction.
#   5. CamelCase type names (SignedBundle) are canonical for code
#      contexts; English form (signed bundle) is the prose form of the
#      same concept and not a separate aliasing decision.
#   6. snake_case identifiers (cert_id, domain_flag) are canonical for
#      wire formats and YAML; camelCase is the TS convention for the
#      same field.
#
# Sort: by `id`, alphabetical. Preserve when editing.
#
# Source of variants: doc plan §1.4, unification roadmap, refactor-monoliths
# rename PRDs (especially 00A-facet-to-hat-rename.md), the codebase paths
# already cited in the unification roadmap §9, the Plexus Tech v1.3 PDF.

entries:
  - id: adapter
    canonical: adapter
    aliases:
      - adapter
      - surface
    short: |
      A consumer of the substrate that delivers user-facing capability
      (e.g. World Host, Helm, Md Editor). Per the unification roadmap §2,
      this is where ⚠ and ✗ cells cluster — substrate is ✓ by construction;
      adapters are where unification work concentrates.
    definition: |
      An *adapter* is one of the named consumer surfaces in the
      unification matrix that exposes substrate capability to a user-,
      operator-, or peer-facing context. Adapters compose substrate
      components but never provide substrate primitives themselves; they
      are the integration layer where unification work concentrates.
    sources:
      - docs/prd/SEMANTOS-UNIFICATION-ROADMAP.md
      - docs/EXTENSIONS-VS-TYPES.md
    notes: |
      Reserved "surface" for "surface grammar" (Lisp surface, LaTeX
      surface, etc. — meaning "input syntax for the SIR layer"), where it
      means something distinct. Calling everything an "adapter" reduces
      ambiguity. The unification roadmap will be cleaned up to use
      "adapter" everywhere it currently says "surface" in the matrix
      sense.
      SUPERSEDED (Wave Canonical-Cartridge, 2026-05-18): "adapter" is no
      longer a distinct concept — an infra cartridge (role: infra) that
      `provides` an adapter interface is the canonical form. See the
      `cartridge` entry + textbook Ch.37.

  - id: cartridge
    canonical: cartridge
    aliases:
      - cartridge
      - extension
      - app
      - world-app
      - adapter
    short: |
      THE unit of installable capability. "App", "extension",
      "world-app" and "adapter" are no longer distinct concepts — every
      one is a *cartridge*, classified by `role`
      (infra | experience | grammar-lexicon), described by one
      `cartridge.json`, owned by an affine PushDrop license UTXO, and
      loaded by both the Brain shell and the PWA shell.
    definition: |
      A *cartridge* is the single canonical packaging + ownership +
      composition unit. It has one manifest (`cartridge.json` — the
      evolved ExtensionManifest), a `role` (infra cartridges `provides`
      adapter interfaces; experience cartridges have a PWA surface;
      grammar-lexicon cartridges are pure vocabulary), a Brain part and
      a PWA-experience part bound by the manifest's
      `experience.flutterPackage`, composes other cartridges only via
      typed `consumes`/`provides` (never an `extends` edge), and is
      owned by the key its affine PushDrop license UTXO is P2PK-locked
      to (acquisition = an atomic pay-for-rights tx; revocation = spend;
      gated at load by the proven K15/SW2 SPV path). The Brain shell
      resolves + license-gates + serves cartridges and advertises them
      at `/api/v1/info`; the PWA shell renders them via a registry every
      experience self-registers into.
    sources:
      - docs/design/CANONICAL-CARTRIDGE-MODEL.md
      - docs/design/CARTRIDGE-MARKETPLACE-OWNERSHIP.md
      - docs/design/SELLABLE-NODE-LICENSE.md
      - docs/canon/commissions/wave-canonical-cartridge.md
    notes: |
      RATIFIED C1–C6 (Todd 2026-05-17). "App"/"extension"/"world-app"/
      "adapter" remain valid only as informal English for a cartridge of
      the corresponding role; canonical artifacts say "cartridge". The
      old `adapter` entry is retained but superseded (an adapter = an
      infra cartridge that `provides`). Textbook Ch.37 is the narrative;
      Ch.15/28/31 are reframed (banners) to this model.

  - id: anf
    canonical: ANF
    aliases:
      - ANF
      - A-normal form
    short: |
      A-normal form — the intermediate-form discipline used by OIR. Every
      sub-expression is bound to a name; no nested computation in operand
      position.
    definition: |
      *ANF* (A-normal form) is the intermediate-form discipline used by
      OIR in which every non-trivial sub-expression is bound to a named
      variable, and operand positions hold only names or constants. ANF
      makes data-flow explicit and continuations sequential, simplifying
      lowering to bytecode.
    sources:
      - core/semantos-ir/
      - docs/PIPELINE.md
    notes: |
      "ANF" is the universal short form in the PL literature; expand to
      "A-normal form" only on first introduction in any new artifact.

  - id: avatar
    canonical: avatar
    aliases:
      - avatar
      - LINEAR cube
      - cube
    short: |
      A user-controlled entity in a World Host region. Currently realised
      as a LINEAR cube: identity-bound (color from the cert's public key),
      session-controlled, server-authoritative.
    definition: |
      An *avatar* is a user-controlled WorldEntity in a World Host
      region — an OTP-process-backed object whose state is mutated only
      by intents authored by the controlling user's BRC-52 cert.
      Currently rendered as a LINEAR cube whose colour is derived from
      the controlling cert's public key.
    sources:
      - apps/world-host/lib/world_host/avatar.ex
      - apps/world-client/src/entity.ts
      - core/cube-object/src/cube-mesh.ts
    notes: |
      "Cube" is a rendering-implementation artefact; "LINEAR cube" is the
      current shorthand combining linearity class with the rendering. The
      concept is "avatar"; what it looks like is a separate, replaceable
      decision.

  - id: bca
    canonical: BCA
    aliases:
      - BCA
      - Blockchain Channel Address
    short: |
      Address derived from a cert_id, used as a peer identifier in the
      mesh and as the channel-funding key for MFP payment channels.
    definition: |
      A *BCA* (Blockchain Channel Address) is a deterministic
      cert-derived IPv6-shaped address used as a peer identifier in the
      mesh and as the channel-funding key for MFP payment channels. The
      derivation is implemented in `core/cell-engine/src/bca.zig` with
      conformance vectors at `core/cell-engine/tests/vectors/bca_*.json`;
      a TS mirror is the D-A0 deliverable.
    sources:
      - core/cell-engine/src/bca.zig
      - core/cell-engine/tests/vectors/bca_*.json
    notes: |
      "BCA" canonical; expand to "Blockchain Channel Address" only on
      first introduction. The D-A0 deliverable proposes a shared TS BCA
      library mirroring the Zig implementation.

  - id: beef
    canonical: BEEF
    aliases:
      - BEEF
    short: |
      Background Evaluation Extended Format — the SPV envelope format
      used by Plexus and Semantos to carry transactions with merkle
      proofs, enabling indexer-less verification.
    definition: |
      *BEEF* (Background Evaluation Extended Format, BRC-62) is the wire
      envelope that carries one or more transactions together with the
      merkle paths required to verify them via SPV. Pairs with BUMP
      (the merkle-proof shape itself); BRC-95 atomic-BEEF is the
      single-transaction-focused variant with a `0x01010101` prefix.
    sources:
      - docs/Semantos-Protocol-Spec-v0.01.docx
      - "Plexus Tech §4 (Network SDK), §11 (Recovery Service)"
    notes: |
      Single canonical name; no alias variation in production use.

  - id: boot-sequence
    canonical: boot sequence
    aliases:
      - boot sequence
      - 15-step boot
      - sovereign-node boot
    short: |
      The 15-step canonical boot of a sovereign node from email +
      challenges through recoverable, federated, metered, K1–K10-compliant
      online state. The unifying narrative of the documentation and the
      gating milestone for textbook publication.
    definition: |
      The *boot sequence* is the canonical 15-step procedure that takes
      a sovereign node from cold start (operator email + recovery
      challenges) through recoverable, federated, metered, fully
      K1–K10-compliant online state. The sequence is the unifying
      narrative of the documentation and the gating milestone for
      textbook publication; the canon's `boot-sequence.yml` is its
      authoritative form.
    sources:
      - docs/prd/SEMANTOS-UNIFICATION-ROADMAP.md
      - docs/canon/boot-sequence.yml
    notes: |
      Canonical "boot sequence" rather than "15-step boot" — the count
      could change as the substrate evolves. The 15-step framing is
      tied to the current Unification Matrix snapshot.

  - id: brc-100
    canonical: BRC-100
    aliases:
      - BRC-100
    short: |
      The signed-request standard. Every cross-process or cross-node
      message in the unified architecture is a BRC-100 signed envelope,
      carrying x-brc100-identitykey, x-brc100-nonce, x-brc100-timestamp,
      x-brc100-signature, and x-brc52-certificate.
    definition: |
      *BRC-100* is the BSV signed-request standard. Every cross-process
      and cross-node message in the unified architecture is wrapped in a
      BRC-100 envelope carrying `x-brc100-identitykey`,
      `x-brc100-nonce`, `x-brc100-timestamp`, `x-brc100-signature`, and
      `x-brc52-certificate`. The Verifier Sidecar enforces validity at
      every adapter boundary.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §1, §4, §8"
      - core/plexus-contracts/src/transport.ts
    notes: |
      Single canonical name; no alias variation in production use.

  - id: brc-103
    canonical: BRC-103
    aliases:
      - BRC-103
    short: |
      Mutual-authentication handshake. Used to bind an edge-creation
      transcript and to prevent Trust-On-First-Use vulnerabilities at
      the start of recovery sessions.
    definition: |
      *BRC-103* is the mutual-authentication handshake protocol used to
      bind an edge-creation transcript and to prevent
      Trust-On-First-Use vulnerabilities at the start of recovery
      sessions.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §4, §11, §12"
    notes: |
      Single canonical name; no alias variation in production use.

  - id: brc-108
    canonical: BRC-108
    aliases:
      - BRC-108
      - Identity-Linked Token Protocol
    short: |
      The identity-linked token format used for capability UTXOs.
      Spending a capability UTXO atomically revokes the capability —
      they're treated as LINEAR semantic resources.
    definition: |
      *BRC-108* (the Identity-Linked Token Protocol) defines the wire
      format for capability tokens — UTXOs whose locking script binds
      the token to a BRC-52 cert subject and whose spending atomically
      revokes the capability. Capability tokens under BRC-108 are
      modelled in Semantos as LINEAR semantic resources.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §6, §7"
      - core/plexus-contracts/src/transport.ts
    notes: |
      "BRC-108" canonical; expand to "Identity-Linked Token Protocol"
      only on first introduction.

  - id: brc-42
    canonical: BRC-42
    aliases:
      - BRC-42
    short: |
      Client-side key derivation. Used for both root-seed reconstruction
      (PBKDF2 100k iterations) and deterministic child derivation under
      a parent cert.
    definition: |
      *BRC-42* (BSV Key Derivation Scheme) is the standard for
      deterministic client-side key derivation used throughout Plexus
      identity flows: root-seed reconstruction (PBKDF2, 100 000
      iterations, against the recovery challenge set) and deterministic
      child derivation under a parent cert.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §1, §4, §10"
      - core/plexus-vendor-sdk/src/crypto.ts
    notes: |
      Single canonical name; no alias variation in production use.

  - id: brc-43
    canonical: BRC-43
    aliases:
      - BRC-43
    short: |
      The custom-opcode range allocation protocol that Semantos uses to
      claim 0x4C–0xD0 (formerly described as 0xC0–0xCF in v0.01 spec —
      reconciliation pending).
    definition: |
      *BRC-43* is the BSV standard for security levels, protocol IDs,
      key IDs, and counterparty-namespacing of derived keys. Semantos
      uses BRC-43 to claim the Plexus extension opcode range and to
      partition derived-key namespaces by domain flag.
    sources:
      - docs/Semantos-Protocol-Spec-v0.01.docx
    notes: |
      Doc plan §1.2 flags the 0xC0–0xCF (v0.01 spec) vs 0x4C–0xD0
      (current Zig source) range mismatch as needing reconciliation.
      Resolved by reading core/cell-engine/src/opcodes.zig (canonical)
      when filling opcodes.yml. The BRC-43 entry itself is unaffected;
      the range it claims is a separate fact.

  - id: brc-52
    canonical: BRC-52
    aliases:
      - BRC-52
      - cert
      - certificate
    short: |
      The certificate ID standard. A BRC-52 cert encodes a 33-byte
      compressed public key, parent cert ref, and field set; SHA-256 of
      the canonical preimage is the cert_id, the user's identity hash.
    definition: |
      *BRC-52* (Identity Certificates) is the standard for the
      certificate format used as the unit of identity in the Plexus DAG.
      A BRC-52 cert encodes a 33-byte compressed public key, an issuer
      cert reference, an app ID, a child index, and a field set. The
      SHA-256 of the canonical preimage is the cert's `cert_id` — the
      stable identity hash the user node is known by.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §1, §9, §15"
      - core/plexus-contracts/src/identity.ts
    notes: |
      "BRC-52" is the formal canonical for the standard. "BRC-52 cert"
      and "certificate" are acceptable in formal prose; "cert" is fine
      informally. The hash is `cert_id` (snake_case) on the wire and in
      Zig; `certId` (camelCase) in TS by convention.

  - id: brc-69
    canonical: BRC-69
    aliases:
      - BRC-69
      - edge backup recipe
    short: |
      Key linkage revelation recipe — the mathematical "recipe" stored
      by Plexus's recovery layer that lets a recovering device
      reconstruct an ECDH shared secret without Plexus ever knowing it.
    definition: |
      *BRC-69* (Revealing Key Linkages) defines the mathematical recipe
      stored by Plexus Recovery that lets a recovering device
      reconstruct a previously-established ECDH shared secret without
      Plexus ever holding the secret itself. This is the substrate
      mechanism behind edge recoverability.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §12, §26"
    notes: |
      "BRC-69" canonical; "edge backup recipe" is the descriptive name
      for what BRC-69 encodes and is acceptable in narrative prose.

  - id: brc-94
    canonical: BRC-94
    aliases:
      - BRC-94
    short: |
      Verifiable revelation of shared secrets via Schnorr — the
      zero-knowledge edge-presence proof used in attestations.
    definition: |
      *BRC-94* defines verifiable revelation of shared secrets using a
      Schnorr-protocol-based zero-knowledge proof. Used in Plexus as
      the edge-presence proof underlying attestations.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §3, §11"
    notes: |
      Single canonical name; no alias variation in production use.

  - id: bump
    canonical: BUMP
    aliases:
      - BUMP
    short: |
      The merkle-proof format that pairs with BEEF for indexer-less SPV
      verification. Phase 1 of the three-phase verification pipeline.
    definition: |
      *BUMP* (BSV Unified Merkle Path, BRC-74) is the merkle-proof
      format that pairs with BEEF to support indexer-less SPV
      verification. BUMP is the merkle path; BEEF is the transaction
      envelope that carries it.
    sources:
      - docs/Semantos-Protocol-Spec-v0.01.docx
    notes: |
      Single canonical name; no alias variation in production use.

  - id: bundle-hash-commitment
    canonical: bundle hash commitment
    aliases:
      - bundle hash commitment
      - bundle hash
    short: |
      The 32-byte SHA-256 of an extension bundle's bytes, committed to
      the chain via the OP_RETURN payload of the D-W2 publish tx. The
      foundation for SPV-verifiable extension integrity.
    definition: |
      The *bundle hash commitment* is the 32-byte SHA-256 of an
      extension bundle's verbatim bytes, embedded in the OP_RETURN
      payload of an `extension-publish-tx` (D-W2 Phase 1). Subscribed
      brains receive the bundle bytes via the shard-proxy, recompute
      the SHA-256, and reject the bundle if the recompute disagrees
      with the on-chain commitment. The chain's proof-of-work is what
      secures bundle integrity — there's no central registry, no
      content-addressing service, no trust in a CDN.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_publish.zig
    notes: |
      For v0.1, the bundle is whatever single file the operator points
      at (`.wasm`, `.tar.gz`, etc.) — the hash is over the bytes
      verbatim, no packaging-format enforcement. A future PR may add a
      canonical archive shape.

  - id: capability-token
    canonical: capability token
    aliases:
      - capability token
      - capability UTXO
      - cap.* token
      - permission
    short: |
      A BRC-108 UTXO bound to a BRC-52 cert, granting time-bounded
      authority to perform a specific action class. Linear semantic
      resource — spending consumes it. Six well-known classes:
      cap.recovery, cap.permission, cap.data_access,
      cap.compute_delegation, cap.metered_access, cap.transfer.
    definition: |
      A *capability token* is a BRC-108-formatted UTXO bound to a
      BRC-52 cert subject that grants time-bounded authority to perform
      a specific action class. Spending the UTXO atomically revokes the
      capability — capabilities are LINEAR semantic resources. Six
      well-known classes: `cap.recovery`, `cap.permission`,
      `cap.data_access`, `cap.compute_delegation`, `cap.metered_access`,
      `cap.transfer`.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §6, §7, §14"
      - core/identity-ports/src/types.ts
    notes: |
      "Capability token" canonical. "Permission" is retired for this
      concept (it conflated authorisation with the act of granting);
      its only acceptable use now is as one of the seven jural
      categories ("permission" in the Hohfeldian sense, meaning
      "absence of duty to refrain"). "Capability UTXO" is the
      implementation-level synonym; "cap.* token" refers to specific
      well-known classes.

  - id: cell
    canonical: cell
    aliases:
      - cell
      - LoomObject
      - SemanticObject
      - SemObj
    short: |
      The primary type of the 2-PDA cell engine. A 1KB max binary unit
      with a 256-byte CellHeader + payload. Hash-chained state via
      prevStateHash; carries linearity class, pipeline phase, and
      cryptographic provenance.
    definition: |
      A *cell* is the primary unit handled by the 2-PDA cell engine: a
      1024-byte binary structure with a 256-byte typed header followed
      by up to 768 bytes of payload, plus zero or more 1024-byte
      continuation cells. The header carries the type hash, linearity
      class, pipeline phase, owner identifier, version, timestamp, and
      hash-chain pointers (`parentHash`, `prevStateHash`). Cells are
      the substrate's primitive of meaning, identity, and provenance.
    sources:
      - core/cell-engine/src/cell.zig
      - core/cell-ops/src/packer/cell-packer.ts
      - docs/Semantos-Protocol-Spec-v0.01.docx
      - docs/PIPELINE.md
    notes: |
      "Cell" canonical, matching the cell engine, the K1–K10
      invariants, the protocol spec, the whitepaper, and paper A1.
      `LoomObject` is a runtime/services-layer wrapper that *contains*
      a cell along with UI-presentation metadata; it is not a
      synonym. `SemanticObject` and `SemObj` appear in older docs and
      should be migrated to `cell`.

  - id: cell-engine
    canonical: cell engine
    aliases:
      - cell engine
      - PDA
      - 2-PDA
      - kernel
    short: |
      The two-stack push-down automaton with bounded execution that
      enforces K1 (linearity), K2 (authorisation), and the broader
      kernel invariants. ~4,900 LOC of Zig; full WASM is 185 KB,
      embedded profile 29 KB.
    definition: |
      The *cell engine* is the deterministic, bounded, two-stack
      push-down automaton (2-PDA) at the execution layer of the
      substrate. It enforces the kernel invariants K1 (linearity),
      K2 (authorisation), K3 (domain isolation), K4 (failure
      atomicity), and K5 (deterministic termination) at the bytecode
      gate. Implementation is approximately 4 900 lines of Zig
      compiled to WebAssembly; the full profile is 185 KB and the
      embedded profile is 29 KB.
    sources:
      - core/cell-engine/src/
      - "FORMAL-VERIFICATION-STRATEGY.md §1"
    notes: |
      "Cell engine" canonical for the component. "2-PDA" is the
      machine-model description (acceptable in formal prose). "PDA"
      alone is ambiguous (could mean the abstract automaton class) and
      should be avoided. "Kernel" is overloaded — it sometimes means
      the cell engine specifically, sometimes the broader substrate's
      execution layer including the Verifier Sidecar; prefer "cell
      engine" for precision.

  - id: cell-signing-mobile
    canonical: mobile cell signer
    aliases:
      - mobile cell signer
      - cell_signer.dart
      - Dart cell signer
    short: |
      Pure-Dart ECDSA-secp256k1-sha256 signer that produces 64-byte
      compact (r||s) signatures over canonical-JSON cell payload
      bytes.  Deviates from canonical RFC 6979 to match Zig stdlib's
      `Hmac(Sha256oSha256)` deterministic-k scheme byte-for-byte —
      the load-bearing parity that keeps the brain accepting Dart-
      signed cells.  Pinned by the cross-language fixture at
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/fixtures/cell-signing-fixture.json`.
    definition: |
      *mobile cell signer* is the pure-Dart ECDSA signer at
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/identity/cell_signer.dart`.
      Algorithm: SHA-256(payloadBytes) → ECDSA(secp256k1, devicePriv,
      digest) with a Zig-stdlib-compatible deterministic-k (RFC
      6979 framing PLUS a 32-byte zero "noise" slot in the HMAC
      preimage AND HMAC underlying hash = Sha256(Sha256(.)) instead
      of plain Sha256), then low-s normalisation per BIP-62.
      Output: 64 raw bytes (r big-endian || s big-endian); no
      recovery byte (the brain's recovery loop tries all four
      candidates).  Verify helper (for tests) recovers the pubkey
      via the same recovery-byte loop the brain uses.  Production
      mobile code only signs; the brain is the verifier.  Cross-
      language parity is asserted by a fixture generated by Zig and
      consumed byte-for-byte by Dart.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/identity/cell_signer.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/identity/cell_signer_test.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/fixtures/cell-signing-fixture.json
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/cell_signing_fixture_conformance.zig
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O5m"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-8 capture+upload (2026-05-02).  The
      Zig-stdlib-compatibility quirk (`Hmac(Sha256oSha256)` rather
      than plain `Hmac(Sha256)`, plus 32-byte zero noise slot)
      derives from how `bsvz.signCompact` rides on Zig's
      `EcdsaSecp256k1Sha256oSha256` scheme — without matching that
      scheme byte-for-byte, the Dart producer would emit signatures
      the brain rejects.  D-O5m.followup-2 will migrate to a
      Keychain/Keystore-backed signing key handle so the priv bytes
      never leave the secure enclave; today the raw-priv form is
      in place because the on-disk pairing record stores priv hex.

  - id: cert-id
    canonical: cert_id
    aliases:
      - cert_id
      - certId
      - cert id
    short: |
      32-byte hash of a BRC-52 certificate's canonical preimage. The
      stable identifier for a node in the Plexus identity DAG.
    definition: |
      A *`cert_id`* is the 32-byte SHA-256 hash of the canonical
      preimage of a BRC-52 certificate. It is the stable identifier
      for a node in the Plexus identity DAG and the input to BCA
      derivation.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §15"
      - core/plexus-contracts/src/identity.ts
    notes: |
      `cert_id` (snake_case) canonical — matches Plexus Tech, the wire
      format, and the Zig implementation. `certId` (camelCase) is the
      standard TypeScript spelling of the same field; not a separate
      concept. "Cert id" with a space is the prose form; equivalent.

  - id: challenge-set
    canonical: challenge set
    aliases:
      - challenge set
      - challenge_set
      - recovery challenges
    short: |
      The user-defined Q&A set that gates a recovery session. Minimum
      3 questions; answers normalized + salted + SHA-256 hashed before
      storage. Used only for session authentication, never for key
      derivation.
    definition: |
      The *challenge set* is the user-defined question-and-answer set
      that gates a Plexus recovery session. Minimum 3 questions;
      answers are normalised, salted, and SHA-256-hashed before
      server-side storage. The challenge set is used only for session
      authentication, never for key derivation — the root seed comes
      from a separate PBKDF2 over the answer concatenation, performed
      client-side.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §16, §11"
      - extensions/recovery/src/challenge.ts
    notes: |
      "Challenge set" canonical for prose; `challenge_set` in YAML and
      Zig; `challengeSet` is the natural TS spelling of the same
      concept.

  - id: compression-gradient
    canonical: compression gradient
    aliases:
      - compression gradient
    short: |
      The discipline of progressive entropy reduction through
      inspectable, verifiable intermediate forms — natural language to
      semantic intent to typed cell to bytes. The animating principle of
      the pipeline; subject of paper A1.
    definition: |
      A *compression gradient* is a discipline of progressive entropy
      reduction through inspectable, verifiable intermediate forms. In
      Semantos, the gradient runs from natural language through the
      semantic IR (SIR), the opcode IR (OIR) in administrative normal
      form, opcode bytes, and bounded execution. Each layer is equipped
      with a canonical form, a validation rule, an explicit loss
      boundary, and an emit pass to the next layer; across layers the
      gradient satisfies a semantic-preservation property under
      α-equivalence. Subject of paper A1.
    sources:
      - docs/INTENT-PIPELINE.md
      - docs/papers/Semantos-A1-Compression-Gradient-DRAFT.md
      - "doc plan §3 cluster A.A1"
    notes: |
      Single canonical phrase; coined in this work and used uniformly
      across the whitepaper, paper A1, and intent-pipeline doc.

  - id: cors-preflight
    canonical: CORS preflight
    aliases:
      - CORS preflight
      - OPTIONS preflight
      - access-control-allow-origin
    short: |
      Browser-issued OPTIONS request that asks a Semantos Brain-served origin
      whether a forthcoming cross-origin POST/PUT/DELETE is allowed. brain
      answers via per-site `cors_allowed_origins` config in `site.json`;
      a 204 with `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` lets the browser proceed,
      a 204 without it makes the browser block. Lands with D-W1 Phase 3
      + brain issue #273.
    definition: |
      A *CORS preflight* is the OPTIONS request a browser sends before
      any cross-origin call that doesn't fit the "simple request"
      criteria (custom headers, JSON content-type with credentials,
      anything other than GET/HEAD/POST). The brain HTTP transport
      handles preflight at a single short-circuit at the top of
      `site_server.handleRequest`: if the request method is OPTIONS,
      `cors.Cors.optionsHeaders` is rendered and emitted as a 204
      response, regardless of whether the URL maps to a configured
      route. Per-site policy lives in `SiteConfig`:
      `cors_allowed_origins` (exact match or `"*"` wildcard;
      empty = same-origin only), `cors_allowed_methods`,
      `cors_allowed_headers`, `cors_max_age_seconds`,
      `cors_allow_credentials`. The parser refuses to start a site
      whose config combines `"*"` with `cors_allow_credentials = true`
      (CORS spec violation; browsers would reject anyway, but failing
      at parse time gives the operator a clear hint). On non-OPTIONS
      responses, the same matched-origin echo (`Access-Control-Allow-
      Origin` + `Vary: Origin` + optional `Access-Control-Allow-
      Credentials`) is merged into `serveStatic`, `serveDirectory`,
      and the API stub responses (REPL, wallet, device-pair, chat).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/cors.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/site_server.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/site_config.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/cors_conformance.zig
      - "BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §5.3 + §8 Phase 3"
      - "https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/HTTP/CORS/Preflight_request"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-W1 Phase 3 (2026-05-01). Same dispatcher seam,
      one OPTIONS handler — every brain route inherits it (chat, REPL,
      wallet, device-pair, static, directory). No per-route override
      yet: site-level config is the operator-tier control. Range
      requests + an HTTP/1.1 stdlib rewrite are deferred follow-ups
      (deliverables.yml D-W1 Tier 3).

  - id: dispatch-envelope
    canonical: dispatch envelope
    aliases:
      - dispatch envelope
    short: |
      A semantic object with per-facet (per-hat) RELEVANT/AFFINE patches,
      enabling auditable cross-organisational workflow without
      point-to-point integration. Subject of paper C4.
    definition: |
      A *dispatch envelope* is a single semantic object referenced by
      multiple organisations, on which each participant attaches
      per-hat RELEVANT or AFFINE patches. Faceted visibility is
      enforced by the policy evaluator at field level; AFFINE patches
      are encrypted to the authoring hat's key. The envelope replaces
      point-to-point integration with a single auditable object whose
      cross-organisational evidence chain is regulator-grade by
      construction. Subject of paper C4.
    sources:
      - docs/PLATFORM-ARCHITECTURE.md
      - runtime/services/src/services/loom/channelService.ts
    notes: |
      Single canonical phrase; the alternative phrasings ("envelope",
      "dispatch object") are too generic and should be avoided.

  - id: domain-flag
    canonical: domain flag
    aliases:
      - domain_flag
      - domain flag
      - functional domain flag
    short: |
      4-byte uint32 namespace partition. 0x00000001–0x000000FF reserved
      for Plexus well-known domains; 0x00000100–0x0000FFFF for extended
      Plexus standards; 0x00010000–0xFFFFFFFF for client sovereignty.
    definition: |
      A *domain flag* is a 4-byte uint32 namespace identifier that
      partitions BRC-43 derived-key namespaces, capability scopes,
      lexicon authorities, and governance contexts. Three well-known
      ranges: `0x00000001`–`0x000000FF` reserved for Plexus well-known
      domains; `0x00000100`–`0x0000FFFF` for extended Plexus standards;
      `0x00010000`–`0xFFFFFFFF` for operator sovereignty. Enforced
      structurally at the bytecode layer by `OP_CHECKDOMAINFLAG` (K3).
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §3, §10, §30"
      - core/plexus-contracts/src/domain-flags.ts
    notes: |
      "Domain flag" canonical for prose; `domain_flag` in YAML / wire
      format; `domainFlag` in TS. "Functional domain flag" is the
      Plexus-Tech-formal name and acceptable on first introduction.

  - id: edge
    canonical: edge
    aliases:
      - edge
      - edge_record
      - peer-to-peer connection
    short: |
      A peer-to-peer cryptographic relationship between two cert nodes
      in the Plexus DAG. Established via ECDH (BRC-85 PIKE); the shared
      secret is hashed, never the raw secret. Per Plexus §12, the
      "primary recoverable unit."
    definition: |
      An *edge* is a peer-to-peer cryptographic relationship between
      two cert nodes in the Plexus identity DAG, established via ECDH
      under the BRC-85 PIKE protocol. The shared secret is hashed and
      never persisted in raw form. Per Plexus Tech §12, the edge is
      the "primary recoverable unit" — recovery-substrate semantics
      are designed around edge persistence.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §12, §25"
      - core/plexus-contracts/src/graph.ts
    notes: |
      "Edge" canonical (matches Plexus Tech, graph theory, and the
      codebase). `edge_record` is the YAML/Zig storage form;
      "peer-to-peer connection" is the descriptive English form.

  - id: extension-publish-tx
    canonical: extension-publish tx
    aliases:
      - extension-publish tx
      - extension publish transaction
      - publish tx
    short: |
      A BSV transaction whose OP_RETURN output commits an extension
      bundle's hash + name + version + signer pubkey + signature. The
      transaction id derives the shard group on the proxy fabric and
      anchors the bundle's integrity to proof-of-work.
    definition: |
      An *extension-publish tx* (D-W2 Phase 1) is a 1-input → 2-output
      BSV transaction. Output 0 is an OP_RETURN with payload
      `extension-publish-v1 || bundle_hash (32B) || name_len ||
      name || version_len || version || signer_pubkey (33B) ||
      signature (64B compact)`. Output 1 is change to the
      operator's P2PKH address. Broadcast via ARC. The tx id derives
      the shard group via `sha256("extension-publish:" || tx_id_hex)`;
      subscribed brains correlate received extension-bundle frames to
      the on-chain publish tx via this derivation.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_publish.zig
    notes: |
      The signature is ECDSA-SHA256 over `sha256d(bundle_hash ||
      version)`. We emit 64-byte compact `r || s` form (bsvz's
      internal 65-byte form has a 1-byte recovery prefix that we
      strip; verification reconstructs all four candidates and asks
      bsvz which one recovers the publisher's pubkey).

  - id: extension-subscriber
    canonical: extension subscriber
    aliases:
      - extension subscriber
      - subscriber sidecar
      - subscribe-bundles
    short: |
      The receive + verify + apply half of D-W2's platform-as-update-
      distributor loop. A TS sidecar joins each trusted-signer's
      multicast group; brain decodes + SPV-verifies + hash-checks +
      signature-checks + scope-checks + applies received frames.
    definition: |
      The *extension subscriber* (D-W2 Phase 2) inverts the publish
      flow. Where Phase 1 (`extension_publish.zig`) builds + signs +
      broadcasts the publish tx and pushes the bundle frame, Phase 2
      (`extension_subscriber.zig` + `transport/extension_subscribe.zig`)
      receives the bundle frame, SPV-verifies the publish tx, hash-
      checks the bundle bytes, signature-checks against the trusted
      signer, scope-checks the namespace, and applies (writes the
      bundle to `<data_dir>/extensions/<namespace>/<version>/bundle.bin`
      and registers handlers via the dispatcher). The cross-language
      seam is a TS sidecar (`extensions/oddjobz/tools/subscribe-
      bundles.ts`) joining the IPv6 multicast groups + forwarding
      received BRC-12 frames to brain's `POST /api/v1/bundle-frame`.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_subscriber.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/transport/extension_subscribe.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/tools/subscribe-bundles.ts
    notes: |
      Subscribe is opt-in per deployment: brain defaults to no
      `--bundle-frame-endpoint`; a tenant brain wanting upstream
      updates flips the flag + runs the sidecar. Apply is replay-
      idempotent (same bundle_hash on disk → no re-write, no double-
      register). v0.1's SPV client is a deny-all stub; production
      wires a real BSV-node-backed adapter — see operator runbook.

  - id: extension-frame-verify-pipeline
    canonical: extension frame verify pipeline
    aliases:
      - extension frame verify pipeline
      - frame verify pipeline
      - verifyFrame pipeline
    short: |
      The §5.2 step-by-step verification a subscribed brain runs on
      every received extension-bundle frame: decode → SPV → hash →
      signature → trusted-signer → scope.
    definition: |
      The *extension frame verify pipeline* (D-W2 Phase 2,
      BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md §5.2) is the ordered
      verification sequence implemented by
      `extension_subscriber.verifyFrame`:

        1. Decode the BRC-12 outer frame + inner extension-bundle-v1
           payload.
        2. SPV-verify the publish_txid via the configured SpvClient
           (depth ≥ N; v0.1 default 1, operator-tunable per §10).
        3. Verify the bundle hash matches the publish-tx OP_RETURN
           commitment.
        4. Verify the publish-tx OP_RETURN signature against the
           pubkey carried in the OP_RETURN.
        5. Match the publish-tx pubkey against `[trusted_signers]`;
           reject `unknown_signer` on miss.
        6. Scope-check the extension_name against the signer's
           `scope` glob; reject `scope_mismatch` on miss.

      Each step has a typed error (`spv_verify_failed`,
      `hash_mismatch`, `signature_invalid`, `unknown_signer`,
      `scope_mismatch`) the audit log surfaces.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_subscriber.zig
    notes: |
      The pipeline is transport-agnostic. The HTTP receive seam
      (`transport/extension_subscribe.zig`) is the v0.1 caller; future
      BLE / multicast / Plexus-push subscribers reuse the same
      pipeline via the same entry point.

  - id: extension-nullifier-tx
    canonical: extension-nullifier tx
    aliases:
      - extension-nullifier tx
      - nullifier tx
      - nullifier transaction
      - revocation tx
    short: |
      A BSV transaction whose OP_RETURN output commits the pubkey
      being revoked + a reason code + a timestamp + (optionally) a
      replacement pubkey signed by the rotation authority. The chain
      is the canonical revocation record; subscribers apply the
      revoke + (optionally) promote atomically on receive.
    definition: |
      An *extension-nullifier tx* (D-W2 Phase 3) is a 1-input → 2-output
      BSV transaction. Output 0 is an OP_RETURN with payload
      `extension-nullifier-v1 || revoked_pubkey (33B) || reason_code
      (u8) || timestamp (u64-be) || has_replacement (u8) ||
      [replacement_pubkey (33B) || rotation_authority_signature
      (64B)]`. The trailing replacement + signature fields are
      present iff `has_replacement = 1` (rotation case) and absent
      iff `has_replacement = 0` (pure-revocation case). Output 1
      is change to the operator's address. Broadcast via ARC.
      Subscribed brains receive the nullifier frame on the signer's
      shard group + run the receive pipeline's nullifier branch
      (decode → target-known check → rotation-authority signature
      verify → atomic apply).
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_nullifier.zig
    notes: |
      Reason codes: `compromised`, `superseded`, `voluntary`,
      `breach`. The publish-tx-id is the natural replay key — same
      nullifier tx = same revocation; subscribers' apply path is
      idempotent (same revoked pubkey twice = no-op). Pure-revocation
      payload is 65 bytes; rotation payload is 162 bytes.

  - id: rotation-authority
    canonical: rotation authority
    aliases:
      - rotation authority
      - rotation-authority key
      - recovery authority
    short: |
      A separate cold key the operator (or third-party signer) holds,
      registered as the signer's `recovery_enrolment_id`. It's the
      only key authorised to sign the rotation preimage that
      promotes a replacement pubkey in an atomic revoke + promote.
    definition: |
      The *rotation authority* (D-W2 §4.3) is the Plexus identity
      registered at the original signer-registration time as the
      authoritative key for rotating the signer's signing pubkey.
      During rotation, the rotation authority signs the digest
      `sha256d(revoked_pubkey || replacement_pubkey || timestamp_be)`
      and the signature is embedded in the nullifier transaction's
      OP_RETURN payload. Subscribed brains verify the signature
      against the on-chain rotation-authority pubkey before applying
      the promote.

      For the platform tier, the rotation authority is typically the
      operator's `tenant.recovery_enrolment_id` (a hardware-isolated
      cold key). For tenant-elected signers, it's whatever recovery
      key the third party registered.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_nullifier.zig
    notes: |
      The rotation-authority key has no operational duties — it
      never signs bundles. A compromised rotation-authority key is
      a worst-case scenario; defence-in-depth is the public chain
      itself (tenants can monitor for unexpected rotations and
      reject the apply via off-chain signalling if needed).

  - id: revoked-keys-index
    canonical: revoked-keys index
    aliases:
      - revoked-keys index
      - revoked keys file
      - extension-revoked-keys.json
    short: |
      A per-tenant JSON-lines audit log of every revoked pubkey,
      written at `<data_dir>/extension-revoked-keys.json`. Preserved
      permanently; used as the idempotence gate for nullifier replay.
    definition: |
      The *revoked-keys index* (D-W2 Phase 3) is the local audit
      record of every key that's been revoked on the brain. Format:
      one JSON object per line, fields
      `{"pubkey":"<hex>","reason":"<name>","timestamp":N,"signer":"<name>","replacement":"<hex|empty>"}`.
      Append-only. The brain's nullifier-apply path consults this
      index BEFORE rewriting the manifest — if the revoked pubkey is
      already present, the apply is a no-op (idempotent replay).
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_nullifier.zig

  - id: previous-pubkey-chain
    canonical: previous_pubkey_chain
    aliases:
      - previous_pubkey_chain
      - previous pubkey chain
      - rotation history field
    short: |
      A manifest field appended to a `[trusted_signers.<name>]`
      section after a rotation, carrying the historical chain of
      pubkeys this signer has cycled through (most-recent-old first).
    definition: |
      The *previous_pubkey_chain* field (D-W2 Phase 3) is the on-disk
      audit trail of a signer's pubkey rotations. After every
      `brain signer rotate`, the receive pipeline:

        1. Rewrites `[trusted_signers.<name>].pubkey` to the new
           replacement pubkey.
        2. Prepends the OLD pubkey to `previous_pubkey_chain`
           (creating the field if absent, extending it if present).

      The most recent rotation is at index 0; earlier rotations
      follow. Operators can audit a signer's full key history by
      reading the chain field.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_nullifier.zig
    notes: |
      The field is not validated by the manifest parser — it's
      written + read purely by the nullifier apply path's text
      mutation. Keeping it out of the structured parser avoids
      schema-version coupling between the rotation flow and the
      D-O8 manifest schema.

  - id: extension-quarantine-state-machine
    canonical: extension quarantine state machine
    aliases:
      - extension quarantine
      - quarantine state machine
      - quarantine lifecycle
    short: |
      The four-state lifecycle (`active`, `quarantined`,
      `pending_evaluation`, `removed`) every installed extension
      passes through. Quarantine is the default disposition for an
      install whose publishing signer was revoked on-chain; bundle
      bytes preserved on disk, dispatcher refuses to invoke handlers.
    definition: |
      The *extension quarantine state machine* (D-W2 Phase 4) governs
      the runtime disposition of every installed extension. States:

        - `active` — dispatcher routes calls to the extension's
          handlers normally.
        - `quarantined` — disabled. Dispatch returns
          `error.handler_quarantined` (wire transports map to 503
          Service Unavailable). Bundle bytes preserved on disk.
        - `pending_evaluation` — reserved for a future async-operator
          workflow.
        - `removed` — hard-deleted. Bundle bytes gone, dispatcher
          entry unmarked. Tombstone in the index for audit.

      Transitions are recorded as new lines in the persistent
      quarantine index (`<data_dir>/extension-quarantine.json`). The
      latest record per `extension_name` wins.

      Default behaviour on signer revocation: every install whose
      `meta.json.signer_pubkey` matches the revoked pubkey transitions
      to `quarantined`. The `[trusted_signers].quarantine_on_revoke =
      false` opt-out switches to hard-remove instead. Operator drives
      re-evaluation post-rotation via `brain extension quarantine
      evaluate <namespace>`; if a fresh signer entry covers the
      namespace, transition is `quarantined → active`.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_quarantine.zig
      - docs/operator-runbooks/extension-quarantine.md
    notes: |
      The quarantine flag lives on the dispatcher as a parallel
      `quarantined_handlers: HashSet`, NOT on the `ResourceHandler`
      vtable. Cleaner separation; multiple callers (CLI, REPL,
      audit) can consult the set without going through a handler
      indirection.

  - id: quarantine-record
    canonical: quarantine record
    aliases:
      - quarantine record
      - QuarantineRecord
      - quarantine index entry
    short: |
      One transition event in the per-tenant quarantine index. JSON-
      lines format. Append-only. Documents an extension's state
      transition with its previous state, reason, and signer pubkey.
    definition: |
      A *quarantine record* (D-W2 Phase 4) is one line in the
      quarantine index at `<data_dir>/extension-quarantine.json`.
      Fields: `extension_name`, `version`, `signer_pubkey` (66-char
      compressed-SEC1 hex), `state` (one of the four lifecycle
      states), `quarantined_at` (Unix-seconds), `reason` (one of
      `signer_revoked`, `signer_rotated_unsigned_bundle`,
      `manual_quarantine`, `evaluation_passed`, `operator_remove`,
      `revoke_hard_delete`), `original_install_path`,
      `previous_state`.

      The index is append-only; readers (e.g. `brain extension
      quarantine list`) deduplicate by `extension_name` and surface
      the latest record. Operators MAY archive old records; MUST NOT
      edit existing lines.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_quarantine.zig

  - id: quarantine-evaluation
    canonical: quarantine evaluation
    aliases:
      - quarantine evaluation
      - evaluateQuarantine
      - re-evaluate quarantine
    short: |
      The operator-driven re-evaluation step that flips a
      `quarantined` install back to `active` after the original
      publisher's signer rotated and a fresh `[trusted_signers]`
      entry now covers the install's namespace.
    definition: |
      *Quarantine evaluation* (D-W2 Phase 4) is the post-rotation
      recovery primitive. CLI: `brain extension quarantine evaluate
      <namespace>`. REPL: `extension quarantine evaluate <namespace>`.

      The evaluation logic:
        1. Load the latest quarantine record for `<namespace>`.
        2. If the record's state is `active` or `removed`, the call
           is a no-op (idempotent — see ambiguity (c) in the Phase 4
           brief).
        3. Otherwise, walk the manifest's `[trusted_signers]` entries
           looking for one whose `scope` covers `<namespace>`.
        4. If found, transition `quarantined → active`: append a new
           record with `state = active`, `reason = evaluation_passed`,
           `previous_state = quarantined`. Clear the dispatcher's
           quarantine flag.
        5. If not found, stay quarantined.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_quarantine.zig
      - docs/operator-runbooks/extension-quarantine.md
    notes: |
      v0.1 trusts the manifest entry as the signal that the bundle
      is now legitimate (the signer's `plexus_identity_tx` was SPV-
      verified at manifest-load time; an unverifiable entry never
      makes it past the manifest validator).  Production deployments
      with paranoid threat models can additionally re-run the full
      Phase 2 verify pipeline by hard-removing the install and
      letting the new bundle frame arrive on the shard group.

  - id: late-joiner-replay
    canonical: late-joiner replay
    aliases:
      - late-joiner replay
      - historical replay
      - Pravega replay
      - replayHistorical
    short: |
      The §5.3 mechanism by which a brain coming online for the first
      time (or after a long offline period) walks a signer's frame
      history + applies each frame in order, converging to the same
      state as a brain that received the frames live.
    definition: |
      *Late-joiner replay* (D-W2 §5.3) is the property that makes the
      extension distribution system robust without relying on any
      specific server's uptime. The chain stores the manifest of
      published transactions; the shard-proxy's archival layer
      (Pravega in the long-term design; per-tenant local cache in
      v0.1) caches the bundle frames; a brain reconstructs by walking
      every published frame in order, running the same verify+apply
      pipeline as the live path.

      Phase 2 implements the `replayHistorical` interface fully; the
      underlying "where do I get historical frames" is a
      `ReplaySource` plugin point. v0.1 ships an operator-supplied
      stub source (per-tenant local cache + BSV-node tx-history pull);
      Pravega integration replaces the stub when it lands.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_subscriber.zig
    notes: |
      Replay is idempotent: re-applying an already-applied
      (namespace, version) is a no-op (hash-equal on-disk bundle is
      the gate). One bad frame doesn't stall the replay — per-frame
      verify or apply errors are audit-logged + skipped, replay
      continues to convergence.

  - id: hat
    canonical: hat
    aliases:
      - hat
      - facet
      - HatPayload
      - HatRecord
    short: |
      A role/capacity dimension under which a user signs actions —
      "Bob-as-tenant" vs "Bob-as-friend". Implemented in the calendar
      extension's HatPayload/HatRecord structures; targeted for BRC-52
      backing in deliverable D-A5.
    definition: |
      A *hat* is a role-or-capacity dimension under which a user signs
      actions — distinguishing "Bob-as-tenant" from "Bob-as-friend"
      from "Bob-as-trustee". Each hat is associated with a distinct
      BRC-52 cert (or, transitionally, a distinct HatPayload backed
      by a single cert) and a distinct capability scope. Hat identity
      is the per-action signing principal; jural-tier enforcement at
      the SIR layer rejects cross-role authoritative claims
      structurally.
    sources:
      - extensions/calendar/src/domain/hat.ts
      - docs/prd/refactor-monoliths/00A-facet-to-hat-rename.md
    notes: |
      Renamed from `facet` to `hat` per refactor PRD 00A. "Facet" is
      retired; existing codebase paths still use `facet` in many
      places and will be migrated. `HatPayload` and `HatRecord` are
      the calendar extension's TS type names and are not aliases of
      the concept — they are storage-layer structures *that hold* a
      hat. D-A5 migrates the storage to BRC-52 cert backing.

  - id: hash-chain
    canonical: hash chain
    aliases:
      - hash chain
      - state hash chain
      - prevStateHash
    short: |
      The per-entity / per-region / per-channel / per-domain progression
      of state hashes that gives the substrate a verifiable cryptographic
      time. Several distinct chains co-exist at different scopes; the
      branching policy varies (see D-E-md, D-E-cal).
    definition: |
      A *hash chain* is the cryptographically-linked progression of
      state hashes that gives the substrate verifiable time at a given
      scope. Several distinct hash chains co-exist at different scopes:
      per-cell (`prevStateHash` chain), per-region (Merkle root over
      entity hashes per WorldTick), per-channel (MFP nSequence
      progression), per-domain (BKDS monotonic `current_index`).
      Branching policy is per-surface (tree-of-chains for documents;
      chain-forks for recurring rules).
    sources:
      - "core/cell-engine/src/cell.zig (per-cell)"
      - "docs/prd/WORLD-PROTOCOL.md §6, §10 (per-region)"
      - "Plexus Tech §10, §14, §23 (per-channel, per-domain)"
    notes: |
      "Hash chain" canonical for the concept. `prevStateHash` is the
      specific field name on a cell; "state hash chain" is the
      descriptive variant. The textbook should disambiguate the four
      named chain scopes (cell / region / channel / domain) on first
      introduction since they appear in distinct contexts.

  - id: helm
    canonical: Helm
    aliases:

    short: |

    definition: |
      *Helm* is the convergence surface of the substrate — the
      operator's workbench where every unification axis becomes
      user-visible: identity hat, signed actions, cell evidence chain,

    notes: |

  - id: find-calendar-resource
    canonical: find_calendar resource
    aliases:
      - find_calendar resource
      - jobs.find_calendar
      - typed find_calendar
    short: |
      The brain dispatcher's `jobs.find_calendar` command — derived
      query over `jobs-store` that groups scheduled jobs into per-day
      buckets across a [from, to] date range.  Days with no jobs
      scheduled return `jobs: []` so the helm renders a calendar
      grid without missing-key checks.
    definition: |
      *find_calendar resource* is the `jobs.find_calendar` command on
      the typed `jobs` dispatcher resource (`runtime/semantos-brain/src/
      resources/jobs_handler.zig`).  Filter args: `{from?: "YYYY-MM-
      DD", to?: "YYYY-MM-DD"}` (both inclusive); when `from` is
      omitted, defaults to the current week's Monday; when `to` is
      omitted, defaults to start-of-week + 7 days.  Range is capped at
      31 days defensively against runaway operator queries.  Returns
      a JSON array `[{date, jobs: [{id, customer_name, state,
      scheduled_at}, ...]}, ...]`, one entry per day in [from, to]
      ascending; each day's `jobs` array is sorted by `scheduled_at`
      ascending.  Cap: cap.oddjobz.read_jobs (no new cap — calendar
      is a read-only derived view over jobs).  Consumed by
      `apps/loom-svelte/src/views/Calendar.svelte` and
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/calendar_screen.dart`.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/jobs_handler.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/jobs_handler_conformance.zig
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/views/Calendar.svelte
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/calendar_screen.dart
      - "BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §3"
    notes: |
      Closes the calendar slice of D-O5.followup-3 (alongside
      `find-attention-resource`).  Derived query — no new store, no
      new cap; just an additional command on the existing `jobs`
      resource.  Job inclusion is by ISO-date prefix match against
      `scheduled_at`; jobs with empty `scheduled_at` are excluded
      (unscheduled leads belong on the Jobs view, not the Calendar).

  - id: job-transition-resource
    canonical: job_transition resource
    aliases:
      - job_transition resource
      - jobs.transition
      - typed jobs.transition
    short: |
      The brain dispatcher's `jobs.transition` command — drives an
      existing job through the canonical §O4 Job FSM (mirror of
      `extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/job-fsm.ts`).  Per-row
      cap requirement, principal-kind requirement, and the typed
      JSON error envelope let the helm render an operator-readable
      message on rejection.
    definition: |
      *job_transition resource* is the `jobs.transition` command on
      the typed `jobs` dispatcher resource (`runtime/semantos-brain/src/
      resources/jobs_handler.zig`).  Args: `{id, to_state,
      presented_cap?, principal_kind, scheduled_at?}`.  The handler
      looks up the (current_state, to_state) row in the canonical
      §O4 table (see `job-fsm-zig-port`), validates the row's
      `cap_required` against either the explicit `presented_cap` arg
      or the dispatcher-time `CapabilitySet`, validates the row's
      `principal_kinds`, then applies via `jobs_store_fs.updateState`.
      Three success-side response shapes:
        • bare Job        — transition applied
        • {status: "already_in_state", job}  — idempotent retry
        • {error, from, to, cap_required}    — typed FSM rejection
          (kinds: wrong_cap | not_reachable | wrong_principal |
          unknown_state | not_found)
      Dispatch-level cap-gating uses `cap.oddjobz.read_jobs` as the
      baseline (caller must be able to read jobs to know what to
      transition).  Per-row caps (cap.oddjobz.quote / dispatch /
      invoice / close) are checked inside the handler against
      `ctx.capabilities` and surfaced as typed JSON bodies on
      mismatch.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/jobs_handler.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/job_fsm.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/jobs_handler_conformance.zig
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/views/JobDetail.svelte
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/repl/jobs_repository.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/job_detail_screen.dart
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O4"
      - "BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §3"
    notes: |
      Closes D-O4 followup-1 (Job FSM cutover for the Semantos Brain dispatcher).
      The pre-followup-1 helms (post-#307/#308/#310) could READ +
      CREATE jobs through the dispatcher but had no transition path —
      every job stayed in `lead` forever.  This resource ships the
      canonical FSM cutover; both helms gain state-aware action
      buttons (`lead` → Quote, `quoted` → Schedule, …).  REPL verbs
      `quote job <id>`, `schedule job <id> [--at X]`, `start job <id>`,
      `complete job <id>`, `invoice job <id>`, `mark job paid <id>`,
      `close job <id>`, plus a generic `transition job <id> <to>`
      fallback for cancellation rows the FSM table may grow later.

  - id: job-fsm-zig-port
    canonical: Job FSM Zig port
    aliases:
      - Job FSM Zig port
      - job_fsm.zig
      - JOB_TRANSITIONS (Zig)
    short: |
      The brain-side Zig port of the canonical §O4 Job FSM table.
      Mirror of `extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/job-fsm.ts`'s
      `JOB_TRANSITIONS` array (seven LINEAR rows) plus a
      `validateTransition` entry point used by `jobs.transition`
      (see `job-transition-resource`).
    definition: |
      *Job FSM Zig port* lives at `runtime/semantos-brain/src/job_fsm.zig`.
      Exports `JOB_TRANSITIONS` (a `[7]Transition` array; row order
      matches the TS canon), `findTransition(from, to)`, and
      `validateTransition(current_state, to_state, presented_cap,
      principal_kind)`.  `Transition` carries `from`, `to`,
      `cap_required: ?[]const u8` (snake_case mirror of the TS
      `capRequired`), and `principal_kinds: []const PrincipalKind`.
      Validation produces a tagged-union `ValidationResult` that
      `jobs_handler.zig::handleTransition` maps onto either the
      success path (apply via `jobs_store_fs.updateState`) or the
      typed JSON error body the helm consumes.

      Cross-language parity is enforced by `cross-language-fsm-parity`
      (the conformance test that drives every TS-side transition
      through this Zig port).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/job_fsm.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/jobs_handler_conformance.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/job-fsm.ts
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O4"
    notes: |
      The Zig port deliberately omits the K1 `ConsumedCellSet` /
      `runFailureAtomic` shape the TS module carries — those are
      kernel-gate concerns that only matter once cell-DAG bytes flow
      through this code path.  The brain-side store
      (`jobs-store`) holds a SUBSET of the canonical
      `oddjobz.job.v1` cell payload; idempotency on retry is provided
      by the store's append-only log + the handler's "already in
      to_state" short-circuit, not by a `consumed` set.  When the
      cell-DAG substrate lands in a later phase the FSM module will
      hoist into a kernel-gate frame; today the contract is "FSM-
      table-correct + parity-with-TS".  Future PRs will ship Zig
      ports of the Quote / Visit / Invoice FSMs alongside this one.

  - id: cross-language-fsm-parity
    canonical: cross-language FSM parity
    aliases:
      - cross-language FSM parity
      - FSM conformance vector
      - job_fsm.json oracle
    short: |
      The load-bearing correctness proof for `job-fsm-zig-port`: the
      canonical conformance vector at
      `extensions/oddjobz/tests/vectors/state-machines/job_fsm.json`
      drives every TS-side transition through the Zig dispatcher's
      `jobs.transition` command and asserts the post-transition state
      matches the TS-side `expectedOutput.status` byte-for-byte.
    definition: |
      *cross-language FSM parity* is the `D-O5 followup-1
      jobs.transition: cross-language parity oracle` test in
      `runtime/semantos-brain/tests/jobs_handler_conformance.zig`.  It loads the
      canonical JSON oracle (the same file the TS-side
      `extensions/oddjobz/tests/state-machines/vector-parity.test.ts`
      reads), iterates `transitions[]`, and for each row dispatches
      `jobs.transition` with the row's `from`/`to`/`capRequired`/
      `principalKinds` values.  The Zig response's `state` field
      must equal the row's `expectedOutput.status` for every row.

      A regression on either side (TS canon drift, Zig table drift,
      handler mis-routing) breaks loud here.  This test is
      mandatory — it is the cross-language correctness proof the
      brain-side cutover stands on.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/jobs_handler_conformance.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/tests/vectors/state-machines/job_fsm.json
      - extensions/oddjobz/tests/state-machines/vector-parity.test.ts
    notes: |
      The same pattern will be applied to the Quote / Visit / Invoice
      FSM ports as they land; each gets its own conformance vector +
      its own parity test.  Cross-language parity is the canonical
      bar for any FSM-table cutover that adds a Zig substrate
      mirroring an existing TS canon.

  - id: attention-feed
    canonical: attention feed
    aliases:
      - attention feed
      - AttentionFeed
      - operator action buckets
    short: |
      The three operator-action buckets surfaced by `jobs.find_
      attention`: pending_quote (jobs in state=lead), pending_
      schedule (state=quoted), pending_invoice (state=completed).
      Jobs in non-action states (scheduled, in_progress, invoiced,
      paid, closed) are deliberately excluded — they do not require
      an immediate operator action.
    definition: |
      *attention feed* is the helm view-shape that aggregates jobs
      needing operator action right now.  The brain-side `jobs.find_
      attention` resource (see `find-attention-resource`) groups by
      Job FSM state into three buckets:
        • pending_quote   ← state=lead       (operator should respond
                                              with a quote)
        • pending_schedule← state=quoted     (customer accepted; operator
                                              schedules the visit)
        • pending_invoice ← state=completed  (work done; operator
                                              invoices)
      Each Job in a bucket carries the canonical helm field set
      (id, customer_name, state, scheduled_at).  The response also
      carries a `total` int — the sum across all three buckets — so
      the helm can render an unread-style badge without recomputing
      the sum locally.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/jobs_handler.zig
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/views/Attention.svelte
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/repl/jobs_repository.dart
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5.followup-3 (2026-05-02).  The bucket → state
      mapping mirrors the Job FSM transitions where the operator is
      next to act; future `urgency` / `category` scoring (per the
      cell-engine canon) can refine ordering within a bucket without
      breaking the bucket envelope.

  - id: ir
    canonical: IR
    aliases:
      - IR
      - intermediate representation
    short: |
      Generic term for an intermediate representation in the pipeline.
      In Semantos there are specifically two: SIR (semantic) and OIR
      (opcode). Bare "IR" is ambiguous and should be avoided in favour
      of SIR or OIR specifically.
    definition: |
      *IR* (intermediate representation) is the umbrella term for the
      pipeline's intermediate forms. In Semantos there are exactly
      two: SIR (semantic IR — jural-typed) and OIR (opcode IR — ANF).
      Bare "IR" should be reserved for the umbrella concept; whenever
      a specific representation is meant, use SIR or OIR.
    sources:
      - docs/PIPELINE.md
      - core/semantos-ir/
      - core/semantos-sir/
    notes: |
      "IR" canonical for the umbrella concept. The doc plan §1.4
      explicitly listed "IR vs SIR vs OIR" as drift; the resolution
      is that bare "IR" is acceptable only when speaking generically
      about intermediate representations.

  - id: customers-store
    canonical: customers store
    aliases:
      - customers store
      - CustomersStore
      - customers.jsonl
    short: |
      Append-only JSONL store at `<data_dir>/oddjobz/customers.jsonl`
      backing the Semantos Brain dispatcher's `find_customers` resource.  Mirrors
      a subset of the canonical `oddjobz.customer.v1` cell payload
      (id, display_name, phone, email, address, notes, created_at) for
      fast helm reads.
    definition: |
      *customers store* is the file-backed ArrayList of `Customer`
      records the `find_customers resource` reads from.  Implementation
      at `runtime/semantos-brain/src/customers_store_fs.zig`; same shape as
      `jobs-store` (one JSON object per line, in-memory index rebuilt
      by replaying the file at startup, atomic appends via O_APPEND).
      Idempotent on duplicate id — re-appending a created event
      leaves the in-memory record untouched but logs the event for
      audit.  Not a substitute for the cell-DAG: this is a rendered
      helm view-shape store, not the canonical authoritative record
      (which lives in `core/cell-engine`).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/customers_store_fs.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/cell-types/customer.ts
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5.followup-3 (2026-05-02).  Sits alongside
      jobs.jsonl in `<data_dir>/oddjobz/`.  Log rotation is a known
      gap shared with bearer_tokens.log + audit.log + jobs.jsonl —
      TODO follow-up if customers.jsonl grows past ~16MB.  display_name
      filter via `findByName` is a case-insensitive ASCII substring
      match suitable for operator typeahead; multi-byte case-folding
      is byte-wise (good-enough for the helm).

  - id: visits-store
    canonical: visits store
    aliases:
      - visits store
      - VisitsStore
      - visits.jsonl
    short: |
      Append-only JSONL store at `<data_dir>/oddjobz/visits.jsonl`
      backing the Semantos Brain dispatcher's `find-visits-resource`.  Mirrors a
      subset of the canonical `oddjobz.visit.v1` cell payload (id,
      job_id, visit_type, status, notes, actual_start, outcome,
      created_at, updated_at) for fast helm reads.  FK to `jobs-store`
      via `job_id`; FK validation lives at the handler layer (loose
      coupling — the store itself doesn't know about jobs).
    definition: |
      *visits store* is the file-backed ArrayList of `Visit` records
      the `find_visits resource` reads from.  Implementation at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/visits_store_fs.zig`; same JSONL log shape as
      `customers-store` and `jobs-store`.  Idempotent on duplicate id
      — re-appending a created event leaves the in-memory record
      untouched but logs the event for audit.  `updateState` mutates
      in-place + emits an `updated` log line for FSM transitions; the
      store's `findById` / `findByJobId` accessors borrow into the
      heap-stable per-record OwnedStrings backing rather than the
      single-arena pattern jobs/customers use, sidestepping the
      cross-record dangling-slice hazard tracked separately for the
      older stores.  Not a substitute for the cell-DAG: this is a
      rendered helm view-shape store, not the canonical authoritative
      record (which lives in `core/cell-engine`).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/visits_store_fs.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/cell-types/visit.ts
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/visit-fsm.ts
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O4.followup-2 (2026-05-02).  Status validator
      enumerates the four canonical Visit FSM states verbatim
      (`extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/visit-fsm.ts`
      VISIT_FSM_STATES).  Visit type validator enumerates the five
      canonical visit types (VISIT_TYPES — inspection, quote_visit,
      scheduled_work, return_visit, emergency).  Sits alongside
      jobs.jsonl + customers.jsonl in `<data_dir>/oddjobz/`.

  - id: visit-fsm-zig-port
    canonical: Visit FSM Zig port
    aliases:
      - Visit FSM Zig port
      - visit_fsm.zig
      - VISIT_TRANSITIONS (Zig)
    short: |
      The brain-side Zig port of the canonical §O4 Visit FSM table.
      Mirror of `extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/visit-fsm.ts`'s
      `VISIT_TRANSITIONS` array (four LINEAR rows: scheduled →
      in_progress, scheduled → cancelled, in_progress → completed,
      in_progress → cancelled) plus a `validateTransition` entry point
      used by `visits.transition` (see `find-visits-resource`).
    definition: |
      *Visit FSM Zig port* lives at `runtime/semantos-brain/src/visit_fsm.zig`.
      Exports `VISIT_TRANSITIONS` (a `[4]Transition` array; row order
      matches the TS canon), `findTransition(from, to)`, and
      `validateTransition(current_state, to_state, presented_cap,
      principal_kind)`.  Same shape as `job-fsm-zig-port` post-#311 —
      `Transition`, `PrincipalKind`, `ValidationError`,
      `ValidationResult` are duplicated locally so the visit FSM
      module stays a leaf with no imports beyond std.

      Cross-language parity is enforced by `cross-language-fsm-parity`
      (the conformance test extended to drive every TS-side Visit
      transition through this Zig port via the canonical
      visit_fsm.json oracle).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/visit_fsm.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/visits_handler_conformance.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/visit-fsm.ts
      - extensions/oddjobz/tests/vectors/state-machines/visit_fsm.json
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O4"
    notes: |
      Every Visit FSM row is ungated at the cap-mint layer (the
      gating story for Visit transitions is delegated to the parent
      Job FSM per the visit-fsm.ts canon).  The brain dispatcher gates
      `visits.transition` on `cap.oddjobz.read_visits` at the
      dispatcher layer; the handler also resolves per-FSM-row caps
      inside `validateTransition` so future FSM rows that gain a cap
      slot in cleanly.  Closes the second of the four FSM cutovers
      (Job + Visit landed; Quote + Invoice are tracked as
      D-O4.followup-3 / followup-4).

  - id: leads-store
    canonical: leads store
    aliases:
      - leads store
      - LeadsStore
      - leads.jsonl
    short: |
      Append-only JSONL store at `<data_dir>/oddjobz/leads.jsonl`
      backing the Semantos Brain dispatcher's `find-leads-resource`.  Mirrors a
      SUBSET of the canonical `oddjobz.lead.v1` cell payload narrowed
      to the operator-facing helm view-shape (id, customer_name,
      phone, email, summary, source, source_correlation_id, status,
      rejection_reason, hat_id, created_at, updated_at).  No FK seam
      — leads are job precursors with no parent cell.
    definition: |
      *leads store* is the file-backed ArrayList of `Lead` records the
      `find_leads resource` reads from.  Implementation at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/leads_store_fs.zig`; same JSONL log shape as
      `visits-store` and `customers-store` and `jobs-store`.
      Idempotent on duplicate id — re-appending a created event leaves
      the in-memory record untouched but logs the event for audit.
      `updateState` mutates in-place + emits an `updated` log line for
      FSM transitions (`leads-fsm`).  The store uses the per-string-
      heap-allocation pattern (mirror of visits_store_fs post-#312/
      #319): each Lead's String fields are individually heap-allocated
      via `allocator.dupe`; an `OwnedStrings` ArrayList tracks them so
      `deinit` can free in lock-step.  The legacy `oddjobz.lead.v1`
      cell payload (the AFFINE-cell ratification anchor minted at
      ratification time) lives in the cell-DAG, NOT in this store —
      this store is the brain-side queue the operator triages from
      (pending leads accumulate; ratification mints a Lead cell + drives
      the Job FSM `∅ → lead` transition out of band).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/leads_store_fs.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/leads_handler_conformance.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/cell-types/lead.ts
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-7 Phase A (2026-05-02).  Status
      validator enumerates the five canonical Lead FSM states
      (pending / ratified / rejected / deferred / archived).  Source
      validator enumerates the four canonical input channels
      (chat / voice / text / manual).  Sits alongside jobs.jsonl +
      visits.jsonl + customers.jsonl in `<data_dir>/oddjobz/`.

  - id: leads-fsm
    canonical: Lead FSM
    aliases:
      - Lead FSM
      - leads.transition table
    short: |
      The 7-row FSM table the Semantos Brain `leads.transition` command validates
      against.  Inlined in `runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/leads_handler.zig`
      (no separate `lead_fsm.zig` module — the table is small enough to
      live with the handler, unlike the Job/Visit/Quote/Invoice FSMs
      which are large enough to warrant their own per-FSM Zig port).
    definition: |
      *Lead FSM* table:
        pending  → ratified  : cap.oddjobz.write_customer (operator)
        pending  → rejected  : cap.oddjobz.write_customer (operator)
        pending  → deferred  : cap.oddjobz.read_jobs       (operator)
        ratified → archived  : cap.oddjobz.write_customer (operator)
        rejected → archived  : cap.oddjobz.write_customer (operator)
        deferred → pending   : cap.oddjobz.read_jobs       (operator)
        deferred → archived  : cap.oddjobz.write_customer (operator)

      All transitions today are operator-driven; "principal_kind=service"
      is reserved for future automation (e.g. an auto-archive sweep on
      stale rejected leads).  The handler emits `lead.transitioned`
      after every successful transition with `requires_operator_attention=
      false` (the operator IS the actor — no point pushing back to
      themselves).  Idempotent: same-state transition returns the
      typed `{status: "already_in_state", lead}` body.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/leads_handler.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/leads_handler_conformance.zig
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-7 Phase A (2026-05-02).  Reuses the
      existing `cap.oddjobz.read_jobs` (0x00010107) +
      `cap.oddjobz.write_customer` (0x00010101) caps; no new caps
      minted in this PR.

  - id: find-leads-resource
    canonical: find_leads resource
    aliases:
      - find_leads resource
      - leads.find
      - typed find_leads
      - leads resource
    short: |
      The brain dispatcher's typed `leads` resource (commands `find`,
      `create`, `find_by_id`, `transition`).  Returns canonical JSON
```
