      end and emits `lead.created` (operator-attention=true) +
      `lead.transitioned` (operator-attention=false) through the
      `helm_event_broker`.
    definition: |
      *find_leads resource* is the typed dispatcher resource at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/leads_handler.zig` that fronts the
      `leads-store`.  It exposes four commands:
      `leads.find` (optional `status` and `hat_id` filters;
      `cap.oddjobz.read_jobs`),
      `leads.create` (`cap.oddjobz.write_customer`; idempotent on
      duplicate id with identical contents, rejects same-id-different-
      contents via `lead_id_in_use_with_different_contents`; emits
      `lead.created` with `requires_operator_attention=true` —
      closes the wiring deferred from D-O5m.followup-9 Phase A's
      brain-side push pipeline),
      `leads.find_by_id` (`cap.oddjobz.read_jobs`), and
      `leads.transition` (driven by the inlined `leads-fsm` table;
      dispatcher-gated on `cap.oddjobz.read_jobs`, per-FSM-row caps
      checked inside the handler against ctx.capabilities).  Output
      is canonical JSON consumed verbatim by the (Phase B) mobile
      ratification card + future helm-over-HTTP consumers.

      Closes D-O5m.followup-7 Phase A (brain-side primitives).  No new
      caps minted — reuses `cap.oddjobz.read_jobs` +
      `cap.oddjobz.write_customer`.  Phase B (mobile voice/text input
      bar + ratification card + queue client) ships in a separate PR
      and consumes `find leads` / `ratify lead` / `reject lead` /
      `defer lead` via the existing typed REPL JSON path.

  - id: ratify-lead-flow-brain
    canonical: ratify-lead flow (brain-side)
    aliases:
      - ratify lead flow
      - operator ratification flow

    short: |
      Operator-facing ratification path that consumes a `pending` lead
      from the `leads-store` and drives it to `ratified` via the
      `leads.transition` REPL verb (or the dispatcher's HTTP shim).
      Anchors the chat-lead extraction's TS-side `RATIFIES_INTENT`
      seam (runtime/intent/src/triage.ts + ratification.ts) on the
      brain-side queue.
    definition: |
      *ratify-lead flow (brain-side)* is the Semantos Brain-side half of the
      §O6b ratification pipeline.  A chat-bot extraction (TS-side
      `runtime/intent/src/handle-message.ts` → triage.ts →
      conversation-patch.ts) calls `leads.create` to enqueue a fresh
      `pending` lead in the `leads-store`; the brain emits
      `lead.created` with `requires_operator_attention=true` so the
      §O5m-g push dispatcher (D-O5m.followup-9 Phase B) wakes the
      operator's mobile device; the operator opens the (Phase B)
      ratification card, taps `ratify`, and the mobile shell drives
      `leads.transition pending → ratified` through the typed REPL
      JSON path.  Out-of-band, the ratification mints a
      `oddjobz.lead.v1` cell + drives the Job FSM `∅ → lead`
      transition (the cell-DAG-side ratification anchor).
    sources:

      - runtime/intent/src/ratification.ts
      - runtime/intent/src/triage.ts
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/cell-types/lead.ts
    notes: |
      Phase A scope (this entry): brain-side primitives — store + REPL
      verbs + `lead.created` emit.  Phase B (mobile ratification card
      consuming the typed REPL JSON path) is a separate PR.  The
      cell-DAG-side mint of the AFFINE `oddjobz.lead.v1` anchor is
      out-of-band of the brain-side queue and is owned by the §O6b
      ratification pipeline proper, not by this resource.

  - id: ratification-queue-client-mobile
    canonical: ratification queue client (mobile)
    aliases:
      - RatificationQueueClient

    short: |
      Dart-side typed client over the bearer-gated REPL HTTP endpoint
      (`POST /api/v1/repl`) that the mobile-helm Leads tab +
      RatificationCardScreen call to drive the §O6b ratification queue.
    definition: |
      *ratification queue client (mobile)* mirrors `JobsRepository`
      (post-#311) for the Lead cell type.  Methods:
      `findPending({hatId})` issues `find leads --status pending [--hat
      <id>]`; `findById(id)` issues `find lead <id>`; `ratify(id)`,
      `reject(id, reason)`, `defer(id)` issue the matching operator
      verbs; the response is parsed against the typed Lead JSON shape
      (verbatim from `leads_handler.zig::writeLeadJson`).  When wired
      to a HelmEventStream the client subscribes to `lead.created` +
      `lead.transitioned` and surfaces them on `cacheEvents` so
      LeadsListScreen + an open RatificationCardScreen invalidate
      themselves on operator A's transition.

      *ratification card (mobile)* is the operator-facing surface for
      the ratification queue.  PushNotificationRouter (#328) pushes
      `/ratify` with `arguments: {'lead_id': '<id>'}` when the operator
      taps a `lead.created` push; the screen fetches the lead via
      `RatificationQueueClient.findById`, renders a card with customer
      details + summary + source attribution, and exposes a sticky
      bottom action bar.  Reject opens a bottom-sheet reason picker
      (`not_viable | duplicate | spam | out_of_scope | other`).  All
      three actions route through the queue client and pop the route
      with a typed RatificationCardOutcome on success.  The state
      machine + button-tap dispatch live in the pure-Dart
      `RatificationCardController` so the unit tests run without
      flutter_test.

    canonical: text intent service (mobile)

      shape for the typed-text branch: given operator-typed text, run

      `source='nl'`, then drive the `DartIntentPipeline` (L1→L2→L3→L4)
      locally.  Surfaces a typed [TextIntentOutcome] — never throws
      on an expected refusal so the input bar can pattern-match on the
      failure shape (extractor refusal, pipeline rejection at SIR or
      kernel stage, network error, extractor/pipeline unavailable).

      differences are the input source (typed text vs transcribed
      audio) and the `Intent.source` stamp.

    definition: |

      `quote-fsm-zig-port`; dispatcher-gated on

  - id: invoices-store
    canonical: invoices store
    aliases:
      - invoices store
      - InvoicesStore
      - invoices.jsonl
    short: |
      Append-only JSONL store at `<data_dir>/oddjobz/invoices.jsonl`
      backing the Semantos Brain dispatcher's `find-invoices-resource`.  Mirrors
      a subset of the canonical `oddjobz.invoice.v1` cell payload (id,
      job_id, status, amount, amount_paid, external_invoice_id, notes,
      sent_at, viewed_at, paid_at, created_at, updated_at) for fast
      helm reads.  FK to `jobs-store` via `job_id`; FK validation
      lives at the handler layer (loose coupling — the store itself
      doesn't know about jobs).
    definition: |
      *invoices store* is the file-backed ArrayList of `Invoice`
      records the `find_invoices resource` reads from.  Implementation
      at `runtime/semantos-brain/src/invoices_store_fs.zig`; same JSONL log shape
      as `quotes-store` and `visits-store` and `customers-store` and
      `jobs-store`.  Idempotent on duplicate id — re-appending a
      created event leaves the in-memory record untouched but logs
      the event for audit.  `updateState` mutates in-place + emits an
      `updated` log line for FSM transitions; the store's `findById`
      / `findByJobId` accessors borrow into the heap-stable per-record
      OwnedStrings backing rather than the single-arena pattern
      jobs/customers use, sidestepping the cross-record dangling-slice
      hazard tracked separately for the older stores.  Amount fields
      are i64 cents so the canonical TS shape's `amount` /
      `amountPaid` round-trip without precision loss.  Not a
      substitute for the cell-DAG: this is a rendered helm view-shape
      store, not the canonical authoritative record (which lives in
      `core/cell-engine`).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/invoices_store_fs.zig

      Closes the Semantos Brain-side cutover of all 4 oddjobz FSMs.

    aliases:

    short: |

    definition: |
      *Invoice FSM Zig port* lives at `runtime/semantos-brain/src/invoice_fsm.zig`.
      Exports `INVOICE_TRANSITIONS` (a `[15]Transition` array; row
      order matches the TS canon), `findTransition(from, to)`, and
      `validateTransition(current_state, to_state, presented_cap,
      principal_kind)`.  Same shape as `quote-fsm-zig-port` post-#313
      — `Transition`, `PrincipalKind`, `ValidationError`,
      `ValidationResult` are duplicated locally so the invoice FSM
      module stays a leaf with no imports beyond std.

      Cross-language parity is enforced by `cross-language-fsm-parity`
      (the conformance test extended to drive every TS-side Invoice
      transition through this Zig port via the canonical
      invoice_fsm.json oracle).

    notes: |
      Every Invoice FSM row is ungated at the cap-mint layer (the
      gating story for Invoice transitions is delegated to the parent
      Job FSM per the invoice-fsm.ts canon).  The brain dispatcher
      gates `invoices.transition` on `cap.oddjobz.read_invoices` at
      the dispatcher layer; the handler also resolves per-FSM-row
      caps inside `validateTransition` so future FSM rows that gain
      a cap slot in cleanly.  Closes the FOURTH and FINAL FSM
      cutover (Job + Visit + Quote + Invoice are all brain-side now).

  - id: jural-category
    canonical: jural category
    aliases:
      - jural category
      - Hohfeldian category
      - normative position
    short: |
      One of the seven categories — declaration, obligation, permission,
      prohibition, power, condition, transfer — used in the SIR layer
      to type semantic objects. Adapted from Hohfeld's analysis of
      jural relations.
    definition: |
      A *jural category* is one of the seven elementary categories used
      in the SIR layer to type semantic objects: **declaration**,
      **obligation**, **permission**, **prohibition**, **power**,
      **condition**, and **transfer**. Adapted from Hohfeld's 1913
      analysis of fundamental legal conceptions; the seven-category
      set is the minimum vocabulary sufficient to distinguish every
      act the substrate performs.
    sources:
      - "docs/SEMANTIC-IR-ARCHITECTURE.md"
      - proofs/lean/Semantos/Lexicons/Jural.lean
    notes: |
      "Jural category" canonical, matching SEMANTIC-IR-ARCHITECTURE.md,
      the whitepaper, and paper A1. The previous `short:` referenced
      the raw Hohfeldian eight-category set (right/duty,
      privilege/no-right, power/liability, immunity/disability) — that
      is the *theoretical source* and the Lean Jural lexicon's logical
      basis, but the *implemented* category set in the SIR is the
      seven-category adapted-for-computational-governance set above.

  - id: kernel-invariant
    canonical: kernel invariant
    aliases:
      - kernel invariant
      - K1
      - K2
      - K3
      - K4
      - K5
      - K6
      - K7
      - K8
      - K9
      - K10
    short: |
      A property of the cell-engine execution semantics provable
      mechanically (Lean for K1, K2, K3, K4, K5, K7, K8, K9, K10;
      TLA+ model-checked for K6 and the distributed properties).
    definition: |
      A *kernel invariant* is a property of the cell-engine execution
      semantics provable mechanically over the abstract 2-PDA model.
      Five execution invariants (K1 linearity, K2 authorisation, K3
      domain isolation, K4 failure atomicity, K5 deterministic
      termination), one object-integrity invariant (K7 cell
      immutability), and three additional invariants (K8 demotion
      safety, K9 temporal morphism, K10 Turing-completeness bound) are
      proved in Lean 4. K6 (hash-chain integrity) and the distributed
      protocol properties are model-checked in TLA+.
    sources:
      - proofs/lean/Semantos/Theorems/
      - proofs/tla/
      - "docs/FORMAL-VERIFICATION-STRATEGY.md §1"
    notes: |
      "Kernel invariant" canonical for the umbrella term. K1 through
      K10 are the named instances and should be cited by their
      identifier in any artifact that references a specific invariant.

  - id: lexicon
    canonical: lexicon
    aliases:
      - lexicon
      - domain vocabulary
    short: |
      A substrate-polymorphic Lean type registering an instance of the
      `Lexicon` typeclass with header injectivity. Eight ship today:
      jural, CDM, circuit, project-mgmt, property-mgmt, risk-assessment,
      bills-of-lading, control-systems.
    definition: |
      A *lexicon* is a substrate-polymorphic Lean registration of a
      domain vocabulary as an instance of the `Lexicon` typeclass with
      header injectivity. Each lexicon supplies an `inductive` for the
      categories, a `header` function, and the injectivity proof; the
      substrate's M1–M4 and D1–D3 lemmas then apply to every
      registered lexicon by specialisation. Eight ship today: jural,
      CDM, circuit, project-management, property-management,
      risk-assessment, bills-of-lading, control-systems.
    sources:
      - proofs/lean/Semantos/Lexicons/
      - "doc plan §1.1"
    notes: |
      "Lexicon" canonical (the formal name and what the typeclass is
      called). "Domain vocabulary" is descriptive but less precise.

  - id: linearity
    canonical: linearity
    aliases:
      - linearity
      - substructural type
      - linearity class
    short: |
      The cell's substructural type. Four numeric codes — LINEAR (0,
      consume exactly once), AFFINE (1, at most once), RELEVANT (2, at
      least once), UNRESTRICTED (3) — enforced by K1 in the cell engine.
    definition: |
      *Linearity* is the cell's substructural type, taking one of four
      values: LINEAR (0, consumed exactly once), AFFINE (1, consumed
      at most once), RELEVANT (2, used at least once), UNRESTRICTED
      (3). Enforced structurally by K1 (linearity) at the bytecode
      gate of the cell engine; the linearity class is read from the
      cell header at offset 16 and is read-only after packing (K7).
    sources:
      - core/cell-engine/src/linearity.zig
      - core/cube-object/src/linearity.ts
      - proofs/lean/Semantos/Theorems/LinearityK1.lean
    notes: |
      "Linearity" canonical for the property. "Linearity class" is
      acceptable when speaking specifically of the four-value enum;
      the two are nearly interchangeable. "Substructural type" is the
      broader PL-theory category and acceptable on first introduction
      in academic prose.

  - id: mobile-camera-adapter

      - mobile camera adapter

      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/sensors/camera_capture.dart` over
      the platform camera (image_picker on iOS + Android).
      `captureFromCamera({picker, clock})` invokes the injected
      picker, reads the bytes + mime type, stamps a UTC ISO-8601
      timestamp via the injected clock, and returns a CapturedPhoto
      (or null on cancel/error).  The picker is typed as
      `Future<PickedPhoto?> Function()` so the production wiring
      (in helm_app.dart) adapts image_picker's XFile to PickedPhoto
      out-of-band, keeping the dart-test-runnable surface
      pointycastle/sqflite/test-only.  Production permissions are
      iOS NSCameraUsageDescription + Android android.permission.CAMERA
      (already present from D-O5m's QR scanning surface; reused for
      photo capture).

      the platform geolocator (the `geolocator` package on iOS +
      Android).  `captureCurrentLocation({geolocator, clock})`
      reads the OS-level service-enabled flag, requests location
      permission as needed, fetches a one-shot Position, and
      returns a CapturedGpsPin (or null on permission denied /
      service off / transient error).  The GeolocatorAdapter
      interface (`isLocationServiceEnabled`, `checkPermission`,
      `requestPermission`, `getCurrentPosition`) is the production
      seam — production wiring adapts the geolocator package
      directly; tests inject a stub returning a fixture position.
      The CapturedGpsPin is canonicalised via [gpsBlobBytes] into
      the lex-ordered JSON the brain stores under
      `<sha256>.bin` (`{accuracy_m?, captured_at, lat, lng}`).
      Production permissions are iOS
      NSLocationWhenInUseUsageDescription + Android
      android.permission.ACCESS_FINE_LOCATION /
      ACCESS_COARSE_LOCATION (added with this PR).

      the sibling PR completing the sensor adapter trio).  The brain-

  - id: voice-memo-adapter
    canonical: voice memo adapter
    aliases:
      - voice memo adapter
      - voice_memo_capture.dart
      - VoiceRecorderController
    short: |
      The mobile-side sensor adapter that drives the platform
      microphone via the `record` package and emits a
      `CapturedVoiceMemo` (recorded bytes + mime type + ISO-8601
      timestamp + duration) for the helm to feed into
      `attachment_builder.buildSignedAttachment` with `kind:
      voice_memo`.  Owns a stateful VoiceRecorderController with
      start/stop/cancel + a state stream for the recording UI.
    definition: |
      *voice memo adapter* is the wrapper at
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/sensors/voice_memo_capture.dart`
      over the platform recorder (the `record` package on iOS +
      Android).  Unlike the camera + GPS adapters (which are
      stateless one-shot calls), voice recording requires a
      controller because the operator drives start/stop/cancel
      from a recording sheet UI; the
      `VoiceRecorderController(recorder, maxDuration, clock)`
      carries the state machine (`idle → recording → stopped /
      cancelled / error`), the timeout watchdog (default 60s
      safety cap), and the broadcast stateStream the UI binds to.
      The VoiceRecorderAdapter interface (start / stop / cancel)
      is the production seam — production wiring adapts the record
      package; tests inject a stub.  On stop the controller
      returns a CapturedVoiceMemo whose bytes are fed verbatim
      into attachment_builder with the recorded mime type
      (`audio/m4a` or `audio/aac` per platform).  The complementary
      VoicePlaybackAdapter + VoiceMemoPlayerScreen handle playback
      of previously-uploaded memos via the bearer-gated
      `/api/v1/attachments/<id>/blob` endpoint.  Production
      permissions are iOS NSMicrophoneUsageDescription + Android
      android.permission.RECORD_AUDIO (added with this PR).
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/sensors/voice_memo_capture.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/sensors/voice_memo_capture_test.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/voice_memo_player_screen.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/attachments/attachment_capture_service.dart
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O5m-f"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-8 GPS + voice memo adapters
      (2026-05-02).  Completes the §O5m-f sensor adapter trio
      alongside `mobile-camera-adapter` and `gps-sensor-adapter`.
      Same architectural posture: the brain-side substrate accepts
      `voice_memo` as one of the four canonical attachment kinds,
      so the producer plugs into the existing pipeline without any
      brain-side changes.

  - id: mesh
    canonical: mesh
    aliases:
      - mesh
      - IPv6 multicast
      - peer mesh
    short: |
      The peer-discovery + signed-bundle transport layer. Peers
      identified by BCA; frames carried over IPv6 multicast with a
      codec port (post-Prompt-38 split).
    definition: |
      The *mesh* is the substrate's peer-discovery and signed-bundle
      transport layer. Peers are identified by BCA; frames travel as
      `SignedBundle<T>` over IPv6 multicast (the default transport)
      via a codec port that is replaceable per Phase 35A. The same
      `SessionRuntime` state machine runs unchanged against the WSS
      adapter, the multicast adapter, and the in-design compact
      adapter for non-IP transports.
    sources:
      - runtime/session-protocol/

    notes: |
      "Mesh" canonical (concise, generic). "IPv6 multicast" is the
      default transport implementation but not the only one; treating
      it as the canonical name would over-bind the concept.

  - id: mfp
    canonical: MFP
    aliases:
      - MFP
      - Metered Flow Protocol
      - payment channel
      - cashlane
    short: |
      The 8-state 2-of-2 multisig channel FSM that meters paid resource
      flows. nSequence settlement; HMAC-authenticated ticks; SPV-finalised
      on close. Capability UTXOs gate participation.
    definition: |
      *MFP* (Metered Flow Protocol) is the 8-state finite-state
      machine over a 2-of-2 multisig UTXO that meters paid resource
      flows in the substrate. Each tick produces an HMAC-authenticated
      proof; settlement uses Bitcoin's original `nSequence` mechanism
      (miners accept the highest `nSequence`); on close, the channel
      is finalised on-chain via SPV. Capability UTXOs gate
      participation.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §14"
      - core/plexus-contracts/src/domain-flags.ts
    notes: |
      "MFP" canonical for the short form; "Metered Flow Protocol" only
      on first introduction. "Cashlane" is older terminology and
      should be retired. "Payment channel" is a generic term for the
      class of mechanism MFP is one instance of.

  - id: octave
    canonical: octave
    aliases:
      - octave
      - VFS slot
    short: |
      Content-addressed storage slot in the VFS. Cells live at octave
      paths; the VFS resolves names to addresses via lexicon-typed
      parent/child constraints.
    definition: |
      An *octave* is a content-addressed storage slot in the substrate's
      VFS. Cells live at octave paths; the VFS resolves names to
      content addresses via lexicon-typed parent/child constraints.
      Octave addressing is what makes the substrate's storage layer
      content-addressable while still permitting human-readable path
      navigation.
    sources:
      - core/cell-engine/src/octave.zig
      - runtime/shell/src/vfs/
    notes: |
      "Octave" canonical (concise, distinctive — a Semantos coinage).
      "VFS slot" is the descriptive variant.

  - id: oddjobz-cap-read-jobs
    canonical: cap.oddjobz.read_jobs
    aliases:
      - cap.oddjobz.read_jobs
    short: |
      Operator-held read-only capability authorising enumeration of
      Job cells via the Semantos Brain dispatcher's `jobs.find` / `jobs.find_by_id`
      resource commands. Domain flag 0x00010107.
    definition: |
      *cap.oddjobz.read_jobs* is the operator-held capability that gates
      the Semantos Brain dispatcher's typed jobs read commands (`jobs.find`,
      `jobs.find_by_id` per `find-jobs-resource`). It carries domain
      flag 0x00010107 (operator-sovereignty range; mint-time-
      deterministic per the §O3 scheme). Held by the operator-root cert
      and delegated to phone child certs by default via the D-O5p
      pairing allowlist — operators read their own jobs from any device
      they paired into. Read-only by design: the cap permits enumerating
      Job cells in their current FSM state but does NOT permit any FSM
      transition (those gate on `cap.oddjobz.quote`,
      `cap.oddjobz.dispatch`, `cap.oddjobz.invoice`, `cap.oddjobz.close`).
    domain_flag: 0x00010107
    holder: operator-root
    gates:
      - "(read-only — not an FSM transition)"
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/capabilities.ts
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/jobs_handler.zig
      - "BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §3"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5.followup-1 / D-O5m.followup-4 (2026-05-02).
      Conformance vector at
      extensions/oddjobz/tests/vectors/capabilities/read_jobs.json.
      Surfaces a separate read-cap so a future read-only-helm role
      (e.g. an operator's accountant) can be issued a cert that lists
      jobs without being able to mutate them.

      mints the Quote cell in `draft` state).  This `write_quote` cap
      is the read-side mirror — the dispatcher gate that permits an
      operator (or paired device) to create a Quote record in the
      helm-side store.  The two caps coexist by design.

  - id: oddjobz-chat-route
    canonical: oddjobz-chat-route
    aliases:
      - oddjobz-chat-route
      - chat route
      - RouteType.chat
    short: |
      Per-site `RouteType.chat` route declared in site.json that brain
      dispatches into `chat_http.handle` rather than serving a static
      file or running a WASM handler. Carries `scope`, `system_prompt`,
      `max_message_chars`. Public chat v0.5 wire seam.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz-chat-route* is a `RouteType.chat` site-config route the
      operator declares in `site.json` (e.g. `/api/v1/chat`). Visitor
      POSTs to this path are handled by brain's native `chat_http`
      module, not by a WASM handler binary. The route's `scope` is
      forwarded to `dispatcher.dispatch(llm.complete, scope=..., ...)`
      and is also the basis for the cap-name (`cap.llm.complete:<scope>`)
      that the site-level `anonymous_caps` allowlist must contain for
      visitors to reach the endpoint. The `system_prompt` is the
      tenant-configured prompt prepended to every visitor message.
      Lands with D-O6a; D-O6b layers persistence + lead extraction.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/site_config.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/chat_http.zig
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O6"
      - "BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §3 (line 182), §11 (line ~428)"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O6a (2026-05-01). Same-origin only on v0.5; full
      CORS lands with D-W1 Phase 3 + brain issue #273. The chat route
      shares one dispatcher with the rest of brain (REPL, identity_certs,
      bearer_tokens) — `--enable-repl` is the gate.

  - id: oddjobz-chat-widget-v05
    canonical: oddjobz-chat-widget-v05
    aliases:
      - oddjobz-chat-widget-v05
      - chat widget v0.5
    short: |
      Plain HTML/CSS/JS chat widget shipped at
      `extensions/oddjobz/public/chat-widget/`. Mounts into
      `#oddjobz-chat-widget`, POSTs to `/api/v1/chat`, renders bubbles.
      No build step; no framework. Lands with D-O6a.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz-chat-widget-v05* is a vanilla-JS, no-build chat widget
      that operators copy into their site's `content_root`. It auto-
      mounts into `#oddjobz-chat-widget` on `DOMContentLoaded`,
      POSTs `{message, session_id}` JSON bodies to a configurable
      endpoint (default `/api/v1/chat`) via `fetch`, and renders
      visitor / bot / system bubbles in an aria-live region. v0.5 has
      no persistence — chat messages do NOT become canon cells; that
      lands with D-O6b. Wire shape and accessibility behaviours
      documented at `extensions/oddjobz/public/chat-widget/README.md`.
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/public/chat-widget/chat-widget.js
      - extensions/oddjobz/public/chat-widget/chat-widget.css
      - extensions/oddjobz/public/chat-widget/README.md
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O6"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O6a (2026-05-01). The widget calls
      `dispatcher.dispatch(llm.complete, ...)` indirectly via the
      `oddjobz-chat-route` it POSTs to. Persistence (mapping replies +
      visitor messages onto `oddjobz.message.v1` cells, lead-extraction
      → `oddjobz.estimate.v1` drafts, ratification flow) is the D-O6b
      layer.

  - id: oddjobz-customer-cell-type
    canonical: oddjobz.customer.v1
    aliases:
      - oddjobz.customer.v1
      - oddjobz Customer cell
    short: |
      PERSISTENT cell carrying the identity of a trades customer; the
      cell accumulates Job/Visit/Invoice references and is never
      consumed (wire-level RELEVANT, code 3).
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.customer.v1* is the canonical identity record for a
      trades customer in the oddjobz extension. It is PERSISTENT
      (high-level §O2 label; wire-level RELEVANT) — the cell is never
      consumed by §O4 transitions; mutable fields like contact details
      flow via prevStateHash-chained successor cells of the same type.
      The type-hash is computed as
      SHA-256("oddjobz.customer:identify:inst.identity.customer-record").
    type_hash: c4cf2fd44009863eb6c45863875e34480f780b5c735e7025e3b0c44298fc1c14
    linearity_label: PERSISTENT
    wire_linearity: 3
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/cell-types/customer.ts
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O2"
    notes: |

  - id: oddjobz-message-cell-type
    canonical: oddjobz.message.v1
    aliases:
      - oddjobz.message.v1
      - oddjobz Message cell
    short: |

      many message cells accumulate, compaction reduces; wire-level

    definition: |
      *oddjobz.message.v1* is a chat message that patches a Job (or
      Customer) it references via parentHash. Per §O2 it is PATCH —
      wire-level RELEVANT (DUP allowed, no DROP). The kernel permits
      unbounded message cells against the same Job; the §O8
      compaction phase reduces them periodically.

      oddjobz.message.v1" naming-resolution decision, the §O6b chat
      persistence layer reuses this cell type rather than introducing
      a separate `chat.*` namespace; the cell already carries the
      `senderType=customer|operator|system|ai` enum and a
      `channel=webchat` value, so a chat-thread message and a
      legacy-OJT messages-table row are structurally the same cell.

  - id: oddjobz-lead-cell
    canonical: oddjobz.lead.v1
    aliases:
      - oddjobz.lead.v1
      - oddjobz Lead cell
      - oddjobz lead anchor
    short: |
      AFFINE cell — the ratification anchor for an inbound inquiry.
      Distinct from the Job FSM `lead` *state*; a Lead cell is the
      audit-anchor that links a chat session, a drafted Estimate, and
      the materialised Job; wire-level AFFINE (code 2).
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.lead.v1* is the cell minted at operator-ratification time
      alongside the §O4 `∅ → lead` Job genesis transition. Per D-O6b
      it is AFFINE — used at most once at ratify, droppable on stale
      queue entries, never DUP'd. Carries the chat-session id, the
      drafted Estimate id, the customer hint, the freshly-minted Job
      id, the operator cert that signed, the ratification timestamp,
      and the provenance enum (`from_chat`, `from_walk_in`,
      `from_phone`, `from_email`, `from_sms`, `from_referral`). NO
      FSM transition consumes a Lead cell; it sits alongside the Job
      it spawned as the record-of-creation.
    type_hash: c4cf2fd44009863ee3456bc1f4d270f4fdcdf8d87307f0d0e3b0c44298fc1c14
    linearity_label: AFFINE
    wire_linearity: 2
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/cell-types/lead.ts
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O6b (D-O6b)"
    notes: |
      Hash stable as of D-O6b (2026-05-01). Distinct concept from the
      Job FSM `lead` state — the FSM `lead` is a transient state on
      the LINEAR Job cell; the Lead CELL is a separate AFFINE cell
      that captures the ratification provenance.

  - id: oddjobz-lead-extract-resource
    canonical: oddjobz.lead_extract
    aliases:
      - oddjobz.lead_extract resource
      - lead-extract resource
    short: |
      Dispatcher resource that scans a chat session's messages and
      drafts an `oddjobz.estimate.v1` shape if a lead is detected.
      Internally calls the `llm.complete` resource with a lead-
      extraction system prompt scoped to `oddjobz-internal`.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.lead_extract* is the §O6b dispatcher resource that
      reads all `oddjobz.message.v1` cells for a given chatSessionId,
      runs them through `llm.complete` with a lead-extraction system
      prompt, and returns `{has_lead, draft_estimate, confidence}`.
      The drafted Estimate is NOT yet signed — that's the
      `oddjobz.ratification_queue` resource's job. This resource is
      service-side: it spends the same `cap.oddjobz.public_chat_serve`
      cap that minted the chat messages, so the lead-extraction step
      runs without operator capabilities (cheap and runtime-bounded).
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/lead-extract.ts
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O6b Deliverable 2"
      - "BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §2.5"
    notes: |
      Carpenter-musician motivating example from
      BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §2.5 verbatim: "resource:
      oddjobz.lead_extract (uses llm.complete with carpenter scope)".

  - id: oddjobz-ratification-queue-resource
    canonical: oddjobz.ratification_queue
    aliases:
      - oddjobz.ratification_queue resource
      - ratification queue resource
    short: |
      Dispatcher resource that holds drafted leads pending operator
      review. On `ratify`, signs the Estimate, mints the Lead cell,
      and drives the Job FSM `∅ → lead` transition.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.ratification_queue* is the §O6b dispatcher resource
      that bridges the lead-extraction service path to the operator-
      signed canonical-cell path. Commands:
        • `enqueue` — service-side, called when `oddjobz.lead_extract`
          returns has_lead=true. Persists the draft Estimate shape +
          chatSessionId on disk.
        • `list_pending` — operator reads pending entries.
        • `ratify` — operator signs. Spends
          `cap.oddjobz.write_customer`, mints the §O2
          `oddjobz.estimate.v1` cell, mints the §O6b
          `oddjobz.lead.v1` cell, drives the §O4 Job FSM `∅ → lead`
          genesis transition.
        • `reject` — operator drops the draft.
      The queue persists to disk so operator restart doesn't lose
      pending leads.
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/ratification-queue.ts
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O6b Deliverable 3"
    notes: |
      Cap-spend semantics: `cap.oddjobz.write_customer` is what the
      §O4 `∅ → lead` row gates against per the Job FSM table.
      Ratification is the only path that drives that genesis
      transition under operator authority.

  - id: oddjobz-chat-persistence
    canonical: oddjobz.chat_persistence
    aliases:
      - oddjobz chat persistence
      - chat persistence layer
    short: |
      The §O6b layer that persists each visitor message + LLM reply
      from the public chat widget as `oddjobz.message.v1` cells.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.chat_persistence* is the D-O6b shape that turns the
      stateless chat widget from D-O6a into a persistent thread.
      Each visitor turn produces TWO cells:
        1. `oddjobz.message.v1` for the visitor's message
           (senderType=customer, channel=webchat).
        2. `oddjobz.message.v1` for the LLM's response
           (senderType=ai, channel=webchat).
      Both cells carry the chat session id (so a thread is
      reconstructable) and the per-tenant context (oddjobtodd.info
      etc.). The visitor side spends `cap.oddjobz.public_chat_serve`
      via the dispatcher; the AI side is signed by the node service
      principal under the same cap.
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/chat-persistence.ts
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O6b Deliverable 1"
    notes: |
      The `oddjobz.message.v1` vs `chat.message.v1` naming-resolution
      decision lives here: D-O6b reuses `oddjobz.message.v1` from
      D-O2 rather than introducing a separate `chat.*` namespace.
      Justification: the §O2 messageCellType already declares
      `senderType ∈ {customer, operator, system, ai}` and a
      `channel=webchat` enum — exactly what a chat persistence layer
      needs. Adding a parallel `chat.message.v1` would fork the
      schema across the same logical concern; keeping the namespace
      unified preserves the §O8 compaction story (one message
      compactor, not two).

  - id: oddjobz-job-fsm
    canonical: oddjobz.job-fsm
    aliases:
      - oddjobz Job FSM
      - oddjobz.job-fsm
    short: |
      The Job state machine per §O4: the eight-state lead → quoted →
      scheduled → in_progress → completed → invoiced → paid → closed
      chain, with kernel-gated transitions enforced by K1/K2/K4.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.job-fsm* is the canonical state machine for
      oddjobz.job.v1 LINEAR cells per ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O4.
      Each transition consumes the current Job cell at the kernel
      gate (OP_ASSERTLINEAR / K1) and mints a successor under a
      fresh cell-id; cap-gated transitions additionally spend a
      capability UTXO matched by OP_CHECKDOMAINFLAG / K3a. The four
      cap-gated rows are lead → quoted (cap.oddjobz.quote),
      quoted → scheduled (cap.oddjobz.dispatch), completed →
      invoiced (cap.oddjobz.invoice), and paid → closed
      (cap.oddjobz.close); the three ungated rows are clock-tick or
      mark-done with the §O4 principal column dictating who signs.
    transitions: 7
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/job-fsm.ts
      - proofs/lean/Semantos/Extensions/Oddjobz/StateMachines/JobFSM.lean
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O4"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O4 (2026-05-01). Conformance vector at
      extensions/oddjobz/tests/vectors/state-machines/job_fsm.json
      (7 transitions). Lean theorems prove totality + K1 + K2 + K4
      with no `sorry`/`admit`.

  - id: oddjobz-quote-fsm
    canonical: oddjobz.quote-fsm
    aliases:
      - oddjobz Quote FSM
      - oddjobz.quote-fsm
    short: |
      The Quote state machine per §O4: draft → presented →
      {accepted | rejected | expired | superseded}. Gateless at the
      cell layer (the cap.oddjobz.quote spend lives on the Job FSM
      side); K1 is what kernel-enforces single-consumption.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.quote-fsm* is the state machine for oddjobz.quote.v1
      LINEAR cells. The §O4 plan describes only the Job FSM in full;
      the Quote FSM is inferred from the cell-type's QUOTE_STATUSES
      enum and §O4's claim that cap.oddjobz.quote is spent on the
      Job side's lead → quoted transition. Internal Quote
      transitions (draft → presented; presented → accepted | rejected
      | expired | superseded) are gateless at the cell layer; the
      customer's signature on accepted/rejected is modelled as the
      service principal at the TS-FSM altitude.
    transitions: 6
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/state-machines/quote-fsm.ts
      - proofs/lean/Semantos/Extensions/Oddjobz/StateMachines/QuoteFSM.lean

      extensions/oddjobz/tests/vectors/state-machines/quote_fsm.json.

  - id: oddjobz-visit-fsm
    canonical: oddjobz.visit-fsm
    aliases:
      - oddjobz Visit FSM
      - oddjobz.visit-fsm
    short: |
      The Visit state machine per §O4: scheduled → in_progress →
      completed (or cancelled). Mirrors the Job FSM's middle
      segment; gateless at the cell layer.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.visit-fsm* is the state machine for oddjobz.visit.v1
      LINEAR cells. Visit transitions mirror the Job FSM's
      scheduled → in_progress → completed segment — the
      cap.oddjobz.dispatch spend that mints a Visit happens on the
      Job side, so the Visit's own transitions are gateless at the
      cell layer. K1 still applies (each Visit cell is consumed once
      into its successor). Stamps actualStart on in_progress entry
      and outcome+actualEnd on completed entry per the cell-type
      validator's requirements.
    transitions: 4

  - id: oddjobz-invoice-fsm
    canonical: oddjobz.invoice-fsm
    aliases:
      - oddjobz Invoice FSM
      - oddjobz.invoice-fsm
    short: |
      The Invoice state machine per §O4: draft → sent → {viewed,
      partial, paid, overdue, cancelled}. Gateless at the cell
      layer; the §O4 K4 acceptance test grounds in this FSM's
      sent → paid (Stripe webhook).
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.invoice-fsm* is the state machine for
      oddjobz.invoice.v1 LINEAR cells. The §O4 plan's
      completed → invoiced (Job FSM) spends cap.oddjobz.invoice and
      mints the Invoice cell in draft state; the Invoice's own
      lifecycle then proceeds via draft → sent → {viewed | partial |
      paid | overdue | cancelled}. The §O4 K4 acceptance test
      grounds in this FSM's sent → paid (or any ancestor → paid) —
      an induced HTTP failure on the Stripe webhook leaves the
      Invoice cell unchanged and a retry succeeds.
    transitions: 15

      (15 transitions covering the full draft → … → paid|cancelled lattice).

  - id: oir
    canonical: OIR
    aliases:
      - OIR
      - Opcode IR
      - opcode-IR
    short: |
      The lower IR — A-normal-form, opcode-shaped, immediately
      lowerable to bytecode via `emit()`. Output of the lowering pass
      from SIR.
    definition: |
      *OIR* (Opcode IR) is the lower of the two intermediate
      representations in the pipeline. ANF-shaped: every binding has a
      name and a kind (`comparison`, `logical`, `capability`,
      `domainCheck`, `timeConstraint`, `hostCall`, `typeHashCheck`,
      `deref`); operands are names or constants only. The output of
      `lowerSIR()`; the input to `emit()`.
    sources:
      - core/semantos-ir/
      - docs/PIPELINE.md
    notes: |
      "OIR" canonical for the short form; "Opcode IR" only on first
      introduction. Two SIR programs that express the same semantic
      intent must produce α-equivalent OIR programs (the
      α-equivalence claim of paper A1).

  - id: opcode
    canonical: opcode
    aliases:
      - opcode
      - opcode set
    short: |
      A byte in the cell-engine's instruction set. Standard Bitcoin
      Script opcodes 0x00–0x4B; Plexus extension opcodes 0x4C–0xD0.
    definition: |
      An *opcode* is a byte in the cell engine's instruction set.
      Standard Bitcoin Script opcodes occupy `0x00`–`0x4B`; the Plexus
      extension range occupies `0x4C`–`0xD0`. The full opcode table
      is in `docs/canon/opcodes.yml` (which is the source of truth for
      the protocol spec's opcode reference).
    sources:
      - core/cell-engine/src/opcodes.zig
      - docs/canon/opcodes.yml
    notes: |
      "Opcode" canonical for the individual instruction; "opcode set"
      is fine when referring to the collection. The Protocol Spec
      v0.01 documents the Plexus extension range as `0xC0`–`0xCF`;
      current Zig source uses `0x4C`–`0xD0`. This is a reconciliation
      task tracked against `docs/canon/opcodes.yml` (canonical:
      `0x4C`–`0xD0` per the implementation).

  - id: plexus
    canonical: Plexus
    aliases:
      - Plexus
    short: |
      The recovery substrate, identity DAG, and capability domain that
      Semantos depends on. Built by Dusk Inc on behalf of RBS (RBS owns
      70%); per doc plan §5, treated as part of the integrated stack
      under RBS, not as a separate product.
    definition: |
      *Plexus* is the recovery substrate, identity DAG, capability
      domain, and attestation authority that Semantos integrates.
      Implemented as a Go service (single deployable, Gin framework,
      BRC-100-authenticated middleware) plus client-side libraries.
      RBS-owned IP (70%); engineered by Dusk Inc on behalf of RBS.
      Per doc plan §5, Plexus is treated as part of the integrated
      stack and documented under the RBS umbrella, not as a separate
      external dependency.

    notes: |

      is settled per doc plan §5; engineering credit to Dusk Inc is
      handled in colophons and acknowledgements rather than via
      separate-product framing.

  - id: provision-tenant
    canonical: provision-tenant
    aliases:
      - provision-tenant
      - brain provision-tenant
      - semantos node provision-tenant
    short: |
      The CLI verb that runs the §11 operator flow end-to-end —
      validate manifest, allocate port, lay down dirs, mint caps,
      copy bundles, write systemd + Caddy, run first-boot, emit
      pairing URL.  D-O10's productisation gate.
    definition: |
      *provision-tenant* is the Semantos Brain CLI verb (`brain provision-tenant
      <manifest.toml>`) that runs the full §11 operator flow for a
      new tenant brain on a Semantos sovereign-node host.  Twelve
      numbered steps from "validating manifest" through "emit pairing
      token", with byte-stable `[provision] <message>...    <result>`
      log lines per the canonical example in
      ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §11.  D-W2 Phase 0 fold-in: the
      flow auto-injects `[trusted_signers.platform]` between steps
      1 and 2, baking the operator's pubkey into the canonical
      manifest archive at `/etc/semantos/tenants/<domain>.toml` with
      `removable = false`.  Plexus-side calls (owner-cert + recovery-
      enrolment SPV verification) are STUBBED for v0.1; D-W2 Phase 1
      replaces the stubs with real Plexus client calls.  Ships as
      `brain provision-tenant`; a future `semantos node provision-
      tenant` wrapper is documented as TODO.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/provision_tenant.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/cli.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/provision_tenant_conformance.zig
      - docs/operator-runbooks/provision-tenant.md
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §11"
      - docs/canon/deliverables.yml D-O10
    notes: |
      D-O10 ships as `brain provision-tenant`.  The §11 brief writes
      it as `semantos node provision-tenant`; a thin `semantos`
      wrapper binary that delegates is future work.  The flow is
      idempotent on re-runs against the same domain (port re-used;
      compareImmutability refuses any edit/drop of `removable=false`
      signers vs the prior archive).

  - id: publish-frame
    canonical: publish frame
    aliases:
      - publish frame
      - extension-bundle frame
      - publish-bundle frame
    short: |
      A BRC-12 framed UDP datagram that carries an extension bundle's
      bytes, namespace, version, and signer pubkey to the shard-proxy
      ingress. The frame's txid slot points at the on-chain
      extension-publish tx so subscribers can SPV-cross-reference.
    definition: |
      A *publish frame* is a BRC-12 UDP datagram emitted by the D-W2
      Phase 1 shard-proxy publisher (`extensions/oddjobz/tools/
      publish-bundle.ts`). The outer frame is `ShardFrame.encode`'s
      canonical envelope (44-byte header + payload, `core/protocol-
      types/src/overlay/shard-frame.ts`); the txid slot carries the
      publish-tx's txid in internal byte order. The inner payload is
      `extension-bundle-v1 || u32 bundle_len || bundle_bytes ||
      ns_len || ns || ver_len || ver || signer_pubkey (33B)`.
      Subscribers receive the frame, recompute `bundle_hash`, SPV-
      verify the publish tx, signature-check, scope-check, then apply
      or quarantine.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - extensions/oddjobz/tools/publish-bundle.ts
    notes: |
      Frame type is discriminated by the inner payload's version tag.
      Future frame types (`nullifier`, `bundle-ack`, `metadata-update`)
      ride the same outer envelope with a different inner tag. v0.1
      caps the bundle payload at `SHARD_MAX_PAYLOAD_SIZE` (10 MiB);
      larger bundles will need chunking, deferred to a future PR.

  - id: recovery-payload
    canonical: recovery payload
    aliases:
      - recovery payload
      - recovery export
      - metadata export
      - export payload
    short: |
      ~3.4KB BRC-100-signed JSON blob assembled by the Plexus Recovery
      Service in phase 3 of the recovery flow. Contains derivation_state
      + domain_ceilings + edge_backup_recipes + schemaMappings; lets a
      recovering device locally re-derive its key universe.
    definition: |
      A *recovery payload* is the approximately-3.4-KB BRC-100-signed
      JSON blob assembled by the Plexus Recovery Service in phase 3 of
      the four-phase recovery flow. Contains derivation state, domain
      ceilings, edge backup recipes, and schema mappings — the
      deterministic metadata sufficient for a recovering device to
      locally re-derive its full key universe via PBKDF2 over the
      challenge set. The payload is cryptographically useless without
      the user's challenge answers (zero-knowledge property).
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §11, §28"
      - extensions/recovery/src/export-payload.ts
      - core/identity-ports/src/types.ts
    notes: |
      "Recovery payload" canonical (matches Plexus Tech §11). The
      other variants ("recovery export", "metadata export", "export
      payload") are descriptive but inconsistent across older docs.

  - id: region
    canonical: region
    aliases:
      - region
      - shard
      - WorldHost.Region
    short: |
      Authoritative shard in the World Host. One Region = one OTP
      GenServer = one PubSub topic = one supervisor owning its entities.
      A1 in the unification matrix.
    definition: |
      A *region* is an authoritative shard in the World Host. One
      region equals one OTP supervisor process, one PubSub topic, and
      one set of co-located WorldEntity GenServers. Authority is
      exclusive — exactly one process commits state for a given entity
      at a time. Cross-region entity migration uses a 2-phase commit
      that preserves the per-entity hash chain. A1 in the unification
      matrix.
    sources:
      - apps/world-host/lib/world_host/region.ex
      - "docs/prd/WORLD-PROTOCOL.md"
    notes: |
      "Region" canonical (matches WORLD-PROTOCOL.md and the codebase).
      "Shard" is the generic distributed-systems term and acceptable
      in academic prose; `WorldHost.Region` is the Elixir module name.

  - id: signed-bundle
    canonical: SignedBundle
    aliases:
      - SignedBundle
      - signed bundle
      - BRC-100 envelope
    short: |
      The wire envelope for any cross-process or cross-node message.
      BRC-100 signed; carries identity + nonce + timestamp +
      signature + cert. Phoenix-channel JSON gets wrapped in this
      via deliverables D-C1/D-C2.
    definition: |
      A *`SignedBundle<T>`* is the canonical wire envelope for any
      cross-process or cross-node message in the unified architecture.
      A BRC-100-signed CBOR envelope carrying an
      `x-brc100-identitykey`, `x-brc100-nonce`, `x-brc100-timestamp`,
      `x-brc100-signature`, and `x-brc52-certificate`, wrapping a
      payload of type `T`. Verifier-Sidecar-checked at every adapter
      boundary.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §1, §4"
      - runtime/session-protocol/src/bundle-envelope.ts
    notes: |
      `SignedBundle` (PascalCase, code-style) canonical because it is
      the actual TS type name. "Signed bundle" is the prose form of
      the same concept; "BRC-100 envelope" is the standard-citation
      variant. The three are equivalent referents.

  - id: signed-bundle-envelope
    canonical: SignedBundle envelope
    aliases:
      - SignedBundle envelope (Phase 4)
      - mesh transport envelope
      - dispatch SignedBundle
    short: |
      The D-W1 Phase 4 wire envelope a mesh peer (mobile shell,
      federated tenant brain) wraps a dispatch Request inside before
      sending it to a Semantos Brain brain. Cert chain + signature + nonce +
      timestamp + payload.
    definition: |
      The *SignedBundle envelope* is the D-W1 Phase 4 mesh transport's
      wire shape (per BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §5.4). Carries the
      sender's BRC-52 cert chain (leaf-first), an addressed
      `recipient_cert_id` (the brain's own root cert id; broadcast
      bundles are rejected), a typed `payload_type` tag (e.g.
      `"dispatch.request"`), the opaque payload bytes (typically a
      wire `Request` envelope), an ECDSA-secp256k1 64-byte compact
      signature over `"BRAIN-SIGNED-BUNDLE-v1" || canonical_json`, and
      `signature_metadata` with the algorithm + nonce_hex (32-byte
      anti-replay) + Unix timestamp. Codec lives in
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/signed_bundle.zig`; TS sender helper at
      `extensions/oddjobz/tools/send-bundle.ts`.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §5.4
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/signed_bundle.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/tools/send-bundle.ts
    notes: |
      Distinct from the `signed-bundle` glossary entry above, which is
      the BRC-100-signed CBOR envelope used at the Verifier-Sidecar
      boundary. The Phase 4 envelope is a structurally similar but
      separately-versioned wire shape — JSON over HTTP today, with
      BRC-52 cert chain semantics and addressed-bundle posture (Slice
      5c). Future revisions may converge the two; for v0.1 they're
      sibling envelopes serving distinct seams.

  - id: signed-bundle-transport
    canonical: SignedBundle mesh transport
    aliases:
      - SignedBundle transport
      - mesh transport (D-W1 Phase 4)
      - bundle mesh
    short: |
      The dispatcher transport mesh peers (mobile Flutter shell,
      federated tenant brains) use to drive a Semantos Brain brain's dispatcher.
      Same dispatcher, same audit pair, same cap check — different
      transport adapter.
    definition: |
      The *SignedBundle mesh transport* is one of the four transports
      in the D-W1 unification (alongside in-process, Unix socket,
      HTTP/WSS).  A peer wraps a wire `Request` envelope inside a
      `signed-bundle-envelope`, posts it via the deployment's chosen
      I/O layer (HTTP at v0.1; BLE / multicast / Plexus push in
      future deployments), and the receiving brain decodes →
      verifies cert chain + signature + freshness + nonce → dispatches
      against its single `Dispatcher` instance with `auth.cert =
      <peer's leaf cert>`.  Capability check fires on the leaf cert's
      stored cap set.  Audit pair tagged `transport=signed_bundle`.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §5.4 + §8 Phase 4
      - docs/operator-runbooks/signed-bundle-mesh.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/transport/signed_bundle.zig
    notes: |
      Closes the original D-W1 transport-unification scope — Phases
      0-3 + Phase 4 cover all four transport adapters spec'd in §5.

  - id: bundle-receive-endpoint
    canonical: bundle receive endpoint
    aliases:
      - bundle endpoint
      - signed-bundle endpoint
      - "/api/v1/bundle"
    short: |
      The HTTP path a Semantos Brain brain binds for SignedBundle mesh transport.
      Default `/api/v1/bundle`; opt-in per deployment via
      `brain serve --signed-bundle-endpoint <path>`.
    definition: |
      The *bundle receive endpoint* is the HTTP path the v0.1 mesh
      transport's POST seam binds to.  Default disabled; the operator
      opts in per deployment via `brain serve --signed-bundle-endpoint
      <path>` (conventional value `/api/v1/bundle`).  Reserved BEFORE
      route lookup in `site_server` so the operator's site config
      cannot shadow it.  The brain's `expected_recipient` (operator-
      root cert id) is what mesh peers MUST address bundles to; the
      endpoint path is operator-chosen but the recipient is fixed by
      the brain's identity.  When the operator hasn't enabled the
      endpoint, the path returns 404 — making the absence
      indistinguishable from "not configured".
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/transport/signed_bundle.zig (DEFAULT_BUNDLE_ENDPOINT_PATH)
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/site_server.zig (attachBundleAcceptor)
      - docs/operator-runbooks/signed-bundle-mesh.md
    notes: |
      Future BLE / multicast / Plexus-push transports decode the same
      envelope shape via the same codec but plug into the I/O layer
      differently — `processBundle(bytes) -> Outcome` is the
      transport-agnostic entry point any future transport calls.

  - id: signed-bundle-mobile-port
    canonical: SignedBundle mobile codec
    aliases:
      - Dart SignedBundle codec
      - mobile mesh codec (D-O5m.followup-6)
    short: |
      The Dart port of the Zig SignedBundle codec at
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/`.  Phase 1 of D-O5m.followup-6
      proves byte-identical canonical preimage + signature output
      against the Zig codec via a committed cross-language fixture.
    definition: |
      The *SignedBundle mobile codec* is the pure-Dart implementation
      of the wire shape the Zig brain accepts: `CertRef`,
      `SignatureMetadata`, and `SignedBundle` value classes mirroring
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/signed_bundle.zig`'s structs, plus
      `computeCanonicalPreimage` / `signBundle` /
      `verifyBundleSignature` mirroring the Zig encoder + signer +
      recovery-loop verifier.  Reuses the cell-signer's deterministic-k
      ECDSA primitives (cell_signer.dart) without duplicating the
      crypto.  Cross-language parity is enforced by
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/mesh/signed_bundle_test.dart` against
      the fixture at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/tests/vectors/signed-bundle-canonical-fixture.json`
      (generated by the Zig fixture-gen test that emits identical bytes
      under the same struct inputs).  Phase 2 builds the mesh transport,
      outbox refactor, brain-side routing, and UI on top of this proven
      codec.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/signed_bundle.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/cert_ref.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/signature_metadata.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/mesh/signed_bundle_test.dart
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/signed_bundle_canonical_fixture_gen.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/vectors/signed-bundle-canonical-fixture.json
    notes: |
      Sibling of `cell-signing-mobile` from D-O5m.followup-8: that one
      proves Dart-Zig parity for cell-payload signing; this one proves
      it for the SignedBundle wire envelope.  Both use the same
      cell_signer ECDSA primitives — without that shared signer the
      load-bearing parity claim of "phone speaks the same wire as the
      brain" would split into two parallel implementations to maintain.

  - id: brain-signed-bundle-v1-canonical-preimage
    canonical: BRAIN-SIGNED-BUNDLE-v1 canonical preimage
    aliases:
      - SignedBundle canonical preimage
      - canonical signature preimage (mesh)
    short: |
      The byte sequence the SignedBundle ECDSA signer hashes:
      `"BRAIN-SIGNED-BUNDLE-v1"` ASCII bytes followed by the canonical
      sorted-key JSON serialisation of the bundle MINUS the signature
      field.
    definition: |
      The *BRAIN-SIGNED-BUNDLE-v1 canonical preimage* is the byte string
      the ECDSA-secp256k1-SHA256 signer prehashes when producing or
      verifying a SignedBundle signature.  Construction: the ASCII
      domain tag `"BRAIN-SIGNED-BUNDLE-v1"` (no separator), followed by
      the canonical JSON serialisation of the bundle with the
      `signature` field omitted.  Field order in the bundle JSON is
      fixed (`payload, payload_type, recipient_cert_id,
      sender_cert_chain, signature_metadata, v`); CertRef field order
      is fixed (`cert_id, context_tag, parent_cert_id, pubkey`);
      SignatureMetadata field order is fixed (`algorithm, nonce_hex,
      timestamp_unix`).  No whitespace between tokens; integers
      base-10; strings JSON-escaped per the standard.  The domain tag
      prevents cross-protocol signature reuse — a sig over a bundle
      preimage is meaningfully distinct from a sig over a cell-engine
      envelope or a publish-tx digest.  Three implementations agree
      byte-for-byte: Zig (`signed_bundle.zig::canonicalSignaturePreimage`),
      TS (`send-bundle.ts::canonicalSignaturePreimage`), Dart
      (`signed_bundle.dart::computeCanonicalPreimage`).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/signed_bundle.zig (canonicalSignaturePreimage,
        writeBundleJson)
      - extensions/oddjobz/tools/send-bundle.ts (encodeBundle,
        canonicalSignaturePreimage)
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/signed_bundle.dart
        (computeCanonicalPreimage, _writeBundleJson)
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/vectors/signed-bundle-canonical-fixture.json
    notes: |
      Cross-language byte parity is the load-bearing correctness proof
      for the mesh transport: without it a Dart-built bundle would not
      round-trip through the Zig brain (and vice versa).  The fixture
      test in each language asserts the parity at every commit so
      regressions are caught at CI time, not in the field.

  - id: sir
    canonical: SIR
    aliases:
      - SIR
      - Semantic IR
      - semantic-IR
    short: |
      The upper IR — semantically typed. Carries jural category,
      taxonomy coordinates, identity context, governance domain
      context (trust class, proof requirement, exec authority,
      linearity, allowed emit ops). Output of the surface-language
      compilation phase.
    definition: |
      *SIR* (Semantic IR) is the upper of the two intermediate
      representations in the pipeline. Each SIR node carries a jural
      category (one of the seven), taxonomy coordinates
      (what / how / why / where), an identity binding, a governance
      context (`trustClass`, `proofRequirement`, `executionAuthority`,
      `linearity`, optional `allowedEmitOps`), provenance, and a
      typed constraint structure. Output of any surface-language
      compilation; input to `lowerSIR()`.
    sources:
      - core/semantos-sir/
      - "docs/SEMANTIC-IR-ARCHITECTURE.md"
    notes: |
      "SIR" canonical for the short form; "Semantic IR" only on first
      introduction. The SIR is the layer at which trust-tier and
      allowed-emit-ops enforcement happens (paper A1 §4.3).

  - id: shard-group-derivation
    canonical: shard-group derivation
    aliases:
      - shard-group derivation
      - shard_group_id
      - shard group id
    short: |
      The deterministic mapping from an extension-publish tx's id to
      the shard group on the proxy fabric where bundle bytes are
      delivered: `sha256("extension-publish:" || tx_id_hex)`.
    definition: |
      The *shard-group derivation* (D-W2 §3) is the deterministic
      function that maps an `extension-publish-tx`'s display-order
      txid to the shard-proxy multicast group used for bundle-byte
      delivery: `shard_group_id = sha256("extension-publish:" ||
      tx_id_hex)`. Both publisher and subscriber compute this
      independently — the chain is the source of truth for which
      group an installation lives in. Subscribers join the group at
      boot using the txid from their `[trusted_signers]` table; a
      fresh brain replays the shard's history from Pravega and
      converges to the same state.
    sources:
      - docs/design/BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/extension_publish.zig
    notes: |
      The byte-stable derivation is pinned by `runtime/semantos-brain/tests/
      extension_publish_conformance.zig`. The Zig and TS sides both
      compute it; tests assert byte-equal output. The SHA-256 prefix
      string `"extension-publish:"` discriminates this derivation
      from future related schemes (e.g. nullifier-channel grouping).

  - id: spv
    canonical: SPV
    aliases:
      - SPV
      - Simplified Payment Verification
      - SPV check
    short: |
      Indexer-less verification that a transaction is valid + confirmed
      via merkle proof (BUMP) + tx envelope (BEEF). Used by the
      Verifier Sidecar to check capability UTXO state without a
      blockchain indexer.
    definition: |
      *SPV* (Simplified Payment Verification) is indexer-less
      verification that a transaction is valid and confirmed, using a
      merkle proof (BUMP) and a transaction envelope (BEEF). Used by
      the Verifier Sidecar to check capability UTXO state without
      requiring a blockchain indexer.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §4, §7, §8"
    notes: |
      "SPV" canonical; "Simplified Payment Verification" only on first
      introduction. SPV proves transaction inclusion in a block; it
      does not by itself prove a UTXO is unspent — that requires an
      additional UTXO-set query, liveness protocol, or watchman
      pattern (cf. capability token notes).

  - id: substrate
    canonical: substrate
    aliases:
      - substrate
    short: |
      Components whose job IS to implement the unification axes.
      ✓ by construction (or are bugs against their own spec). Per the

      construction (or are bugs against their own spec). Per the
      unification roadmap §2 the ten substrate components are: cell

      recovery, Capability Domain, Verifier Sidecar, mesh, VFS, SIR
      and lexicons, Lean proof layer, and MFP. The substrate is the

      adapters are the other half.

  - id: sovereign-push
    canonical: sovereign push
    aliases:
      - sovereign push
      - sovereign-push
    short: |
      The architectural property that operator-readable content
      never flows through Google FCM or Apple APNs.  Push payloads
      from the brain are wake-only opaque envelopes; the device
      fetches the real event content from the sovereign brain over
      WSS after waking.
    definition: |
      *Sovereign push* is the property that the operator's economic
      execution path stays inside the sovereign node even when the
      mobile shell is backgrounded.  Google and Apple are
      architecturally unavoidable in the OS-level wake-up loop, but
      they only ever see an opaque envelope of `event_id + ts`.
      Operator content (lead summaries, customer names, prices,
      transcripts) flows directly brain→device over the bearer-
      authenticated WSS via the `helm.fetch_since` RPC, never
      through a third-party push gateway.
    sources:
      - docs/operator-runbooks/push-architecture.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/push_dispatcher.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/helm_event_broker.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced sovereign-push D.1 (PR
      `sovereign-push-d1-wake-only`, brain-side half).  Pairs with
      `wake-only-push` (the wire shape) and `helm.fetch_since`
      (the device-side fetch).  Phase D.2 = mobile silent handler;
      Phase D.3 = UnifiedPush adapter.

  - id: tenant

      The *tenant-extensions-block* is the `[extensions]` table
      (required) plus zero or more `[extensions.config_overrides.<x>]`
      tables (optional) in a tenant manifest.  `extensions.install`
      is a non-empty array of extension names matching `[a-z][a-z0-9-]
      {0,63}`.  Each `[extensions.config_overrides.<x>]` is a free-
      form `key = "string"` map preserved opaquely by the manifest
      parser; the extension's own loader is responsible for typed
      interpretation.  Validator enforces that every override target
      `<x>` appears in `extensions.install`.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/tenant_manifest.zig
      - docs/operator-runbooks/tenant-manifest-schema.md
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §11"
    notes: |
      Lands with D-O8.  Extension-bundle copy step + loader-side
      override delivery lands with D-O10.  Free-form override shape
      is the §3(c) decision in the D-O8 brief — strict per-extension
      typing is deferred until concrete extension overrides land.

  - id: tenant-manifest
    canonical: tenant-manifest
    aliases:
      - tenant-manifest
      - tenant manifest
      - tenant.toml
      - acme-plumbing-tenant.toml
    short: |
      Operator-facing TOML file that fully describes a tenant
      deployment on a sovereign-node host.  Single source of truth
      for what defines a tenant; consumed by D-O9 (systemd / Caddy
      templating) and D-O10 (provisioning CLI).
    definition: |
      A *tenant-manifest* is the operator-facing TOML file that
      defines a tenant deployment on a Semantos sovereign-node host.
      It is the single source of truth for a tenant's identity
      (owner cert, recovery enrolment), installed extensions,
      branding, network surface (CORS / CSP / public origin), and
      default capability allowlists.  The manifest is parsed +
      validated by `runtime/semantos-brain/src/tenant_manifest.zig`; D-O9
      consumes it to render the per-tenant `semantos-shell@.service`
      systemd unit + Caddy block; D-O10's
      `semantos node provision-tenant` runs the full provisioning
      flow end-to-end including cert verification against Plexus,
      port allocation, dir layout, extension-bundle copy, and
      first-boot.  One manifest = one tenant; one tenant maps to
      one or more brain sites (`site_config.zig`).  Conventional
      archive location post-provisioning:
      `/etc/semantos/tenants/<domain>.toml`.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/tenant_manifest.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/vectors/tenant-manifests/
      - docs/operator-runbooks/tenant-manifest-schema.md
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §11 (canonical example)"
      - docs/canon/deliverables.yml D-O8
    notes: |
      Distinct from the substrate-internal `tenant` glossary entry
      which refers to a node in the live structural DAG (a Plexus-
      Tech §19 client-owned graph node).  Same word, different
      layers: substrate-tenant lives in the kernel / cell-engine
      space; tenant-manifest lives in the operator / productisation
      space.  Lands with D-O8 (schema + parser + validator only).
      D-O9 wires templating; D-O10 wires the end-to-end CLI.

  - id: tenant-data-dir-layout
    canonical: tenant-data-dir-layout
    aliases:
      - tenant-data-dir-layout
      - /var/lib/semantos/<domain>
      - tenant data dir
    short: |
      Per-tenant on-disk state layout under
      `/var/lib/semantos/<domain>/`.  Laid down by D-O10's
      `provision-tenant` step 5; isolated per-tenant by D-O9's
      systemd `ReadWritePaths`.
    definition: |
      The *tenant data dir layout* is the canonical directory tree
      every Semantos tenant brain writes to: `/var/lib/semantos/
      <domain>/` containing `audit.log`, `identity-certs.log`,
      `bearer-tokens.log`, `branding/` (logo, favicon, landing-page
      template), `extensions/` (sovereignty + oddjobz + any installed
      extension bundles), and `sites/<domain>/site.json` (the
      D-O9 site config).  D-O10's `provision-tenant` flow step 5
      creates the dirs; the Semantos Brain daemon writes to them at boot.
      D-O9's per-tenant systemd unit pins each tenant to its own
      `ReadWritePaths=/var/lib/semantos/%i` so a compromised brain
      instance for tenant A cannot write into tenant B's state dir.
      The canonical manifest archive is a sibling at
      `/etc/semantos/tenants/<domain>.toml`, not inside the data dir
      — operators edit the archive; the daemon reads it.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/provision_tenant.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/deploy/systemd/semantos-shell@.service
      - docs/operator-runbooks/provision-tenant.md
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §11 (canonical layout)"
    notes: |
      Cross-tenant isolation depends on three layers: systemd
      `ReadWritePaths`, filesystem ownership (semantos:semantos
      0700), and the cell-engine capability domain (per-tenant
      capability tokens, ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §10).  Operator
      backups should snapshot the whole `/var/lib/semantos/` tree
      atomically; partial backups break the cert / token / extension
      cross-references.

  - id: tenant-platform-signer
    canonical: tenant-platform-signer
    aliases:
      - tenant-platform-signer
      - "[trusted_signers.platform]"
      - platform-tier signer
      - operator signer
    short: |
      The Tier 1 signer entry in a tenant manifest's
      `[trusted_signers]` block.  Embedded by D-O10's `provision-
      tenant` at brain creation with `removable = false`; carries
      the operator's authority to push security patches and
      extension updates to the brain.
    definition: |
      The *tenant platform signer* is the Tier 1 entry in a tenant
      manifest's `[trusted_signers]` block (per BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-
      AND-REVOCATION §2 + §3): the operator's signing key, embedded
      at brain creation time by D-O10's `provision-tenant` flow with
      `removable = false`, `scope = "*"`, and a `plexus_identity_tx`
      that registers the pubkey on-chain via Plexus.  The platform
      signer is what gives the operator the authority to push
      security patches, compatibility updates, and core extension
      updates to every tenant brain they've provisioned — without
      polling, without a CDN, without any operator-tenant trust
      handshake at update time.  The brain SPV-verifies the
      `plexus_identity_tx` before honouring the entry (D-W2 Phase 1+);
      the operator-edited fake key gets dropped at parse time.  The
      removability invariant is enforced by the manifest validator's
      `compareImmutability(prev, new)`: any edit or drop of the
      platform entry across manifest versions refuses.  The tenant
      can remove the platform signer only by taking the brain
      off-platform (self-host migration), which is the
      "landlord-doesn't-have-a-key-to-the-front-door" property of
      the tier model.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/tenant_manifest.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/provision_tenant.zig
      - "BRAIN-EXTENSION-DELIVERY-AND-REVOCATION.md §2, §3"
      - docs/operator-runbooks/provision-tenant.md
    notes: |
      D-W2 Phase 0 (the schema extension + provisioning-time
      injection) lands with D-O10.  D-W2 Phases 1-4 (the runtime
      delivery + nullifier + rotation flow that actually consumes
      the platform-signer entry) are subsequent commissions.
      Without D-W2 Phase 1+ runtime, the platform-signer entry is
      future-compat: documented + parsed + validated, but the
      brain doesn't yet subscribe to its shard group.

  - id: tenant-network-block
    canonical: tenant-network-block
    aliases:
      - tenant-network-block
      - "[network]"
      - manifest network section
    short: |
      The optional `[network]` table in a tenant manifest.  Carries
      `public_origin`, `cors_allowed_origins`, `content_security_
      policy` — all propagate to per-site `site_config` at
      provisioning time.
    definition: |
      The *tenant-network-block* is the optional `[network]` table
      inside a tenant manifest.  All fields optional.
      `public_origin` defaults to `https://<tenant.domain>` at
      D-O10 provisioning time.  `cors_allowed_origins` is an array
      of `<scheme>://<host>[:port]` origins (or the literal `"*"`
      wildcard) that propagate to `site_config.cors_allowed_origins`
      (D-W1 Phase 3 surface).  `content_security_policy` is a
      verbatim CSP header value propagating to
      `site_config.content_security_policy`.
    sources:
