    notes: |
      Lands with D-O8 (parser + validator).  Per-site propagation
      step + D-O9 Caddy `server_name` override land with D-O9 / D-O10.

  - id: tenant-systemd-unit
    canonical: tenant-systemd-unit
    aliases:
      - tenant-systemd-unit
      - "semantos-shell@.service"
      - per-tenant systemd unit
      - tenant @-instance unit
    short: |
      The systemd `@`-instance template unit
      (`semantos-shell@.service`) that runs one brain process per
      tenant on a multi-tenant sovereign-node host.  `%i` resolves
      to the tenant domain.
    definition: |
      The *tenant-systemd-unit* is the systemd template at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/deploy/systemd/semantos-shell@.service`,
      installed to `/etc/systemd/system/semantos-shell@.service`.
      Operators start one instance per tenant via
      `systemctl start semantos-shell@<domain>.service`.  The `%i`
      instance specifier resolves to the tenant's FQDN and threads
      through the unit's `Environment=` lines + `ExecStart=`
      (`/opt/semantos/brain serve
      --tenant-manifest=/etc/semantos/tenants/%i.toml`).  Per-tenant
      isolation is enforced by `ReadWritePaths=/var/lib/semantos/%i`
      (cross-tenant write attempts get EACCES).  Distinct from the
      legacy single-tenant `semantos-shell.service` unit which uses
      a `BRAIN_DOMAIN` drop-in instead of an instance specifier; the
      two coexist and the operator chooses based on tenancy model.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/deploy/systemd/semantos-shell@.service
      - runtime/semantos-brain/deploy/systemd/README-multitenant.md
      - docs/operator-runbooks/multi-tenant-deployment.md
      - docs/canon/deliverables.yml D-O9
    notes: |
      Lands with D-O9.  D-O10's `semantos node provision-tenant`
      writes the per-tenant manifest archive at
      `/etc/semantos/tenants/<domain>.toml` + invokes
      `systemctl enable --now semantos-shell@<domain>.service`.

  - id: tenant-caddy-block
    canonical: tenant-caddy-block
    aliases:
      - tenant-caddy-block
      - per-tenant Caddy block
      - tenant Caddy snippet
      - "/etc/caddy/conf.d/<domain>.conf"
    short: |
      The per-tenant Caddy v2 site-block snippet rendered by D-O9
      from a parsed tenant manifest.  Drops at
      `/etc/caddy/conf.d/<domain>.conf`; the host's main Caddyfile
      imports the directory.
    definition: |
      The *tenant-caddy-block* is the Caddy v2 site-block snippet
      rendered for one tenant.  It terminates HTTPS via
      `tls { on_demand }` (Caddy negotiates Let's Encrypt
      per-domain on first request), reverse-proxies `/api/v1/*`,
      `/helm/*`, and the catch-all to `localhost:<listen_port>`
      where `<listen_port>` is the manifest's
      `[tenant] listen_port_start`, optionally emits a CORS
      preflight matcher when `[network] cors_allowed_origins` is
      set (wildcard echo via `{header.Origin}` if `*`, else pinned
      via an `@allowed_origins` matcher), and writes a per-tenant
      access log at `/var/log/caddy/<domain>.access.log`.  The
      renderer at `runtime/semantos-brain/src/caddy_template.zig` is pure +
      byte-stable; conformance vectors live at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/tests/vectors/caddy-blocks/*.conf.expected`.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/caddy_template.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/vectors/caddy-blocks/
      - runtime/semantos-brain/deploy/caddy/Caddyfile.example
      - docs/operator-runbooks/multi-tenant-deployment.md
      - docs/canon/deliverables.yml D-O9
    notes: |
      Lands with D-O9.  Top-level convention: the host's main
      `/etc/caddy/Caddyfile` does
      `import /etc/caddy/conf.d/*` once and each tenant's snippet
      drops in beside the others.  D-O10's CLI verb writes the
      snippet during `provision-tenant`.

  - id: multi-tenant-deployment
    canonical: multi-tenant-deployment
    aliases:
      - multi-tenant-deployment
      - multi-tenant host
      - per-tenant deployment shape
    short: |
      The shape of a sovereign-node host running two or more
      tenants — per-tenant systemd `@`-instance unit, per-tenant
      Caddy snippet, per-tenant state dir, per-tenant manifest
      archive.  Composes D-O8 + D-O9 + D-O10.
    definition: |
      A *multi-tenant deployment* is a Semantos sovereign-node host
      configured to run two or more independent tenant brains on
      the same machine.  Each tenant has a unique FQDN and gets:
      (1) one systemd instance via the
      `semantos-shell@<domain>.service` template; (2) one Caddy
      snippet at `/etc/caddy/conf.d/<domain>.conf`; (3) an isolated
      state dir at `/var/lib/semantos/<domain>/`; (4) a manifest
      archive at `/etc/semantos/tenants/<domain>.toml`; (5) a
      unique listen port allocated from the manifest's
      `[tenant] listen_port_start`.  Cross-tenant isolation is
      enforced at three layers: systemd
      (`ReadWritePaths=/var/lib/semantos/%i`), filesystem
      ownership (per-domain state dirs owned by the `semantos`
      user with mode `0700`), and the cell-engine capability
      domain (per-tenant capability tokens — see
      ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §10).
    sources:
      - docs/operator-runbooks/multi-tenant-deployment.md
      - runtime/semantos-brain/deploy/systemd/semantos-shell@.service
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/caddy_template.zig
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §10, §11"
      - docs/canon/deliverables.yml D-O9
    notes: |
      Lands with D-O9 (template + renderer).  D-O10 ships the
      `semantos node provision-tenant` CLI that automates the
      end-to-end provisioning sequence (manifest → cert verify →
      port alloc → state dir → unit + snippet write → first-boot →
      pairing URL).  Until D-O10 lands, the operator runbook
      covers the hand-curated path.

  - id: ticks
    canonical: tick
    aliases:
      - tick
      - WorldTick
      - MeteringTick
      - BCA tick
    short: |
      A discrete time advance. WorldTick (20 Hz region tick) and
      MeteringTick (per-resource-flow advance of an MFP nSequence) are
      different concepts; same word, different domains.
    definition: |
      A *tick* is a discrete time advance — a hash-chain step at some
      scope. The substrate uses several distinct tick kinds:
      **WorldTick** (per-region monotonic counter at ~20 Hz, advancing
      the region's Merkle-rooted state hash), **MeteringTick**
      (per-resource-flow advance of an MFP channel's `nSequence`), and
      occasional ad hoc per-domain ticks. The unqualified word "tick"
      should not be used in any artifact without disambiguation.
    sources:
      - "docs/prd/WORLD-PROTOCOL.md (WorldTick)"
      - "Plexus Tech §14 (MeteringTick)"
    notes: |
      "Tick" canonical for the umbrella concept. Specific kinds
      (WorldTick, MeteringTick) must be named whenever a particular
      flavour is meant. The textbook's glossary chapter must
      disambiguate these on first introduction.

  - id: trust-domain
    canonical: governance domain
    aliases:
      - governance domain
      - trust domain
    short: |
      The umbrella concept for a sovereign scope under which
      capabilities are minted, lexicons are authoritative, and trust
      class is asserted. Five named *kinds* of governance domain are
      modelled in SEMANTIC-IR-ARCHITECTURE.md §10 — trust, estate,
      realm, corporate, cooperative — but those are kinds, not
      aliases of the umbrella concept.
    definition: |
      A *governance domain* is a sovereign scope under which
      capabilities are minted, lexicons are authoritative, hat
      identities sign, and trust class is asserted. SEMANTIC-IR-
      ARCHITECTURE.md §10 enumerates five kinds — *trust*, *estate*,
      *realm*, *corporate*, *cooperative* — modelled as distinct
      shapes of governance domain rather than as aliases of the
      umbrella concept.
    sources:
      - "docs/SEMANTIC-IR-ARCHITECTURE.md §10"
    notes: |
      "Governance domain" canonical (more precise than "trust domain"
      — `trust` is also the name of one of the five *kinds* of
      governance domain, so using "trust domain" as the umbrella is
      ambiguous). Trust domain is acceptable as a synonym in casual
      prose but should not be used when the umbrella vs. the
      *trust*-kind distinction matters. The earlier glossary listed
      "estate", "realm", "corporate", "cooperative" as aliases —
      those are removed because they are distinct concepts (kinds
      *of* governance domain), not synonyms.

  - id: verifier-sidecar
    canonical: Verifier Sidecar
    aliases:
      - Verifier Sidecar
      - verifier sidecar
      - VerifierStub
    short: |
      Middleware in the Plexus Control Plane API gateway / per-surface
      runtime that intercepts every request, verifies BRC-100 signatures
      + BRC-52 cert authenticity + identity binding + capability UTXO
      validity via SPV. Phase 0.5 / D-V1 in the unification roadmap.
    definition: |
      The *Verifier Sidecar* is the middleware component (per-surface
      in-process, per-node sidecar process, or edge gateway, per the
      D-V2 deployment topology decision) that intercepts every request
      crossing an adapter boundary and verifies the BRC-100 signature,
      the BRC-52 cert authenticity, the identity binding (signing key
      matches `certificate.subject`), and the capability UTXO state
      via SPV. Phase 0.5 / D-V1 in the unification roadmap; it is
      load-bearing for axes A (Identity), C (Transport), and D-cap
      (Capability) simultaneously.
    sources:
      - "Plexus Tech §8"
      - "docs/prd/SEMANTOS-UNIFICATION-ROADMAP.md §5"
    notes: |
      "Verifier Sidecar" (proper noun, two capitals) canonical for the
      component. "verifier sidecar" (lowercase) is acceptable in
      casual prose. `VerifierStub` is the reference-implementation
      class name and refers to the test stub specifically.

  - id: vfs

  - id: world-host
    canonical: World Host
    aliases:
      - World Host
      - world-host
      - world server
    short: |
      The OTP/Elixir authoritative-region runtime. Per
      WORLD-PROTOCOL.md, "Ready Player One"-class persistent 3D shared
      space implementable as a finite delta on the substructural cell
      engine + OTP region servers + client-side WASM prediction.
    definition: |
      *World Host* is the OTP/Elixir authoritative-region runtime
      adapter that hosts persistent shared 3D spaces. Per
      WORLD-PROTOCOL.md, a "Ready Player One"-class persistent space
      is implementable as a finite delta on the substructural cell
      engine plus OTP region servers plus client-side WASM
      prediction. A1 in the unification matrix; the OTP supervision
      tree is the authority surface, with one region per supervisor
      and approximately 10³–10⁴ entities per region.
    sources:
      - apps/world-host/
      - "docs/prd/WORLD-PROTOCOL.md"
    notes: |
      "World Host" (proper noun, space) canonical for the component.
      `world-host` is the package-and-directory name and is what
      appears in code paths. "World server" is generic and ambiguous
      with non-OTP world runtimes; avoid.

  - id: oddjobz-conversation-state-manager
    canonical: oddjobz.conversation_state_manager
    aliases:
      - conversation state manager
      - conversation cascade
    short: |
      The §O7 ported cascade picking the next conversation action
      from the accumulated job state. Hint to the LLM, not a kernel
      gate — the Job FSM remains the source of truth.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.conversation_state_manager* is the operator-tuned
      cascade ported from `oddjobtodd/src/lib/domain/workflow/
      conversationStateManager.ts` under the D-O7 salvage. It reads
      an `AccumulatedJobState` and emits a discriminated `Conversa-
      tionAction` (`continue` | `present_estimate` | `ask_contact` |
      `offer_free_quote_visit` | `summarise_and_close` |
      `needs_more_info` | `not_worth_pursuing` | `needs_site_visit`).
      Operator-tuned thresholds (decisionReadiness ≥ 70 to close,
      estimateReadiness ≥ 50 to present, scopeClarity ≥ 35 to force
      a borderline present, worthiness ≥ 35 + fit ≥ 25 for the free-
      quote-visit pivot) port verbatim. The cascade is HINT-only
      relative to D-O4's Job FSM: the FSM is the source of truth for
      "what's the next valid transition"; this module picks the
      heuristic to inject into the LLM prompt. See D-O7-OJT-SALVAGE-
      REPORT.md Finding 3.
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/conversation/state-manager.ts
      - "docs/design/D-O7-OJT-SALVAGE-REPORT.md"
    notes: |
      The `present_estimate` action emits an `EstimatorRequest` —
      the OJT inlining of `effortBandService` + `estimateService` is
      out of scope for D-O7. The caller resolves the request against
      whatever estimator service it carries.

  - id: oddjobz-hat-scoped-patches
    canonical: oddjobz.hat_scoping
    aliases:
      - oddjobz hat scoping
      - hat-scoped cap presentation
    short: |
      §O7 cryptographic hat isolation — replaces OJT's filter-based
      scoping. ContextTag threaded into cap-mint; presenter pubkey
      enforced at the kernel gate. Per K3.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.hat_scoping* is the D-O7 ported module that replaces
      OJT's `buildOjtHat()` stub (which had `capabilities: []` and
      `domainFlag: 0` hard-coded — see Finding 1). The K3 fix:
      every hat carries a uint8 `contextTag` that is threaded
      through to `mintCapabilityCell(cap, contextTag, ownerId)`.
      A presenter's BKDS-derived child key satisfies the cap's
      cryptographic spend gate IFF the contextTag matches the
      mint contextTag — proven by `oddjobz_cap_isolation_cryptogra-
      phic` in `proofs/lean/Semantos/Capabilities/Oddjobz.lean`
      line 283 (PR #279). The TS-layer `assertHatScopedCap()`
      predicate surfaces the same gate at the application seam so
      the conversation state-manager can reject a wrong-hat
      presentation before the bytes ever hit the kernel. Application-
      layer filtering is no longer the gate; the hat IS the gate.
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/conversation/hat-scoping.ts
      - "proofs/lean/Semantos/Capabilities/Oddjobz.lean line 283"
      - "docs/design/D-O7-OJT-SALVAGE-REPORT.md Finding 1"
    notes: |
      Default contextTag assignments: 0x00 = legacy single-hat
      operator, 0x01 = carpenter (per BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md
      §2.5), 0x02 = musician. Operators add new hats by picking new
      contextTag bytes; values 0x03–0xFF are unallocated.

  - id: oddjobz-system-prompt
    canonical: oddjobz.system_prompt
    aliases:
      - oddjobz system prompt
      - chat persona prompt
    short: |
      §O7 ported chat persona prompt; hat-keyed (carpenter | musician
      | …). Operator-tuned over ~6 months of OJT — preserved verbatim.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.system_prompt* is the operator persona prompt ported
      from `oddjobtodd/src/lib/ai/prompts/systemPrompt.ts` under the
      D-O7 salvage. The OJT version was implicitly single-hat (Todd's
      handyman business). The D-O7 port parameterises by `hatId` so
      a second hat can plug in a different persona at chat time. The
      hat selection is downstream of the K3 isolation check — the
      cap-presenter pubkey identifies which hat is authoring, the
      prompt-builder reads the hat tag and picks the persona. Body
      content (the ROM-not-quote framing, TONE RULES, NEVER block,
      PRICING DISCIPLINE, HANDLING ESTIMATE PUSHBACK, photos
      guidance) is reproduced VERBATIM — every word the operator
      tuned is preserved.
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/prompts/system-prompt.ts
    notes: |
      Built-in personas: `CARPENTER_PERSONA` (operatorName "Todd",
      service area Sunshine Coast) and `MUSICIAN_PERSONA`
      (placeholder for the §2.5 motivating example). Operators add
      new personas by extending the `PERSONAS` map.

  - id: oddjobz-extraction-prompt
    canonical: oddjobz.extraction_prompt
    aliases:
      - oddjobz extraction prompt
      - structured-data extraction prompt
    short: |
      §O7 ported extraction prompt; verbatim from OJT minus the OJT-
      internal lexicon registry dependency. TAGGED FACTS section is
      parameterised.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.extraction_prompt* is the structured-extraction prompt
      ported from `oddjobtodd/src/lib/ai/prompts/extractionPrompt.ts`
      under the D-O7 salvage. The 9 EXTRACTION RULES (job type
      mapping, urgency mapping, estimate-reaction mapping, customer-
      tone mapping, cheapest-mindset signals, conversation-phase
      mapping, missing-info, suburb hints, jobPivot HARD RULES) port
      verbatim. The TAGGED FACTS section depended on OJT's
      `@/lib/lexicons` registry which doesn't exist in semantos-core;
      we ship a trades-job-types-only default and parameterise via
      `taggedFactsSection` so a richer caller can supply more.
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/prompts/extraction-prompt.ts
    notes: |
      The local `JOB_TYPE_VALUES` constant declares the OJT
      taxonomy (carpentry | plumbing | electrical | painting |
      general | fencing | tiling | roofing | doors_windows |
      gardening | cleaning | other). NOT the same as semantos-core's
      `TradesLexicon` (which carries §O4 transition categories: lead
      | estimate | quote | dispatch | visit | invoice | settle |
      message). The two classifications are complementary.

  - id: re-desk-stub-extension
    canonical: re-desk-stub extension
    aliases:
      - re-desk-stub
      - "@semantos/re-desk-stub"
    short: |
      D-O11 phase O11a stub property-management vertical extension.
      Single MaintenanceRequest cell type, single cap, single FSM —
      minimal scaffolding sufficient to validate the chapter-29
      federation primitive end-to-end with the full @semantos/oddjobz
      extension on the receiving side.
    definition: |
      *re-desk-stub* is the property-management-side counterpart to
      `@semantos/oddjobz` for the cross-vertical dispatch envelope
      smoke test. It ships exactly one cell type
      (`re-desk.maintenance-request.v1`, LINEAR), one capability
      (`cap.re-desk.dispatch` at domain flag 0x00010201, gating
      `draft → dispatched`), and one FSM
      (`draft → dispatched → accepted → in_progress → completed →
      invoiced → closed`, plus cancellation paths from
      `dispatched`/`accepted`). The kernel-gate machinery (K1/K2/K4)
      is the same shape as `@semantos/oddjobz`'s `state-machines/
      kernel-gate.ts`, parameterised on this extension's cap
      registry. The intent is structural — to prove the chapter-29
      dispatch envelope composes with two independent extensions —
      not to ship a real PM vertical (a real `re-desk` extension is
      downstream work under the SHOMEE/RE platform).
    sources:
      - extensions/re-desk-stub/
      - "docs/design/ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §3 phase O11"
      - "docs/textbook/29-cross-vertical-dispatch-and-federation.md"
    notes: |
      Domain-flag namespace: claims canonical low-bits page
      0x000102xx (one page above oddjobz at 0x000101xx). The
      `cap.re-desk.dispatch` mints at 0x00010201. The page-aligned
      scheme is documented in `extensions/oddjobz/src/capabilities.ts`
      module head — every shipping extension claims one page so
      audit log diffs across deployments are byte-identical. Adding
      a second canonical extension (e.g. an accounting verticals
      stub) would claim 0x000103xx.

  - id: dispatch-envelope-cell-type
    canonical: dispatch.envelope.v1
    aliases:
      - dispatch.envelope.v1
      - dispatch envelope cell type
    short: |
      D-O11 phase O11b LINEAR cell carrying a payload from one
      vertical extension's hat to another tenant's hat. The bridge
      primitive's wire shape — see chapter 29.
    definition: |
      *dispatch.envelope.v1* is the LINEAR cell type that carries a
      cross-vertical dispatch envelope across the federation seam.
      Fields: `envelopeId` (UUID v4), `fromTenant` + `fromHat`
      (originating tenant-hat reference), `toTenant` + `toHat`
      (receiving tenant-hat reference), `payloadType` (canonical
      name of the inner cell, e.g. `re-desk.maintenance-request.v1`),
      `payload` (lower-case hex of the canonical-encoded inner cell
      bytes), `signedBy` (cert chain of the originating hat),
      `createdAt` (ISO-8601). Linearity is LINEAR per chapter 29
      §"Linearity of the envelope itself" — must be consumed at
      least once on the receiving side; an unaccepted envelope is a
      kernel-invariant violation, not a missed delivery.
    sources:
      - extensions/dispatch/src/cell-types/envelope.ts
      - "docs/textbook/29-cross-vertical-dispatch-and-federation.md"
      - "docs/design/ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §3 phase O11b"
    notes: |
      Companion cell types: `dispatch.accepted.v1` (the receive-
      side ack patch) and `dispatch.completion.v1` (the completion
      + billing patch). Together they compose the full envelope
      lifecycle. The dispatch-envelope conceptual entry is at
      `glossary.yml#dispatch-envelope` (the architectural concept);
      this entry is the on-wire cell-type spec.

  - id: cross-vertical-dispatch
    canonical: cross-vertical dispatch
    aliases:
      - cross-vertical dispatch
      - cross-vertical federation
    short: |
      The federation primitive: two independent vertical extensions
      (e.g. property-management + trades) exchange semantic objects
      via a shared dispatch envelope, without point-to-point
      integration or shared schema. Subject of textbook chapter 29.
    definition: |
      *Cross-vertical dispatch* is the architectural pattern by
      which two independent Semantos verticals — different object
      type registries, different policy trees, different governance
      domains — exchange semantic objects without collapsing into
      point-to-point integration or central-broker mediation. The
      mechanism: each vertical's state machine writes RELEVANT
      patches on a shared `dispatch.envelope.v1` cell; the policy
      evaluator at each end filters per-hat AFFINE patches to that
      hat's contextTag. The session-protocol skeleton from Phase 35A
      provides the transport substrate (`SignedBundle` mesh wire in
      production; in-process `BundleTransport` in test). The
      dispatch handler at `extensions/dispatch/` is the universal
      bridge primitive — payload-type-keyed routing — so adding a
      new vertical does not require modifying the bridge.
    sources:
      - "docs/textbook/29-cross-vertical-dispatch-and-federation.md"
      - extensions/dispatch/
      - "docs/design/ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §3 phase O11"
    notes: |
      First end-to-end smoke test ships in D-O11 (this PR), pairing
      `@semantos/re-desk-stub` (PM side) with `@semantos/oddjobz`
      (trades side). The K3 hat-isolation property generalises
      from the BRAIN-DISPATCHER-UNIFICATION.md §2.5 carpenter+
      musician case to the cross-vertical PM/tradie case: every
      AFFINE patch is hat-keyed via BKDS-derived child key; readers
      under a different contextTag cannot decrypt.

  - id: tenant-hat-reference
    canonical: tenant-hat reference
    aliases:
      - tenant-hat ref
      - "<tenant-domain>#<hat-id>"
    short: |
      Operator-readable address syntax `<tenant-domain>#<hat-id>` for
      a hat within a specific brain (e.g. `oddjobtodd.info#tradie-
      todd`). Used as the `dispatch_to` target on a re-desk
      MaintenanceRequest and as the `toTenant` + `toHat` pair on a
      dispatch envelope.
    definition: |
      A *tenant-hat reference* is a string of the form
      `<tenant-domain>#<hat-id>` identifying a single hat within a
      single tenant brain. The substring before the `#` is the
      receiving brain's brain-routable domain (the hostname whose
      `/api/v1/bundle` SignedBundle endpoint receives federated
      bundles); the substring after is the hat-id within that
      tenant whose contextTag the envelope's accept-handler keys
      against. Domains are `[a-z0-9.-]+`; hat-ids are `[a-z0-9-]+`;
      a single `#` separates them, so the parse is unambiguous.
      Introduced in D-O11 phase O11a.
    sources:
      - extensions/re-desk-stub/src/tenant-hat-ref.ts
      - "docs/design/ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §3 phase O11"
    notes: |
      The two-substring shape is operator-readable (a PM operator
      can type `oddjobtodd.info#tradie-todd` into a UI without
      escaping) and unambiguous-to-parse (one delimiter, one split,
      lowercase forced for both halves). Future revisions may add
      delimiters (`?` for query params, `@` for revision pinning)
      without reshaping the canonical form.

  - id: oddjobz-mobile-shell
    canonical: oddjobz-mobile-shell
    aliases:
      - oddjobz-mobile-shell
      - oddjobz-mobile
      - mobile shell
    short: |
      Flutter app at `apps/oddjobz-mobile/` that runs the operator's
      helm UI on a phone. Pairs into the operator's brain via the
      D-O5p QR-pairing flow and consumes the same bearer-gated
      `POST /api/v1/repl` endpoint the desktop helm SPA
      (`apps/loom-svelte`) does. Introduced by D-O5m.
    definition: |
      The *oddjobz-mobile-shell* is the device-side production
      binary for D-O5m: a Flutter mobile app composed on top of
      `platforms/flutter/semantos_ffi` that scans the QR emitted by
      `brain device pair`, runs the BRC-42 child derivation in pure
      Dart (via pointycastle), POSTs the claim payload to the
      brain's `/api/v1/device-pair` endpoint, persists the resulting
      child cert + bearer in `flutter_secure_storage`, and surfaces
      a helm UI that proxies operator REPL lines through
      `POST /api/v1/repl`. The MVP slice ships pairing + a read-only
      JobList/JobDetail surface + a settings/unpair affordance + an
      sqflite-backed outbox skeleton; voice, sensors, push, and
      full mesh sync land in D-O5m follow-ups.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/
      - "docs/design/ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §Phase O5m"
    notes: |
      The shell is a real Semantos peer node by design — not a thin
      client. The MVP is online-mostly (it talks to the brain via
      REPL), but the package layout reserves space for the on-device
      cell engine + voice pipeline + mesh sync that land in later
      D-O5m follow-ups. The ffi seam is wired through
      `platforms/flutter/semantos_ffi` so adding the on-device
      kernel doesn't require restructuring.

  - id: child-cert-custody
    canonical: child-cert-custody
    aliases:
      - child-cert-custody
      - child cert custody
    short: |
      The mobile shell's surface for persisting + retrieving the
      device's BRC-42-derived signing material + brain endpoints +
      bearer token. Production: iOS Keychain / Android Keystore via
      `flutter_secure_storage`. Tests: in-memory `InMemorySecureStore`.
    definition: |
      *Child-cert-custody* is the surface in the oddjobz-mobile-shell
      that owns the persisted state from a successful pairing: the
      device's identity priv (32-byte hex), the BRC-42 child pub
      (audit identifier), the operator's root pub + cert id, the
      pinned brain HTTPS + WSS endpoints, the capability allowlist,
      the per-device contextTag, the operator-supplied label, and
      the bearer token issued by the brain. The implementation in
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/identity/child_cert_store.dart`
      is keyed by the namespaced `d-o5m.v1.*` slot names (versioned
      to allow zero-downtime schema migration on a future rev).
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/identity/child_cert_store.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/identity/flutter_secure_store_adapter.dart
    notes: |
      The MVP stores the device priv as raw 64-hex bytes inside
      `flutter_secure_storage` (which uses iOS Keychain / Android
      Keystore-backed encryption at rest). A future revision
      (D-O5m.followup-2) will replace the raw priv with a
      Keychain/Keystore-backed signing key handle so the priv bytes
      themselves never leave the secure enclave. The `SecureStore`
      abstraction is intentionally Flutter-import-free so the
      pure-Dart unit tests run under `dart test` without a Flutter
      SDK gate.

  - id: pairing-handshake
    canonical: pairing-handshake
    aliases:
      - pairing-handshake
      - pairing handshake
      - device-pair handshake
    short: |
      End-to-end protocol the mobile shell runs to pair into an
      operator brain: decode the `brain-device-pair-v2` QR payload,
      run the BRC-42 child derivation, POST the claim to
      `/api/v1/device-pair`, persist the response. Introduced by
      D-O5p (brain side) + D-O5m (device side).
    definition: |
      The *pairing-handshake* is the device-side half of the
      D-O5p / D-O5m flow. Sequence:
      (1) the operator runs `brain device pair` to generate a v2
      base64url-encoded JSON payload signed by the operator's root
      priv, rendered as a QR + URL fallback;
      (2) the mobile shell decodes the payload, generates a fresh
      device priv via OS CSPRNG, runs the BRC-42 child derivation
      `child_pub = h*G + operator_root_pub` (where
      `h = HMAC-SHA-256(ECDH(devicePriv,operatorRootPub).compressedSec1, invoice)`
      and the invoice is `"BKDS-BRC42-v1" || u8(contextTag) || u32_be(label.len) || label`);
      (3) the device POSTs `{token, derivation_pubkey, derivation_proof}`
      to the brain's `/api/v1/device-pair`;
      (4) the brain re-derives the child pub via the symmetric path
      (`operator_root_priv * device_pub`), asserts equality, and on
      match registers the child cert + capabilities in the identity
      DAG and returns a 64-hex bearer token;
      (5) the device persists the full record via child-cert-custody.
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/device-pair-client.ts
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/pairing/
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/device_pair.zig
    notes: |
      The Dart implementation is a byte-for-byte port of the TS
      reference at `extensions/oddjobz/src/device-pair-client.ts`.
      Cross-language parity is asserted by the test at
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/pairing/brc42_derive_test.dart`
      against the canonical fixture in
      `extensions/oddjobz/tests/vectors/device-pair/v2-fixture.json`.
      If the parity test fails the port is wrong — fix the port,
      do not dilute the test.

  - id: helm-repl-mobile
    canonical: helm-repl-mobile
    aliases:
      - helm-repl-mobile
      - mobile helm REPL
    short: |
      Bearer-gated `POST /api/v1/repl` client surface in the mobile
      shell, mirroring `apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts`.
      Source of REPL responses for the mobile JobList /
      JobDetail / Settings screens.
    definition: |
      *Helm-repl-mobile* is the device-side REPL HTTP client at
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/repl/repl_client.dart`. It
      mirrors the desktop helm SPA's `ReplClient`
      (`apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts`) field-for-field
      but sources the bearer token from `child-cert-custody` instead
      of `localStorage`. The wire shape is identical
      (`POST /api/v1/repl` with `Authorization: Bearer <hex64>` and
      `{"cmd": "<repl-line>"}` body); the response shape is
      `{result, exit}` on 200 and `{error}` on 400/401/503, mapped
      to typed Dart exceptions (`ReplValidationError`,
      `ReplUnauthorisedError`, `ReplBackendUnavailable`,
      `ReplError`). The mobile shell uses helm-repl-mobile both for
      direct view queries (e.g. `find jobs`) and as the flush
      transport for the outbox-queue skeleton.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/repl/
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts
    notes: |
      Mirrors the D-O5.followup-1 best-effort text-parsing posture
      of the desktop helm: the Semantos Brain REPL today returns free-form
      text rather than typed JSON for `find jobs` and friends, so
      `JobsRepository.parseJobs` falls back through JSON to TSV to
      empty just like the Svelte view does. The first time a
      structured response is needed we'll add a typed dispatcher
      resource (D-O5m.followup-4) and surface it as a typed method.

  - id: outbox-queue
    canonical: outbox-queue
    aliases:
      - outbox-queue
      - outbox queue
    short: |
      sqflite-backed FIFO queue in the mobile shell that buffers
      cell transitions signed while offline; flushed through
      helm-repl-mobile on reconnect. D-O5m-i skeleton; full K1
      conflict resolution surface deferred to D-O5m.followup-5.
    definition: |
      The *outbox-queue* is the mobile shell's persistence layer for
      the offline-to-online state transition. While the device is
      offline the operator can sign cell transitions locally; each
      transition lands in the `outbox_v1` SQLite table
      (`apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/outbox_db.dart`).  On
      reconnect the `OutboxService` walks the FIFO and pushes each
      entry through helm-repl-mobile; successful flushes are
      dequeued, validation failures are recorded with an
      `attempt_count` + `last_error` for the operator to triage,
      and a 401 from the brain halts the flush + signals
      `unauthorised=true` so the helm transitions to the pairing
      screen.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/outbox_db.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/outbox_service.dart
      - "docs/design/ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §Phase O5m-i"
    notes: |
      The MVP stores cell payloads as JSON strings — production-
      shape signed BSV bytes land alongside the on-device cell
      engine in D-O5m.followup-1. The full K1 conflict resolution
      UI ("this didn't apply because state changed — here's the
      current state") is D-O5m.followup-5; for now a 400 from the
      brain leaves the entry queued with `last_error` set and the
      operator can dismiss it from the helm settings screen.

  - id: outbox-failure-model
    canonical: outbox-failure-model
    aliases:
      - outbox-failure-model
      - OutboxFailureKind
    short: |
      Typed failure-record schema on every outbox-queue row that
      maps the brain's typed error JSON bodies to operator-actionable
      kinds (network_error / hash_mismatch / signature_invalid /
      cert_unknown / visit_not_found / state_moved_on / replay /
      validation_failed / unauthorised). Powers k1-conflict-ui.
    definition: |
      The *outbox-failure-model* extends the `outbox_v1` schema
      (`apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/outbox_db.dart`) with
      five typed failure columns: `failure_reason` (one of nine
      `OutboxFailureKind` wire strings), `failure_message` (optional
      human-readable detail from the brain), `failure_at_ms`,
      `failure_count` (incremented per attempt), and
      `last_brain_state` (for state-moved-on-conflict rows). The
      flush handler in `OutboxService.flush` parses the brain's typed
      error JSON body via `parseBrainError` + `extractBrainState` and
      records the typed failure via `recordTypedFailure`. The
      `OutboxFailedEntry` projection + the broadcast
      `OutboxService.failedEntries` stream surface the failed-entry
      set to the conflicts surface.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/outbox_db.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/outbox_service.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/failure_messages.dart
    notes: |
      Landed in D-O5m.followup-5 alongside k1-conflict-ui. The
      mapping table in `parseBrainError` reflects the brain's typed
      error vocabulary surfaced in
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachments_upload_http.zig` + the cell-type
      dispatch handlers; extend in lockstep when the brain grows
      new typed kinds. Operator-facing English strings live in
      `failure_messages.dart::readableMessage` so the conflicts
      screen + AppBar tooltip stay consistent.

  - id: k1-conflict-ui
    canonical: k1-conflict-ui
    aliases:
      - k1-conflict-ui
      - K1 conflict surface
    short: |
      Operator-facing surface in the mobile helm that turns the
      outbox-queue from a silent mechanism into a transparent
      debuggable artifact. Green/yellow/red AppBar status indicator
      + ConflictsScreen with retry/discard/view-conflict actions
      per failed entry.
    definition: |
      *K1-conflict-ui* is the mobile helm's surface for the
      outbox-failure-model. The AppBar carries a green/yellow/red
      status indicator (`OutboxStatusIndicator` in `home_screen.dart`)
      that shows green when the queue is empty + connected, yellow
      when there are pending entries, and red with a count badge
      when there are failed entries. Tapping the red dot opens
      `ConflictsScreen` (`apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/
      conflicts_screen.dart`), which renders one row per failed
      entry with the operator-facing English message
      (`readableMessage`), the brain's `last_brain_state` summary
      where relevant, and per-row Retry / Discard / View-conflict
      actions. Retry resets the typed-failure metadata via
      `OutboxService.retry`; Discard dequeues the entry via
      `OutboxService.discard`; View-conflict (state_moved_on only)
      opens a side-by-side dialog comparing the operator's offline
      payload to the brain's current state.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/conflicts_screen.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/home_screen.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/helm/conflicts_screen_test.dart
    notes: |
      Landed in D-O5m.followup-5 — closes the offline-path UX story
      from D-O5m-i (skeleton). The red-dot count badge reads from
      `OutboxService.failedEntries` so it updates live as the
      operator drains the queue. The yellow/green distinction reads
      from `OutboxService.pendingCount`. Combined with
      D-O5.followup-4 (live-tick stream) the operator-collaboration
      story is complete: changes propagate live; failures surface
      clearly.

  - id: state-moved-on-conflict
    canonical: state-moved-on-conflict
    aliases:
      - state-moved-on-conflict
      - K1 conflict
      - state_moved_on
    short: |
      The canonical K1 conflict surfaced in the outbox-failure-model:
      operator transitioned a job offline, brain advanced the same
      job through a different path; the offline transition can no
      longer be applied. Surfaced via `lastBrainState` on the failed
      outbox row.
    definition: |
      A *state-moved-on-conflict* is the operator-altitude name for
      the outbox-failure-model kind `state_moved_on`. It fires when
      the FSM the operator's offline change targets has advanced
      past the from-state on the brain side. The brain doesn't emit
      `state_moved_on` verbatim; it emits one of `not_reachable`,
      `wrong_principal`, or `wrong_cap` from
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/jobs_handler.zig`'s typed
      transition body, and `parseBrainError` collapses those to
      `OutboxFailureKind.stateMovedOn` client-side. The brain's
      current canonical state is recorded in `last_brain_state` on
      the outbox row + surfaced in the conflicts screen's "View
      conflict" dialog so the operator can reconcile.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/outbox_service.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/conflicts_screen.dart
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/jobs_handler.zig
    notes: |
      The "K1 conflict" name reflects the kernel-invariant K1
      (linearity) framing: the offline cell consumed the brain-side
      cell's state input, but the brain has since consumed it via a
      different successor. The mobile surface treats this as a
      first-class operator interaction (View conflict button,
      side-by-side reconciliation) rather than a generic validation
      failure, since the operator's mental model needs to update.

  - id: repl-typed-errors
    canonical: repl-typed-errors
    aliases:
      - repl-typed-errors
      - ReplStateMovedOnError
      - ReplFkError
    short: |
      Typed error classes in `apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts`
      that promote the brain's typed error JSON bodies into a
      structured TS surface. Used by list/detail views to render
      inline conflict banners with retry/dismiss actions instead of
      a generic "failed to load" red banner.
    definition: |
      *Repl-typed-errors* are the desktop helm's analogue of the
      mobile outbox-failure-model. The Svelte helm is online-only
      (no offline queue) but it can encounter the same K1-class
      errors in real time when REPL calls fail. The typed error
      classes — `ReplValidationError` (400 typed body),
      `ReplStateMovedOnError` (FSM rejection: `not_reachable` /
      `wrong_principal` / `wrong_cap`), and `ReplFkError`
      (`not_found` / `visit_not_found` / `job_not_found`) — carry
      the parsed brain state + entity id so views can render
      structured UX. The `throwIfTypedConflict` helper dispatches a
      200-shape transition body to the appropriate typed throw, and
      `ReplClient.send` promotes 400 typed bodies automatically.
    sources:
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/views/JobDetail.svelte
      - apps/loom-svelte/tests/repl-error-types.test.ts
    notes: |
      Landed in D-O5m.followup-5 alongside k1-conflict-ui. The
      vocabulary mirrors `OutboxFailureKind` so a future sharable
      "conflict view-model" library can sit between the two helms
      without re-defining the typed surface. `JobDetail.svelte`
      catches the typed errors and renders an inline conflict
      banner with Retry / Dismiss actions; other list/detail views
      adopt the same pattern as they grow K1-conflict-prone
      transitions.

  - id: attachment-cell-type
    canonical: oddjobz.attachment.v1
    aliases:
      - oddjobz.attachment.v1
      - oddjobz Attachment cell
    short: |
      LINEAR cell — metadata for a binary artifact captured at a
      Visit (photo, voice memo, GPS pin, file).  Write-once
      (AFFINE-ish — no FSM transitions); deletion supersedes by
      tombstone successor.  Wire-level LINEAR (code 1).
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.attachment.v1* is the metadata cell for a binary
      artifact captured at a Visit.  Per §O5m it is the substrate
      for the mobile sensor-capture flow: the phone signs the
      metadata cell at capture time using a device child cert, and
      the binary blob is uploaded separately keyed by
      content_hash.  Field shape: attachmentId (UUID), visitId
      (UUID — REQUIRED FK to Visit), kind ∈ photo|voice_memo|
      gps_pin|file_other, contentHash (sha256 hex 64 chars),
      contentSize (bytes ≥ 0), mimeType, capturedAt (ISO-8601),
      capturedByCertId (32 hex chars — 16-byte child cert id),
      caption (optional, ≤ 500 chars), createdAt (server-stamped).
      LINEAR by §O2; AFFINE-ish at the operator-altitude (write-
      once, no FSM, never transitions) — Attachments ride the
      LINEAR wire shape so they sit alongside Visit/Job/Quote/
      Invoice cells without a special case.
    type_hash: c4cf2fd44009863e602a5e69c3021bdb460ee6aa3a803591e3b0c44298fc1c14
    linearity_label: LINEAR
    wire_linearity: 1
    sources:
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/cell-types/attachment.ts
      - extensions/oddjobz/tests/cell-types/attachment.test.ts
      - extensions/oddjobz/tests/vectors/oddjobz_attachment.json
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O5m"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-8 substrate (2026-05-02).  This
      PR ships only the cell-type substrate + read-only handler;
      the producer side (mobile camera capture + binary blob upload
      + cell signing) is the load-bearing operator-visible work in
      the subsequent PR.

  - id: attachment-blob-store
    canonical: attachment blob store
    aliases:
      - attachment blob store
      - BlobStore
      - attachment_blobs_fs
    short: |
      Content-addressable filesystem-backed store for the binary
      blobs (photos, voice memos, GPS pins, file_other) referenced by
      `oddjobz.attachment.v1` metadata cells.  Layout: `<data_dir>/
      oddjobz/blobs/<sha256>.bin`.  Atomic writes via temp-file
      rename.  Hash mismatch on write rejects with the typed
      `BlobError.hash_mismatch`.
    definition: |
      *attachment blob store* is the FS-backed BlobStore at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachment_blobs_fs.zig` keyed by sha256 hex
      (matches `oddjobz.attachment.v1.contentHash`).  Supports
      `init(allocator, data_dir)`, `write(hash_hex, bytes)` (atomic
      rename; rejects with BlobError.hash_mismatch when SHA256(bytes)
      != hash_hex), `read(hash_hex)`, and `exists(hash_hex)`.  No
      compression, no rotation logic — MVP posture; the metadata
      cell holding the hash is the canonical referrer.  The upload
      endpoint hashes the multipart blob bytes against the cell's
      contentHash field BEFORE calling write(); the store's own
      hash check is belt-and-suspenders against future signer drift.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachment_blobs_fs.zig
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O5m"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-8 capture+upload (2026-05-02).  Per-
      blob cap matches the upload endpoint's 10 MiB ceiling
      (DEFAULT_MAX_BLOB_BYTES).  Sits alongside attachments.jsonl in
      `<data_dir>/oddjobz/`.  Log rotation / blob GC for orphaned
      hashes is a known gap shared with the JSONL store family —
      tracked separately under D-O5m.followup-N.

  - id: attachments-blob-endpoint
    canonical: attachments_blob endpoint
    aliases:
      - attachments_blob endpoint
      - GET /api/v1/attachments/<id>/blob
      - blob fetch endpoint
    short: |
      Bearer-gated GET endpoint at `/api/v1/attachments/<id>/blob`
      that streams the binary bytes of an Attachment.  Cap-required
      `cap.oddjobz.read_attachments`.  Returns the bytes with
      `Content-Type: <mime_type>`; 404 on unknown id or missing blob.
      Both helms render photo thumbnails inline by fetching this
      endpoint.
    definition: |
      *attachments_blob endpoint* is the bearer-gated GET endpoint at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachments_blob_http.zig`.  Wire shape: GET
      `/api/v1/attachments/<id>/blob` with `Authorization: Bearer
      <hex64>` returns the blob bytes (200 with the metadata cell's
      mime_type as Content-Type, plus an `x-attachment-content-hash`
      response header echoing the sha256 the client can verify
      against the metadata cell).  Errors: 401 on bearer rejection,
      404 on unknown attachment id or missing blob, 405 on non-GET.
      The Svelte helm uses `client.fetchBlob(path)` (a fetch + Blob
      + URL.createObjectURL pattern that survives CORS on
      Authorization-bearing requests) to wire the URL into an `<img>`
      src; the Flutter helm uses `Image.network(..., headers: {auth})`.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachments_blob_http.zig
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/visit_detail_screen.dart
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O5m"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-8 capture+upload (2026-05-02).  The
      endpoint shares the bearer surface with the REPL endpoint —
      same TokenStore, same verifyHex() check.  Cap-gating to
      `cap.oddjobz.read_attachments` is per-cert; today's helm
      bearer is single-session-scoped so the cap check is trivially
      satisfied, and tightens once D-O5p ships per-cert capability
      scoping.

  - id: attachments-upload-endpoint
    canonical: attachments_upload endpoint
    aliases:
      - attachments_upload endpoint
      - POST /api/v1/attachments/upload
      - multipart upload endpoint
    short: |
      Multipart `POST /api/v1/attachments/upload` endpoint that
      receives a signed `oddjobz.attachment.v1` metadata cell + its
      binary blob, hashes the blob, looks up the device child cert,
      verifies the ECDSA signature via the recovery-loop scheme,
      writes the blob to the `attachment-blob-store`, and persists
      the metadata cell via the `attachments-store`.  Per-blob cap
      is 10 MiB (DEFAULT_MAX_BLOB_BYTES).
    definition: |
      *attachments_upload endpoint* is the multipart POST endpoint at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachments_upload_http.zig`.  Wire shape:
      `multipart/form-data` body with two parts — `metadata` (JSON
      with `cell_payload`, `signature_hex`, `captured_by_cert_id`)
      and `blob` (binary).  Flow: validate bearer, parse multipart,
      reject if blob > 10 MiB (413 too_large), assert SHA-256(blob)
      == cell_payload.contentHash (400 hash_mismatch), look up
      captured_by_cert_id in the CertStore (401 cert_unknown),
      re-canonicalise cell_payload (lexicographic-key JSON) +
      verify signature recovers the cert's pubkey via the same
      recovery-byte loop (31..34) signed_bundle.zig::verifySignature
      uses (401 signature_invalid), write the blob via
      attachment_blobs_fs.write, FK-validate visit_id against the
      visits store (404 visit_not_found), persist the metadata cell.
      Returns `{id, status: "created" | "already_exists"}` on 200;
      idempotent on duplicate id with byte-identical contents.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachments_upload_http.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/attachments_upload_http_conformance.zig
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O5m"
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-8 capture+upload (2026-05-02).  The
      brain re-canonicalises the parsed cell_payload before
      verifying the signature so a malicious sender can't sneak
      whitespace/key-order differences into the signed preimage.
      The wrapper-level captured_by_cert_id MUST equal the cell's
      capturedByCertId (defensive against signing-key mismatch
      attacks).  Cross-language signing parity with the Dart
      producer is asserted by the
      `cell-signing-fixture.json` test pair.

  - id: attachments-store
    canonical: attachments store
    aliases:
      - attachments store
      - AttachmentsStore
      - attachments.jsonl
    short: |
      Append-only JSONL store at `<data_dir>/oddjobz/attachments.jsonl`
      backing the Semantos Brain dispatcher's `find-attachments-resource`.  Mirrors
      the canonical `oddjobz.attachment.v1` cell payload (id, visit_id,
      kind, content_hash, content_size, mime_type, captured_at,
      captured_by_cert_id, caption, created_at).  FK to `visits-store`
      via `visit_id`; FK validation lives at the handler layer (loose
      coupling — the store itself doesn't know about visits).
    definition: |
      *attachments store* is the file-backed ArrayList of
      `Attachment` records the `find_attachments resource` reads
      from.  Implementation at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachments_store_fs.zig`; same JSONL log
      shape as `visits-store` and `customers-store` and
      `jobs-store`.  Idempotent on duplicate id — re-appending a
      created event leaves the in-memory record untouched but logs
      the event for audit.  No `updateState` (Attachments are
      AFFINE-ish — write-once, no FSM transitions; deletion
      supersedes by tombstone successor cell, out of scope for the
      substrate PR).  The store's `findById` / `findByVisitId`
      accessors borrow into the heap-stable per-record OwnedStrings
      backing rather than the single-arena pattern jobs/customers
      use, sidestepping the cross-record dangling-slice hazard
      tracked separately for the older stores.  Not a substitute
      for the cell-DAG — this is a rendered helm view-shape store,
      not the canonical authoritative record (which lives in
      `core/cell-engine`, alongside the binary blob the next PR
      uploads).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/attachments_store_fs.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/src/cell-types/attachment.ts
    notes: |
      Stable as of D-O5m.followup-8 substrate (2026-05-02).  Kind
      validator enumerates the four canonical attachment kinds
      verbatim (photo / voice_memo / gps_pin / file_other).
      Content-hash validator enforces 64-char lowercase hex (sha256);
      captured_by_cert_id validator enforces 32-char lowercase hex
      (16-byte cert id).  Sits alongside jobs.jsonl + customers.jsonl
      + visits.jsonl in `<data_dir>/oddjobz/`.  Log rotation is a
      known gap shared with the rest of the JSONL store family.

      `attachments.find` (optional `visit_id` filter;

      (`cap.oddjobz.write_attachment`; FK-validates `visit_id`
      against the `visits-store` and returns
      `{error: "visit_not_found", visit_id}` on miss; idempotent
      on duplicate id with identical contents, rejects same-id-
      different-contents).  No `transition` cmd — Attachments are
      AFFINE-ish (write-once, no FSM).  The `create_metadata`
      command writes ONLY the metadata cell; the binary blob upload
      is a SEPARATE concern handled in the next PR via a multipart
      HTTP endpoint keyed by content_hash.  Output is canonical

      that gates the Semantos Brain dispatcher's typed attachments read
      commands (per `find-attachments-resource`).  It carries

      time-deterministic per the §O3 scheme).  Held by the

      into.  Read-only by design: the cap permits enumerating
      Attachment metadata cells but does NOT permit creating them
      (those gate on `cap.oddjobz.write_attachment`).

  - id: oddjobz-cell-sign-protocol
    canonical: oddjobz.cell-sign/v1
    aliases:
      - oddjobz.cell-sign/v1
      - cell-sign protocol id
    short: |
      BRC-42 BKDS protocolID for per-cell signing in the oddjobz
      cell-DAG (D-DOG.1.0c Phase 4).  keyID =
      SHA-256(canonical-cell-payload); each cell signed by a
      freshly-derived key that is then discarded.
    definition: |
      *oddjobz.cell-sign/v1* is the BRC-42 protocolID under which
      every oddjobz cell-DAG cell (job.v2, customer.v2, site.v2,
      attachment.v2) is signed.  Derivation pattern:
      `derive(root, "oddjobz.cell-sign/v1", contentHash,
      counterparty) → signingKey`.  The derived public key is
      recorded in the cell's `signedBy` field — this gives the
      unlinkability property (third parties see a unique pubkey per
      cell with no cross-cell correlation possible without the
      root).  Compromise blast radius: single derived key
      compromise affects only one cell; root compromise is total.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/hat_bkds.zig
      - "docs/operator-runbooks/cell-signing-bkds.md"
      - "docs/canon/sovereignty-cell-signing.md"
      - "docs/prd/D-DOG-1.0c-LAYER-1-PROMOTION-MATRIX.md §2"
    notes: |
      Bumping the version (e.g. to /v2) is a coordinated change
      across all live cells — every previously-signed cell stays
      verifiable under v1; new cells under v2 use a new derivation.
      Signed cells under /v1 stay verifiable indefinitely.

  - id: legacy-migrate-to-graph-verb
    canonical: legacy migrate-to-graph
    aliases:
      - legacy migrate-to-graph
      - migrate-to-graph verb
    short: |
      Legacy-CLI verb (D-DOG.1.0c Phase 5 G.1) that walks v1
      flat-shape rows in `~/.semantos/data/oddjobz/jobs.jsonl`,
      matches each to its source proposal via the receipt store's
      cellId index, and re-ratifies through the Phase 2A.4 graph-
      walk handler.  Un-matchable rows flagged in
      legacy-unsigned.jsonl.
    definition: |
      *legacy migrate-to-graph* is the one-shot operator verb that
      promotes pre-Phase-2A.4 v1 oddjobz cells to the post-Phase-3
      cell-DAG graph shape.  For each v1 row in jobs.jsonl: looks up
      the receipt whose `cellId` field matches the v1 UUID, finds
      the source proposal in the proposal store, flips the proposal
      back to `pending`, and re-ratifies through the
      RatificationOrchestrator (which signs via Phase 4's BKDS).
      Rows whose source proposal is no longer in the store are
      flagged into `<brainDataDir>/oddjobz/legacy-unsigned.jsonl` so
      the helm + mobile JobList paint a "legacy" pill on them.  Best-
      effort.  Idempotent — a re-run skips proposals that already
      have graph-shaped receipts.
    sources:
      - runtime/legacy-ingest/src/verb.ts
      - "docs/operator-runbooks/job-graph.md"
      - "docs/prd/D-DOG-1.0c-LAYER-1-PROMOTION-MATRIX.md §4 Phase 5 G.1"
    notes: |
      `--dry-run` reports the migration plan (scanned / migrated /
      flaggedLegacy counts + per-row reasons) without writing the
      marker file or calling the orchestrator.  Per matrix R5 the
      operator's first-dogfood 72 v1 cells may include some without
      proposal-store entries; those stay flat with the legacy badge.

  - id: helm-event-broker
    canonical: HelmEventBroker
    aliases:
      - HelmEventBroker

      - helm event broker
    short: |
      Process-scoped publish/subscribe broker on the Semantos Brain side
      (`runtime/semantos-brain/src/helm_event_broker.zig`) that fans out live
      events from resource handlers (jobs.transition emits
      `job.transitioned`) to every WSS-connected helm subscriber.
    definition: |
      *HelmEventBroker* is the process-scoped publish/subscribe
      kernel of the helm live-tick substrate (D-O5.followup-4) —
      one Broker per `brain repl` / `brain serve` instance, owned by
      `cli.zig` and shared by both `wss_wallet` (subscriber-hub) and
      the resource handlers (event sources).  Operations: `subscribe
      → SubscriberId`, `unsubscribe(id)`, `publish(Event)`.  The
      broker's mutex serialises subscribe/unsubscribe/publish so
      callbacks fire on a stable snapshot of the subscriber list;
      callbacks themselves run synchronously inside the lock and are
      contractually fast (write-queue push; never blocking I/O).
      Every helm-facing handler now emits — the substrate's
      cargo-cult cleanup (feat/d-o5-followup-4-emitters) wired the
      same `broker.publish` shape across all five.  The full event
      catalogue:
        - `job.transitioned` (jobs_handler post jobs.transition)
        - `customer.created` (customers_handler post customers.create)
        - `visit.created` (visits_handler post visits.create)
        - `visit.transitioned` (visits_handler post visits.transition)
        - `quote.created` (quotes_handler post quotes.create)
        - `quote.transitioned` (quotes_handler post quotes.transition)
        - `invoice.created` (invoices_handler post invoices.create)
        - `invoice.transitioned` (invoices_handler post
          invoices.transition)
        - `attachment.created` (attachments_handler post
          attachments.create_metadata; no FSM — affine write-once)
      Each emit is best-effort (the store write already landed; the
      live-event is decorative); each carries the audit pair
      (phase=publish + op="publish" + detail=<event-type>).  Both
      helm clients accept any event type — adding a future event
      source is a single broker.publish call with zero client churn.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/helm_event_broker.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/wss_wallet_conformance.zig
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §O5"
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-4 (2026-05-02; substrate + jobs.
      emitter via #318, every-other-handler emit + topic widening
      via feat/d-o5-followup-4-emitters / #319).  Pairs with
      HelmSubscribeRpc (the wire seam) and the two
      HelmEventStream clients on mobile + svelte.  Client-side
      adoption: every cell-type repository (mobile) and store
      (svelte) now subscribes to the relevant event types and
      re-fetches on emission.  PRs: #318 substrate, #319 brain-side
      fanout, feat/d-o5-followup-4-client-hooks client-side fanout.

  - id: helm-subscribe-rpc
    canonical: helm.subscribe
    aliases:
      - helm.subscribe
      - helm-subscribe-rpc
      - helm subscribe RPC
    short: |
      JSON-RPC method on the Semantos Brain `/api/v1/wallet` WSS endpoint
      (`helm.subscribe` / `helm.unsubscribe`) that registers a
      per-WSS-connection subscriber with the HelmEventBroker.  The
      broker's events are then framed as `helm.event` JSON-RPC
      notifications back to the helm.
    definition: |
      *helm.subscribe* is the wire-level JSON-RPC method (D-O5.
      followup-4) that registers a WSS-connected helm with the
      brain's HelmEventBroker.  Request: `{"jsonrpc":"2.0","id":N,
      "method":"helm.subscribe","params":{"topics":["jobs",...]}}`;
      response: `{result:{subscribed:true, topics:[...]}}`.  Topics
      are validated against a fixed set (jobs / customers / visits
      / quotes / invoices / attachments) and replace any prior
      registration on the connection.  Events from the broker are
      delivered as `helm.event` JSON-RPC notifications: `{jsonrpc:
      "2.0", method:"helm.event", params:{type, data}}`.  Topic
      filtering is enforced inside the per-connection callback —
      `job.transitioned` matches the `jobs` topic via the singular→
      plural map.  The companion `helm.unsubscribe` method clears
      the registration (idempotent).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/wss_wallet.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/wss_wallet_conformance.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-4 (2026-05-02).  Bearer auth piggy-
      backs on the existing /api/v1/wallet upgrade path (Bearer
      header or `?bearer=` query string for browser clients).

  - id: helm-event-stream-mobile
    canonical: HelmEventStream (mobile)
    aliases:

    short: |

      *HelmEventStream (mobile)* is the Dart-side client for the

      `<brainWssEndpoint>/api/v1/wallet`, sends `helm.subscribe`

      incoming `helm.event` JSON-RPC notifications into HelmEvent
      objects on a broadcast Stream, and surfaces lifecycle state
      (`disconnected | connecting | subscribed | reconnecting`) on

      backoff is 1s/2s/4s/8s/16s/30s (capped); `disconnect()` stops
      the loop.  Wired into `JobsRepository` so cache-invalidation
      events trigger a list refresh on `JobListScreen` and the

  - id: repl-transcript-store-svelte
    canonical: REPL transcript store (svelte)
    aliases:
      - repl-transcript-store-svelte
      - svelte transcript store
      - helm REPL transcript ring buffer
    short: |
      Svelte writable ring buffer
      (`apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-transcript-store.ts`) that
      captures every REPL exchange the helm SPA issues — cmd,
      timestamp, latency, status (ok | err | pending), and a
      truncated copy of the result text.  Read by the Transcript
      view.
    definition: |
      *REPL transcript store (svelte)* is the operator-visibility
      seam introduced by D-O5.followup-7.  Every `ReplClient.send`
      call calls `pushPending(cmd)` (returning a monotonic id),
      issues the underlying fetch, then calls `completeEntry(id,
      result, durationMs)` once the response resolves or throws.
      Result kinds: `pending` (in-flight), `ok` (text + bytes +
      truncated flag), `err` (error message + optional statusCode).
      The buffer caps at 200 entries (FIFO drop-oldest); per-entry
      result text caps at 8 KiB via `maybeTruncate`, which marks
      `truncated: true` on overflow.  The store exports a read-only
      `transcript: Readable<ReplTranscriptEntry[]>` plus the seam
      functions `pushPending` / `completeEntry` / `clearTranscript`.
      No persistence — process-local, wiped on SPA reload (the brain's
      audit log is the canonical post-hoc record; this store is
      live-debugging quality-of-life).  Companion view:
      helm-transcript-view.
    sources:
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-transcript-store.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/tests/repl-transcript-store.test.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/tests/repl-client-transcript-integration.test.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-7 (2026-05-02).  The store sits
      entirely under ReplClient — view code never touches it
      directly, so adding a new view doesn't bypass the transcript.
      `MAX_ENTRIES=200` × `MAX_TEXT_BYTES=8192` ≈ 1.6 MiB upper
      bound on retained memory.  Test seam:
      `__resetTranscriptForTests()` zeroes the counter + buffer for
      deterministic id assertions.

  - id: helm-transcript-view
    canonical: helm Transcript view
    aliases:
      - helm-transcript-view
      - Transcript.svelte
      - REPL transcript view
    short: |
      Read-only Svelte view
      (`apps/loom-svelte/src/views/Transcript.svelte`) that renders

    definition: |
      *helm Transcript view* is the operator-facing surface of the
      D-O5.followup-7 transcript subsystem.  Subscribes to the
      `transcript` Svelte readable from
      `lib/repl-transcript-store.ts` and renders entries
      newest-first.  Each entry row shows timestamp (HH:MM:SS), cmd
      (monospace), latency formatted as `<n>ms` / `<n.nn>s`, and a
      status badge: `✓ ok` (green), `✗ err (statusCode?)` (red),
      `⏳ pending` (yellow).  Successful entries expose a
      `<details>` summary that inlines the captured result text
      with a "(truncated)" tag when the result hit the 8 KiB cap.
      Filter dropdown narrows the visible feed by status; Clear
      button drops the entire buffer (Svelte writable seam
      `clearTranscript`).  Visible to all bearers — operator-level
      surface, no role gating.  Empty-state copy guides new
      operators ("Issue a command from another tab to populate
      this feed").

    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-7 (2026-05-02).  Process-local — a
      page reload zeroes the buffer.  No direct unit tests on the
      view (per the deliverable brief; the load-bearing piece is
      the store, which is exercised by the unit + integration test
      suites at tests/repl-transcript-store.test.ts +

  - id: helm-bearer-cookie
    canonical: helm bearer cookie
    aliases:
      - helm-bearer-cookie
      - __semantos_helm_bearer
      - helm bearer cookie
    short: |
      Non-HttpOnly Set-Cookie brain's `/auth/callback` writes alongside
      the HttpOnly session cookie.  Carries the freshly-minted helm
      bearer (64-hex) so the Svelte SPA can read it via
      `document.cookie` on first load and promote it into
      `localStorage["helm.bearer"]`.  Single-use: cleared after read.
    definition: |
      *helm-bearer cookie* is the transport mechanism (D-O5.followup-2)
      for getting a fresh helm bearer from brain's auth-callback into
      the SPA's localStorage on first load — replacing the legacy
      query-string `/helm/?bearer=...` redirect.  Cookie shape:
      `__semantos_helm_bearer=<64-hex>; Path=/; SameSite=Lax;
      Max-Age=<session_ttl>` — explicitly NOT HttpOnly so the SPA's
      `document.cookie` access reads it.  The session cookie that
      lands in the same Set-Cookie batch (`__semantos_session`) IS
      HttpOnly, keeping the session id out of JS reach.  On read,
      `repl-client.ts:getStoredBearer` promotes the value to
      `localStorage["helm.bearer"]` and clears the cookie via
      `Max-Age=0`, so the bearer rides on the wire for exactly one
      request round-trip and never lives in URL history / Referer
      headers.  Backward compat: a `?bearer=...` query param (legacy
      callback path) is still honoured by `captureBearerFromUrl` in
      `auth.ts` — older deploys mid-transition keep working.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/auth_handler.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/site_server.zig
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/auth.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/tests/repl-client-bearer-cookie.test.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-2 (2026-05-02).  Security improvement
      over the MVP redirect: bearers no longer appear in URL history,
      Referer headers, server access logs, or analytics beacons.
      Mobile flow (device-pair) is unchanged — it doesn't go through
      `/auth/callback`.

  - id: auth-callback-dual-cookie
    canonical: auth-callback dual cookie
    aliases:
      - auth-callback-dual-cookie
      - dual-cookie auth callback
      - /auth/callback dual cookie
    short: |
      The shape `/auth/callback` writes after a successful
      identity-cert challenge sign: two Set-Cookie headers (HttpOnly
      `__semantos_session` + non-HttpOnly `__semantos_helm_bearer`)
      followed by a 303 redirect to the original return_to with NO
      bearer in the query string.
    definition: |
      *auth-callback dual cookie* is the response shape brain's
      `/auth/callback` emits after verifying an identity-cert
      challenge signature (D-O5.followup-2).  Three pieces:
      - Set-Cookie 1: `__semantos_session=<id>.<hmac>; HttpOnly;
        Path=/; SameSite=Lax; Max-Age=<ttl>` — the session cookie
        that gates subsequent same-origin requests.  HttpOnly so JS
        can't read the session id.
      - Set-Cookie 2: `__semantos_helm_bearer=<64-hex>; Path=/;
        SameSite=Lax; Max-Age=<ttl>` — the freshly-minted helm
        bearer.  NOT HttpOnly so the Svelte SPA reads it via
        `document.cookie` on first load.  See `helm-bearer-cookie`
        for the SPA-side promotion + clear flow.
      - Status 303 + Location: <return_to> — the original URL the
        operator was trying to reach before hitting the 401 stub.
        No `?bearer=...` in the query string (the bearer rides on
        the cookie instead).
      The bearer is minted via `bearer_tokens.TokenStore.issue` with
      label `helm-cookie` so it's distinguishable from operator-CLI
      bearers in the audit log.  When `bearer_tokens` isn't attached
      (read-only deploys without REPL backend), the second
      Set-Cookie is omitted gracefully — the redirect still works,
      REPL routes 401 in that mode anyway.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/auth_handler.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/site_server.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/auth_handler_conformance.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-2 (2026-05-02).  Replaces the
      pre-followup-2 path that stitched the bearer into the redirect
      URL as `?bearer=...` — fine for MVP but exposed the bearer in
      browser history / Referer headers / server logs.  The
      backward-compat `?bearer=...` capture path in `auth.ts`
      remains during the transition window so older deploys keep
      working.

  - id: voice-shell-pipeline
    canonical: voice-shell pipeline
    aliases:
      - voice-shell-pipeline
      - voice command pipeline
      - voice → STT → brain-extraction
    short: |
      End-to-end mobile pipeline that converts a tradie's spoken
      command into a signed cell: phone records audio → on-device
      whisper.cpp STT → cert-bound signed Transcript → multipart POST
      to /api/v1/voice-extract → brain runs the runtime/intent
      gradient → IntentResult flows back to the helm.
    definition: |
      *voice-shell pipeline* is the D-O5m.followup-3 substrate that
      lets an operator say "job 12345 is invoiced" at a job site and
      have the brain turn it into a signed cell.  Phase 1 keeps the
      compression gradient (L1 SIR → L2 OIR → L3 bytes → L4 2-PDA)
      brain-side; the phone runs only the input modality (record +
      STT) and the cert-bound transcript signing.  Phase 2 will
      port the L1 SIR build on-device via llama.cpp; Phase 3 will
      port the full L2-L4 gradient on-device — at which point the
      phone produces signed cells entirely offline.

      Components:
        - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_command_service.dart
          orchestrates record → transcribe → sign Transcript
        - platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/ FFI plugin runs the STT
          locally without bundling the model in the app binary
        - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_extract_uploader.dart
          POSTs the audio + signed transcript + metadata multipart
        - runtime/semantos-brain/src/voice_extract_http.zig verifies the
          transcript signature and shells into bun
        - extensions/oddjobz/tools/voice-extract.ts is the bun CLI
          that (in Phase 2) wraps runtime/intent/processIntent
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_command_service.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_extract_uploader.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/voice_command_sheet.dart
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/voice_extract_http.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/tools/voice-extract.ts
      - docs/papers/Semantos-A1-Compression-Gradient-DRAFT.md
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 1 (2026-05-02).  Phase 1
      shellout to bun is acceptable per the paper's "structural
      argument" — the gradient does the structural work, the LLM
      only produces a candidate at L1.  Once the gradient is on
      device the shellout disappears.

      cert-binding surface in
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_session_service.dart`.

        - createVoiceSession({certStore, nowMs}) → VoiceSession —
          refuses with MissingCertError if no cert is bound
        - addTranscript({session, text, signer, sequence, nowMs}) →
          Transcript — signs the canonical preimage; refuses with
          VoiceContractError when signer.keyId ≠ session.certId
        - verifyTranscript(transcript, devicePubBytes) → bool —
          re-checks signature against canonical preimage

      The byte-level encoding of `voiceSessionPreimage` and
      `canonicalTranscriptPreimage` mirrors
      `runtime/intent/src/voice/preimage.ts` verbatim; the parity
      proof is the cross-language fixture at

      (TS test generates + asserts; Dart test consumes + asserts
      byte-identical output).  Same load-bearing seam as the
      cell-signing fixture (#316).
