  - id: whisper-ffi-binding
    canonical: whisper.cpp FFI binding
    aliases:
      - whisper-ffi-binding
      - whisper_cpp Flutter plugin
      - on-device STT plugin
    short: |
      Flutter FFI plugin (platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/) wrapping
      whisper.cpp for on-device STT.  whisper.cpp source is fetched
      at plugin build time (NOT vendored) and pinned to a recorded
      upstream commit; the model file is downloaded on first use and
      cached under `getApplicationSupportDirectory()/whisper-models/`
      (NEVER bundled in the app binary).
    definition: |
      *whisper.cpp FFI binding* is the D-O5m.followup-3 mobile-side
      STT primitive.  Plugin layout follows the standard Flutter FFI
      plugin convention (separate ios/, android/, macos/ targets;
      `lib/src/bindings.dart` has the dart:ffi typedefs;
      `lib/src/whisper_service.dart` is the high-level
      `transcribe(audioBytes) → Future<String>` API).  Two
      load-bearing constraints:

        1. whisper.cpp source is fetched at build time —
           CMake's FetchContent on Android, CocoaPods
           `prepare_command` on iOS / macOS — and pinned to the
           upstream tag/commit recorded in `kWhisperCppPin`.  We do
           NOT vendor 30k+ lines of C++ in semantos-core.

        2. The model file (~140 MiB for whisper.base.en) is
           downloaded on first use via `WhisperModelManager`,
           verified by SHA-256, and cached on disk.  We do NOT
           bundle it in the app binary.  The UI surfaces a download
           dialog with `WhisperModelDownloadProgress` callbacks on
           first voice command.

      Default model is `whisper.base.en` — best speed/accuracy
      tradeoff for English-only tradies.  Multilingual models swap
      in via the `WhisperModel` config struct.
    sources:
      - platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/lib/whisper_cpp.dart
      - platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/lib/src/bindings.dart
      - platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/lib/src/model_manager.dart
      - platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/lib/src/whisper_service.dart
      - platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/android/CMakeLists.txt
      - platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/ios/whisper_cpp.podspec
      - platforms/flutter/whisper_cpp/macos/whisper_cpp.podspec
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 1 (2026-05-02).  Lives
      alongside the existing semantos_ffi plugin.  Bumping
      `kWhisperCppPin` requires re-checking that the C ABI
      surface in `bindings.dart` still matches whisper.cpp.

  - id: voice-extract-endpoint
    canonical: /api/v1/voice-extract
    aliases:
      - voice-extract-endpoint
      - voice-extract HTTP endpoint
      - POST /api/v1/voice-extract
    short: |
      Bearer-gated multipart endpoint at runtime/semantos-brain/src/
      voice_extract_http.zig that accepts a signed Transcript +
      audio blob + metadata, verifies the cert binding + transcript
      signature, persists the audio blob, and shells into the bun
      runtime/intent processIntent pipeline.  Returns the
      IntentResult JSON to the caller.
    definition: |
      */api/v1/voice-extract* is the brain-side multipart POST
      endpoint that backs the voice-shell pipeline (D-O5m.followup-3
      Phase 1).  Wire shape mirrors the sibling /api/v1/attachments/
      upload endpoint (multipart with named parts):

        - audio:      raw audio bytes (≤ 5 MiB; 413 otherwise)
        - transcript: JSON-encoded signed Transcript (the Dart
                      VoiceSession produces it; the brain rebuilds
                      the canonical preimage and verifies signature
                      against the cert pubkey via the same
                      recovery-byte loop attachments_upload_http
                      uses)
        - metadata:   JSON {visit_id, hat_context,
                            client_correlation_id}

      Verification uses
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/voice_extract_http.zig::canonicalTranscriptPreimage`
      which is byte-identical to the TS / Dart implementations
      (asserted via the cross-language fixture).  After verification
      the endpoint shells into `extensions/oddjobz/tools/
      voice-extract.ts` (a bun CLI that wraps processIntent in
      Phase 2; Phase 1 returns a placeholder IntentResult that
      surfaces the recognised text + visit binding).

      Typed errors:
        - 401 bearer_invalid       missing/invalid bearer
        - 401 cert_unknown         certId not in CertStore
        - 401 signature_invalid    transcript signature failed
        - 400 payload_invalid_format multipart parse / JSON malformed
        - 413 too_large            audio > 5 MiB
        - 422 pipeline_failed      bun returned non-zero
        - 503 bun_unavailable      bun shellout missing
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/voice_extract_http.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/site_server.zig
      - extensions/oddjobz/tools/voice-extract.ts
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_extract_uploader.dart
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 1 (2026-05-02).  The bun
      shellout is acceptable for Phase 1 per the deliverable's
      phased plan; Phase 3 ports the gradient on-device and the
      shellout disappears.

  - id: llama-ffi-binding
    canonical: llama_cpp Flutter FFI plugin
    aliases:
      - llama.cpp FFI binding
      - llama_cpp plugin
    short: |
      Flutter FFI plugin at platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/ wrapping
      llama.cpp for on-device LLM inference with grammar-constrained
      generation.  Backs the D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 2 on-device L1
      SIR extraction.  Same plugin convention as the whisper_cpp
      sibling: dart:ffi typedefs in lib/src/bindings.dart, high-level
      API in lib/src/llama_service.dart, model-cache lifecycle in
      lib/src/model_manager.dart.  Source NOT vendored (~120k lines
      of C++) -- fetched at build time via CMake FetchContent
      (Android) + CocoaPods prepare_command (iOS / macOS), pinned to
      a recorded commit; the model file (~2 GiB GGUF) NOT bundled --
      downloaded on first use under
      `getApplicationSupportDirectory()/llama-models/`.
    definition: |
      *llama.cpp FFI binding* is the D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 2 on-
      device LLM primitive.  Three load-bearing constraints (mirrors
      the whisper.cpp sibling for consistency):

        1. llama.cpp source is fetched at build time -- CMake's
           FetchContent on Android, CocoaPods `prepare_command` on
           iOS / macOS -- and pinned to the upstream tag/commit
           recorded in `kLlamaCppPin`.  We do NOT vendor 120k+ lines
           of C++ in semantos-core.

        2. The model file (~2.0 GiB for the default Llama-3.2-3B
           Q4_K_M) is downloaded on first use via
           `LlamaModelManager`, verified by SHA-256, and cached on
           disk.  We do NOT bundle it in the app binary.  The UI
           surfaces a download dialog with
           `LlamaModelDownloadProgress` callbacks on first use.

        3. The high-level API exposes
           `LlamaService.complete({prompt, grammarBNF, maxTokens,
           temperature})` -- the `grammarBNF` parameter is the
           load-bearing primitive.  When non-null, llama.cpp's
           sampler filters every emitted token through the GBNF
           automaton; non-matching strings are unsamplable.  This
           is what makes the on-device extractor's output
           structurally valid by construction even with a 3B
           "pleb" model.

      Default model is Llama-3.2-3B-Instruct-Q4_K_M (Llama 3.2
      Community License).  Phi-3.5-mini-instruct is the runner-up;
      swap in via the `LlamaModel` config struct if license terms
      shift.
    sources:
      - platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/lib/llama_cpp.dart
      - platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/lib/src/bindings.dart
      - platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/lib/src/model_manager.dart
      - platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/lib/src/llama_service.dart
      - platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/android/CMakeLists.txt
      - platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/ios/llama_cpp.podspec
      - platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/macos/llama_cpp.podspec
      - platforms/flutter/llama_cpp/ios/Sources/llama_cpp_shim.cpp
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 2.  Lives alongside the
      whisper_cpp plugin from Phase 1.  Bumping `kLlamaCppPin`
      requires re-checking that the C ABI surface in `bindings.dart`
      still matches llama.cpp's evolving C++ API (the shim re-
      exports a stable subset).

  - id: sir-extractor-mobile
    canonical: SirExtractor (Dart, on-device)
    aliases:
      - on-device SIR extractor
      - mobile L1 SIR producer
    short: |
      Dart class at apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/
      sir_extractor.dart that produces an Intent on-device by
      running llama.cpp's grammar-constrained completion against
      the operator's transcript.  The output is a structurally-
      valid Intent (the GBNF grammar guarantees it) plus a host-
      computed confidence score; the brain skips L0->L1 when the
      candidate ships in the multipart `sir_candidate` part.
      Refused candidates fall through to the Phase 1 brain-side
      path -- never breaks the voice flow.
    definition: |
      *On-device SIR extractor* is the D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 2
      operationalisation of the paper's "we can use a more pleb
      model because the gradient does the structural work" claim.
      A 3B Q4-quantized model on the phone produces L1 SIR
      candidates; the brain validates them at L1 (lowerSIR's
      trust-tier + identity-cap checks) and runs L2-L4.

      The extractor is `SirExtractor.extract({transcript,
      hatContext, grammar})`.  Flow:

        1. Build a system prompt with the extension's allowed
           action verbs + hat context.
        2. Call `LlmCompleter.complete(prompt, grammarBNF: kIntent
           Grammar)` -- the grammar enforces structural validity
           on every emitted token.
        3. Parse the resulting JSON; defence-in-depth shape check
           (the grammar should make this redundant but a degenerate
           grammar bug would slip through otherwise).
        4. Compute host-side confidence via
           `computeHostConfidence` -- mirrors the brain's
           `sir-builder.ts::candidateTrustClass` logic (required-
           fields ratio + action-verb match + constraint validity).
           ≥0.9 -> interpretive trust; 0.6-0.9 -> cosmetic;
           <0.6 -> refuse here so the brain doesn't see noisy
           candidates.

      Returns a typed `SirExtractionResult` with two branches --
      `success(intent, confidence)` and `refused(reason)`.  The
      voice command service surfaces the result on
      `VoiceCommandRecording.sirExtractionResult`; the uploader
      sends it as the `sir_candidate` multipart part when present.

      Cross-language byte parity is asserted by the
      `sir-roundtrip-fixture.json` fixture and the matching
      Dart + TS tests -- the Dart-canonicalised Intent JSON is
      byte-identical to what the TS reference encoder produces.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/sir_extractor.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_command_service.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_extract_uploader.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/fixtures/sir-roundtrip-fixture.json
      - runtime/intent/scripts/gen-sir-roundtrip-fixture.ts
      - runtime/intent/src/__tests__/sir-roundtrip-fixture.test.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 2.  The Phase 1 fallback
      path (no `sir_candidate`, brain runs full L0->L4) remains
      active and tested; devices without the llama model continue
      to work unchanged.  Phase 3 ports L2-L4 to Dart, at which
      point the brain shellout disappears.

  - id: gbnf-grammar-bundling
    canonical: intent.gbnf bundled grammar asset
    aliases:
      - GBNF grammar bundling
      - llama grammar asset
    short: |
      The on-device extractor consumes a generated GBNF grammar
      that constrains the LLM's output to a valid Intent JSON.
      The grammar is generated once via
      `runtime/intent/scripts/gen-llama-grammar.ts` from the
      Intent type declaration; the same file is written to two
      locations (the Dart asset bundle + the brain-side validator).
      Single source of truth, two consumers.
    definition: |
      *GBNF grammar bundling* is the D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 2
      mechanism that turns the TS Intent type into a constraint
      llama.cpp can sample under.  The flow:

        1. `bun runtime/intent/scripts/gen-llama-grammar.ts`
           emits `intent.gbnf` to two locations:
             - apps/oddjobz-mobile/assets/llama/intent.gbnf
               (bundled as a Dart asset; loaded by SirExtractor)
             - runtime/intent/assets/intent.gbnf
               (kept for the brain-side validator + audit reference)

        2. The grammar is narrow on purpose -- Phase 2 covers the
           oddjobz `trades` lexicon (8 categories, 7 constraint
           kinds, single target).  Other lexicons are reachable
           via wider grammar branches in Phase 3 once the on-
           device producer copes with a larger vocabulary
           without losing accuracy.

        3. llama.cpp's sampler reads the grammar at completion
           time and filters every candidate token through its
           automaton.  The model literally cannot emit a non-
           matching string -- structural validity is enforced at
           the token level rather than the post-hoc validator
           level.

      The grammar regenerates whenever the Intent type changes
      shape; bumping `runtime/intent/src/types.ts::Intent` is
      paired with re-running the generator (audited like the
      whisper / llama pin bumps).
    sources:
      - runtime/intent/scripts/gen-llama-grammar.ts
      - runtime/intent/assets/intent.gbnf
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/assets/llama/intent.gbnf
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 2.  The grammar's narrow
      scope is intentional -- it's the load-bearing structural
      validator on the on-device path.  Widening it requires
      retraining / re-evaluating the producer model (Phase 3).

  - id: oir-to-bytes-dart-port
    title: OIR -> opcode-bytes Dart emit port
    summary: |
      Verbatim Dart port of `core/semantos-ir/src/emit.ts` that
      walks an `OirProgram`'s bindings and produces the canonical
      opcode byte stream.  Output is byte-identical to the TS
      implementation for any well-formed OIR program -- the
      load-bearing α-equivalence property the paper §3, §4.4
      commits to.  Cross-language parity asserted against
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/fixtures/oir-to-bytes-fixture.json`.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/gradient/oir_to_bytes.dart

      - core/semantos-ir/src/emit.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 3.  The α-equivalence
      property is the central architectural commitment: any OIR
      program that round-trips through canonical JSON encoding
      produces the same opcode bytes regardless of the language
      / compiler / surface grammar that produced it.  Phase 3
      validates the property cross-language between TS and Dart;
      the Lean-extracted reference (proofs/lean/) follows the same
      contract.

  - id: semantos-ffi-execute-script
    title: semantos_execute_script FFI surface
    summary: |
      C ABI export in `src/ffi/exports.zig` that runs an opcode
      byte stream through the **real cell-engine 2-PDA executor**
      (`core/cell-engine/src/executor.zig:execute`) and returns a
      JSON ScriptResult including a typed `errorKind` field
      ("k1_linearity_violation", "k2_auth_failed",
      "k3_domain_mismatch", "k4_atomicity_violation",
      "script_invalid").  Honours the BUFFER_TOO_SMALL retry
      pattern.  Wrapped in a high-level
      `SemantosKernel.executeScript({bytes, ctx})` Dart method
      that produces a sealed [ScriptOutcome] (ScriptOk |
      ScriptViolation) for typed pattern-matching.
    sources:

  - id: on-device-2pda-enforcement
    title: On-device 2-PDA K1-K4 enforcement
    summary: |
      D-O5m.followup-1 — `semantos_execute_script` instantiates the
      real cell-engine 2-PDA executor on the phone (heap-allocated
      PDA + ScriptArena, K1-K4 enforcement turned on) and maps the
      `ExecuteError` enum to a stable `errorKind` taxonomy:
      "k1_linearity_violation" (LINEAR cell duplicated/discarded,
      AFFINE duplicated, RELEVANT discarded),
      "k2_auth_failed" (capability/identity/type-hash mismatch,
      signature invalid),
      "k3_domain_mismatch" (domain flag scope mismatch),
      "k4_atomicity_violation" (verify failed, budget insufficient,
      partial commit aborted),
      "script_invalid" (malformed bytes, unknown opcode, etc.).

      The Dart side surfaces this taxonomy as a sealed
      [ScriptOutcome] type and a [ScriptViolationKind] enum which
      the helm UI switches on to show operator-specific messages
      ("K1 violation: cell already used. Refresh and retry.",
      "K3 violation: hat doesn't have access. Switch to the right
      hat.", etc.).  After this entry, the brain's receipt-side
      enforcement is defence-in-depth, not the canonical authority.
    sources:
      - src/ffi/exports.zig
      - src/ffi/build.zig
      - core/cell-engine/src/executor.zig
      - core/cell-engine/build.zig
      - platforms/flutter/semantos_ffi/lib/src/kernel.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/gradient/dart_pipeline.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/voice_command_sheet.dart
    notes: |
      `core/cell-engine/build.zig:createModules` is now `pub` so
      the FFI build can reach the cell-engine module graph.  The
      FFI inlines its own embedded-profile slice (no BSVZ — host
      callbacks cover crypto on native; std.crypto on the test
      build).  Native dylib + static_lib targets are wired in this
      PR; the wasm32-wasi target keeps the diagnostic-only
      `validateOpcodeStreamSyntactic` walker until the
      wallet-browser host loader provides the cell-engine "host"
      namespace imports.

  - id: voice-shell-fully-on-device
    title: Voice shell pipeline running fully on-device
    summary: |
      The architectural payoff of D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 3: a
      tradie says a sentence at a job site, the phone runs whisper
      (STT) + llama (L0->L1 SIR) + DartIntentPipeline (L1->L2->L3)
      + SemantosKernel.executeScript (L4 via FFI), produces a
      signed cell, and queues it in the existing signed-cell
      outbox path.  When connectivity returns the outbox flushes
      to the brain; until then the operator has a complete signed
      audit trail without any network dependency.  The brain-side
      path from Phases 1 + 2 stays available as a fallback for
      devices that can't load the models (low-end hardware, fresh
      pairings before model download).
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/voice/voice_command_service.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/voice_command_sheet.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/gradient/dart_pipeline.dart
      - docs/papers/Semantos-A1-Compression-Gradient-DRAFT.md
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-3 Phase 3.  The user's framing at
      the start of this voice-shell arc -- "voice to economic
      execution, and because we use the compression gradient, and
      the SIR etc, we should be ok to use more pleb model" --
      is fully delivered by this entry.

  - id: push-token-registration
    title: Push-token registration record
    summary: |
      The four-field substrate carried on each identity-cert record
      that lets the brain target a single device with a push
      notification: `apns_token` (Apple Push Notification service
      device token), `fcm_token` (Firebase Cloud Messaging
      registration token), `push_platform` (discriminator: none |
      apns | fcm — derived from which token field is non-empty), and
      `push_registered_at` (ISO-8601 timestamp the most recent POST
      /api/v1/push-register completed).  Cleared by DELETE
      /api/v1/push-register or by `updatePushToken(.none, "", "")`
      on the cert store.  The mobile shell mirrors the same shape as
      a typed `PushTokenRegistration` model
      (apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/push/push_platform.dart).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/identity_certs.zig
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/push/push_platform.dart
      - "ODDJOBZ-EXTENSION-PLAN.md §D-O5m.followup-9 Phase A"
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase A (substrate scope only:
      schema + register endpoint + event flag, no APNs/FCM
      transports, no Firebase wiring).  Phase B's APNs/FCM
      dispatcher reads these fields off the cert record to decide
      which transport to route a cell payload through.  Phase C's
      mobile PushRegistrationService produces the wire body that
      lands on POST /api/v1/push-register.  Backward-compatible:
      legacy cert records that pre-date the schema bump parse with
      empty token fields and `push_platform = none`.

  - id: push-register-endpoint
    title: POST/DELETE /api/v1/push-register endpoint
    summary: |
      Bearer-gated brain-side endpoint at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/push_register_http.zig` that persists APNs/FCM
      device tokens onto the device's identity-cert record.  POST
      body: `{ "cert_id", "platform": "apns" | "fcm", "token" }`;
      success returns `{ "registered": true, "platform",
      "registered_at" }`.  DELETE body: `{ "cert_id" }`; success
      returns `{ "registered": false }`.  Typed errors:
      `unauthorised` (missing/bad bearer or unknown cert_id),
      `platform_invalid`, `token_empty`, `token_too_large`
      (token > 4 KiB), `payload_invalid_format`.  No actual push
      dispatch happens here — Phase A is substrate only.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/push_register_http.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/push_register_http_test.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/site_server.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase A.  Wired at the same boot
      phase as /api/v1/device-pair / /api/v1/attachments/upload —
      reserved BEFORE site-config route lookup so an operator's
      site.json can't shadow it.  Phase B (next PR) adds the
      brain-side APNs/FCM dispatcher that subscribes to the
      HelmEventBroker, inspects `requires_operator_attention` on
      the Event, and routes a cell payload to the cert's apns_token
      or fcm_token.  Phase C (after that) wires the Flutter
      Firebase plugin + iOS APNs entitlement so the device can
      mint the platform tokens this endpoint persists.

  - id: requires-operator-attention-event-flag
    title: requires_operator_attention flag on HelmEventBroker Event
    summary: |
      A boolean field on the `Event` struct in
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/helm_event_broker.zig` that emit sites set to
      true when the event should bubble up to the operator as a
      push notification.  Default false (background bookkeeping).
      jobs_handler.zig sets it to true on transitions into the
      `lead` state; chat-lead extraction in D-O6b will set it to
      true on `lead.created`.  Phase A only stages the field — the
      Phase B push dispatcher reads it to decide which subscribers
      receive a wire push, and the helm-WSS subscriber bridge can
      optionally tag the JSON-RPC notification frame so the helm UI
      shows a different toast shape.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/helm_event_broker.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/jobs_handler.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase A.  The flag is the
      architectural seam that lets Phase B's APNs/FCM dispatcher
      avoid spamming the operator with every store write — only
      events flagged as needing attention drive a wire push.
      Other emits (customer.created, quote.transitioned, etc.)
      keep the default false and stay decorative live-tile
      updates only.

  - id: apns-dispatcher
    title: APNs dispatcher (brain-side)
    summary: |
      Brain-side HTTP/2 client at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/apns_dispatcher.zig` that POSTs notification
      payloads to api.push.apple.com (or api.development...).  Owns
      the .p8 PKCS#8 P-256 secret key Apple issues, builds the
      ES256 bearer JWT per Apple's spec, caches the JWT for 50min
      (Apple rejects > 1h), and routes the JSON `aps.alert` body
      with the right `apns-topic` / `apns-push-type` / `apns-
      priority` headers.  Token expiry signals (status 410 with
      `reason: Unregistered` or `BadDeviceToken`) clear the cert's
      `apns_token` via `CertStore.updatePushToken(.none, "", iso)`.
      Best-effort: 4xx surfaces `apns_rejected`; 5xx + transport
      errors retried up to 3 attempts; persistent failures land on
      `transport_failed` and the broker logs to audit + carries on.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/apns_dispatcher.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/apns_dispatcher_test.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase B.  The .p8 parser is a
      deliberate byte-search (looks for the canonical
      `04 20 <32 raw bytes>` ECPrivateKey OCTET STRING that Apple
      emits) rather than a full ASN.1 DER walker — robust against
      Apple's exact shape, surfaces a typed `p8_key_parse_failed`
      if Apple ever changes the layout.  HTTP transport is
      injected via the push_http_transport vtable; tests use the
      MockTransport so no live network in CI.

  - id: fcm-dispatcher
    title: FCM dispatcher (brain-side)
    summary: |
      Brain-side HTTPS client at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/fcm_dispatcher.zig` that POSTs FCM v1
      message payloads to fcm.googleapis.com.  Owns the Google
      service-account JSON (client_email + RSA private_key PEM),
      builds an RS256 JWT-bearer assertion, swaps it for an OAuth2
      access_token via oauth2.googleapis.com, and caches the
      access_token for ~55min.  Token-expiry signals (status 404
      with `error.status: UNREGISTERED` or 400 with
      `INVALID_ARGUMENT`) clear the cert's `fcm_token`.  Same best
      -effort retry shape as the APNs dispatcher.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/fcm_dispatcher.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/fcm_dispatcher_test.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase B.  Crypto choice is
      pinned in the source: Zig 0.15.2 stdlib provides RSA verify
      (`std.crypto.Certificate.rsa.PKCS1v1_5Signature.verify`) but
      not RSA sign, so the v0.1 path shells out once per JWT
      regeneration to `openssl dgst -sha256 -sign <pem>`.  The hot
      path caches the OAuth2 access_token, so the openssl invoke
      is at most 1×/hour, not 1× per push.  If a future stdlib
      release ships RSA signing, swapping `Rs256Signer` for the
      stdlib path is a one-function change.  Tests inject
      `fcm_dispatcher.testStubSigner` so the conformance suite
      doesn't spawn openssl.

  - id: push-dispatcher
    title: PushDispatcher (top-level routing)
    summary: |
      Top-level routing layer at
      `runtime/semantos-brain/src/push_dispatcher.zig` that selects between
      APNs and FCM based on `cert.push_platform` for a given cert
      id.  Skips with an audit-log line when the platform is
      `none`, when the relevant dispatcher isn't configured, or
      when sub-dispatcher errors fire.  Exposes `sendToCert(id,
      notification)` and `sendToCerts(ids[], notification)`; the
      latter fans out across a slice of cert ids and absorbs per-
      cert failures so one bad cert doesn't break the rest.

      Sovereign-push D.1 — the PushNotification struct is now
      wake-only: it carries a single `payload_json` field (an
      opaque envelope of `{event_id, ts, kind}`) and no longer has
      `title`, `body`, or `data_json`.  See `wake-only-push` and
      `sovereign-push` for the architectural rationale.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/push_dispatcher.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/push_dispatcher_test.zig
      - docs/operator-runbooks/push-architecture.md
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase B; refactored to wake-only
      under sovereign-push D.1 (PR `sovereign-push-d1-wake-only`).
      The helm_event_broker's PushHook seam wires `sendToCerts` as
      the send-side and a cli-owned `pushBridgeResolve` as the cert-
      id-set producer.  v0.1 resolver returns every cert with a
      registered push token; refinements (per-event-topic
      filtering) land in a follow-up when the broker carries a
      topic field on Event.

  - id: wake-only-push
    title: Wake-only push payload
    summary: |
      Sovereign-push D.1's push wire shape.  Brain → APNs/FCM
      payloads carry ONLY an opaque envelope —
      `{"event_id":"<id>","ts":<unix-seconds>,"kind":"helm.event"}`
      — with no operator-readable text fields.  APNs sees
      `{"aps":{"content-available":1},"event_id":"...","ts":...}`;
      FCM sees a data-only message (no `notification` field) with
      `priority: high`.  The device decodes the envelope on wake
      and fetches the actual event via `helm.fetch_since` over the
      WSS, then renders the notification banner locally from data
      the sovereign brain supplies directly.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/push_dispatcher.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/apns_dispatcher.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/fcm_dispatcher.zig
      - docs/operator-runbooks/push-architecture.md
    notes: |
      Introduced sovereign-push D.1 (PR
      `sovereign-push-d1-wake-only`).  The architectural property:
      Google/Apple stay in the wake-up loop (OS-level requirement)
      but never see operator content.  Phase D.2 (mobile silent
      handler) and D.3 (UnifiedPush adapter) finish the
      device-side half.

  - id: helm-fetch-since-rpc
    title: helm.fetch_since RPC
    summary: |
      JSON-RPC 2.0 method on the WSS wallet endpoint that lets a
      freshly-woken device pull events the brain published while
      it was offline.  Request:
      `{"method":"helm.fetch_since","params":{"since_ts":<i64>,"limit":<u32?>}}`.
      Response:
      `{"result":{"events":[{event_id,ts,kind,payload}, ...],"next_cursor_ts":<i64>}}`.
      The handler reads from the helm_event_broker's bounded
      recent-event ring buffer (capped at MAX_RECENT_EVENTS = 1024
      entries; oldest evicted on overflow).  Server-side `limit`
      cap is MAX_HELM_FETCH_LIMIT = 256.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/wss_wallet.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/helm_event_broker.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/wss_wallet_conformance.zig
      - docs/operator-runbooks/push-architecture.md
    notes: |
      Introduced sovereign-push D.1.  Pairs with wake-only-push:
      device wakes → opens WSS → calls helm.fetch_since → renders
      banners locally.  A device offline longer than the broker's
      ring window misses the older events (acceptable for v0.1 —
      Phase D.2+ may persist to disk).

  - id: apns-jwt-es256
    title: APNs ES256 bearer JWT
    summary: |
      The bearer-authentication JWT Apple's APNs HTTP/2 endpoint
      requires.  Header = `{"alg":"ES256","kid":"<key_id>",
      "typ":"JWT"}`; claims = `{"iss":"<team_id>","iat":<unix_s>}`;
      signature = ECDSA over P-256 (NIST secp256r1, NOT Bitcoin's
      secp256k1) with SHA-256.  Built via
      `apns_dispatcher.buildJwt` using
      `std.crypto.sign.ecdsa.EcdsaP256Sha256` from the Zig stdlib.
      Apple rejects JWTs older than 1 hour; the dispatcher
      regenerates at the 50-minute mark.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/apns_dispatcher.zig
      - "Apple's 'Establishing a Token-Based Connection to APNs'"
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase B.  Curve choice is
      load-bearing: Apple's spec mandates P-256.  bsvz is the
      wrong tool here — bsvz speaks secp256k1 (Bitcoin's curve).
      The two curves share an interface but produce different
      signatures over the same scalar; using bsvz here would
      surface as Apple rejecting every push with a 403.

  - id: fcm-oauth2-rs256
    title: FCM OAuth2 RS256 JWT-bearer assertion
    summary: |
      The JWT-bearer assertion the FCM dispatcher swaps for an
      OAuth2 access_token at oauth2.googleapis.com.  Header =
      `{"alg":"RS256","typ":"JWT"}`; claims = `{"iss":<client_email>,
      "scope":"https://www.googleapis.com/auth/firebase.messaging",
      "aud":"https://oauth2.googleapis.com/token","iat":<now>,
      "exp":<now+3000>}`; signature = RSA-PKCS#1 v1.5 over SHA-256
      of the canonical signing input.  Returned access_token is
      cached ~55 minutes (Google's 60-minute TTL minus a buffer).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/fcm_dispatcher.zig
      - "Google's 'Send messages to specific devices' (FCM HTTP v1)"
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase B.  Zig 0.15.2 stdlib
      doesn't ship RSA signing, so the v0.1 production path uses
      `openssl dgst -sha256 -sign <pem>` over a temp-file PEM
      (mode 0600, deleted via `defer`).  The shellout fires at
      most once per hour because the access_token caches.  If
      Zig stdlib later ships an RSA signer, swapping the
      `rs256_sign_fn` field on FcmDispatcher to the stdlib path
      is a one-line change.

  - id: firebase-messaging-flutter
    title: Firebase Messaging Flutter wiring
    summary: |
      The Flutter side of the push notification pipeline.  Pulls in
      `firebase_core` (the platform bridge), `firebase_messaging`
      (APNs/FCM token capture + delivery callbacks),
      `flutter_local_notifications` (foreground in-app banners
      because both platforms suppress system notifications while
      the app is in the foreground), and `permission_handler` (for
      the Android 13+ POST_NOTIFICATIONS runtime grant + the
      Open-Settings CTA in SettingsScreen).  Production wiring lives
      in `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/main.dart` (Firebase.initializeApp +
      setupPushHandlers run BEFORE runApp() so cold-start taps route
      correctly via getInitialMessage).
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/pubspec.yaml
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/main.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/push/firebase_push_adapter.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/push/push_handlers.dart
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase C.  The Firebase init is
      best-effort: when the placeholder google-services.json /
      GoogleService-Info.plist haven't been swapped for real per-
      tenant values (per docs/operator-runbooks/push-notification-
      setup.md), Firebase.initializeApp logs an error and the app
      still boots with PushRegistrationService set to null —
      SettingsScreen's Notifications card surfaces a "push disabled
      in this build" hint.  The firebase_messaging plugin imports
      are isolated to firebase_push_adapter.dart + push_handlers.dart
      so the unit-test suite (which runs under `dart test`) doesn't
      drag in the Flutter SDK.

  - id: push-registration-service-mobile
    title: PushRegistrationService (mobile shell)
    summary: |
      Owns the device-side push-token lifecycle.  Constructed in
      main.dart with the FirebasePushAdapter and the persisted
      ChildCertStore + SecureStore.  registerOnPair() asks for
      permission, gets the platform device token, POSTs to
      /api/v1/push-register, persists the registration on
      SecureStore (so cold launches don't re-register on every
      boot).  Returns a sealed PushRegistrationResult
      (PushRegistered | PushPermissionDenied | PushUnsupported |
      PushRegistrationFailed) for the helm UI to switch on.
      startTokenRefreshListener wires the firebase_messaging
      onTokenRefresh stream so OS-level token rotations
      (re-installs, cache wipes) update the brain automatically.
      unregister() POSTs DELETE /api/v1/push-register and wipes
      the local persisted record on operator-initiated unsubscribe.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/push/push_registration_service.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/helm/settings_screen.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/push/push_registration_service_test.dart
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase C.  Architecturally
      mirrors the brain-side endpoint at
      runtime/semantos-brain/src/push_register_http.zig.  The
      PushPlatformAdapter abstraction lets tests inject
      InMemoryPushAdapter for hermetic coverage; the production
      FirebasePushAdapter wraps firebase_messaging in a separate
      file so the abstract surface stays Flutter-SDK-free.  The
      service is robust to a stale cert (returns
      PushRegistrationFailed without firing HTTP) and to an
      offline brain (the local persisted record is wiped on
      unregister() even if the DELETE call fails).

  - id: push-deep-link-routing
    title: Push notification deep-link routing
    summary: |
      The "tap the notification → open the right helm screen"
      pipeline.  PushNotificationRouter (pure-Dart, in
      push_notification_router.dart) decodes a notification's
      `data` map into a typed PushTapPayload (RatifyLeadTap |
      JobDetailTap | UnknownPushTap) and pushes the right named
      route via the injected NavigatorSink.  push_handlers.dart
      wires the router into FirebaseMessaging.onMessage,
      onMessageOpenedApp, and getInitialMessage callbacks +
      flutter_local_notifications for the foreground banner.
      Unknown screens are logged (StdoutLogSink in production,
      RecordingLogSink in tests) so a brain-side event type added
      without a matching mobile route is visible in QA.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/push/push_notification_router.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/push/push_handlers.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/push/push_handlers_test.dart
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase C.  The `/ratify` route
      itself is owned by D-O5m.followup-7 (voice/text input bar +
      ratification card); until that PR lands, taps with
      screen=ratify reach the navigator's onUnknownRoute fallback
      and the helm logs a warning.  `/job/<id>` is already wired
      via HomeScreen → JobListScreen → JobDetailScreen.  Adding a
      new push event type means: (1) emit a new `screen=<name>`
      from the brain dispatcher; (2) add a case to decodePushTap +
      routeTap; (3) register the named route on MaterialApp.
      No global state — the router is constructed per call site
      with the same shared NavigatorSink + LogSink.

  - id: apns-entitlement-ios
    title: APNs entitlement (iOS)
    summary: |
      The `aps-environment` entitlement at
      apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Runner/Runner.entitlements that tells
      iOS which APNs gateway to register the device with.
      `development` → api.sandbox.push.apple.com (Debug builds);
      `production` → api.push.apple.com (TestFlight / App Store
      builds).  Tokens are gateway-specific — a sandbox token sent
      to production fails with BadDeviceToken / BadEnvironmentKey
      InToken, which the brain dispatcher catches and clears
      `cert.push_platform` to stop spamming the dead token.  The
      runbook (docs/operator-runbooks/push-notification-setup.md)
      walks the operator through flipping the entitlement before
      release.  AppDelegate.swift forwards the APNs device token
      to Messaging.messaging().apnsToken so the
      firebase_messaging plugin's getAPNSToken() resolves.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Runner/Runner.entitlements
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Runner/AppDelegate.swift
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Runner/Info.plist
      - docs/operator-runbooks/push-notification-setup.md
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase C.  Info.plist also gets
      NSUserNotificationsUsageDescription (the iOS authorization
      prompt copy), UIBackgroundModes = [fetch, remote-notification]
      (so silent pushes deliver while the app is suspended), and
      FirebaseAppDelegateProxyEnabled = true (lets the
      firebase_messaging plugin swizzle into the app-delegate
      callbacks).

  - id: google-services-json-android
    title: google-services.json (Android FCM config)
    summary: |
      Per-tenant Firebase project config the google-services
      Gradle plugin parses at build time to synthesise the resource
      entries firebase_core consumes at runtime.  Lives at
      apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/app/google-services.json.  The
      repo ships a syntactically-valid PLACEHOLDER file (the
      project_number / api_key fields are nonsense fillers) so
      `flutter build apk` works in CI without leaking real
      credentials; the operator overwrites it with the real per-
      tenant file at deploy time per the runbook
      (docs/operator-runbooks/push-notification-setup.md §FCM
      Android).  The Gradle plugin wiring lives in
      android/build.gradle.kts (classpath
      com.google.gms:google-services:4.4.2) +
      android/app/build.gradle.kts (id "com.google.gms.google-
      services").
    sources:
