```yml
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/build.gradle.kts
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/app/build.gradle.kts
      - docs/operator-runbooks/push-notification-setup.md
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-9 Phase C.  AndroidManifest also
      gains: POST_NOTIFICATIONS permission (Android 13+ runtime
      grant), WAKE_LOCK (high-priority FCM messages wake the
      device), default_notification_channel_id metadata
      (oddjobz_default_channel — must match the channel
      flutter_local_notifications creates at boot), and
      firebase_analytics_collection_enabled = false (the helm
      doesn't ship analytics; operators flip via tenant manifest
      if telemetry is opt-in).

  - id: mesh-transport-mobile
    canonical: mesh-transport (mobile)
    aliases:
      - MeshTransport (Dart)
      - mobile mesh transport seam
    short: |
      The Dart abstraction the oddjobz mobile shell uses to send +
      receive SignedBundles.  Two backends: ShardProxyMeshTransport
      (real mesh path) and HttpReplFallbackTransport (backward-compat
      path).  Factory selects at app startup based on shard-proxy
      reachability.
    definition: |
      The *MeshTransport (mobile)* is the Dart-side seam at
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/mesh_transport.dart`.  It
      abstracts the wire layer the outbox uses to publish
      SignedBundles to a peer (typically the brain), and the receive
      stream addressed bundles flow in on.  Two backends: the
      [shard-proxy-client-dart]-driven `ShardProxyMeshTransport` (the
      real mesh path; phone+brain are structurally peers) and the
      `HttpReplFallbackTransport` (backward-compat path; routes by
      payload_type to the existing per-kind uploaders +
      ReplClient).  `MeshTransportFactory.select()` runs a
      reachability probe at app startup and picks the right backend;
      operators re-probe via the helm settings screen's "Refresh
      transport" button.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/mesh_transport.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/shard_proxy_client.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/outbox/mesh_outbox_builder.dart
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-6 Phase 2.  Phase 1 shipped the Dart
      SignedBundle codec with cross-language byte parity (#329); this
      Phase 2 stitches that codec into the outbox + a transport seam
      so the brain becomes structurally peer-equivalent (per D-W1
      Phase 4 architectural intent).

  - id: shard-proxy-client-dart
    canonical: ShardProxyClient (Dart)
    aliases:
      - shard-proxy mobile client
      - Dart shard-proxy
    short: |
      Pure-Dart HTTP client mobile uses to publish SignedBundles to a
      shard-proxy relay + long-poll for incoming bundles addressed to
      the device.  Mirrors the operations on the TS shard-proxy-
      client (`core/protocol-types/src/overlay/shard-proxy-client.ts`)
      but speaks HTTP instead of UDP because mobile can't open raw
      sockets without iOS entitlement gymnastics.
    definition: |
      The *ShardProxyClient (Dart)* is the HTTP-layer client at
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/shard_proxy_client.dart` that
      wraps a shard-proxy relay's `POST /publish?shard=<group>` +
      long-polled `GET /subscribe?shard=<group>&recipient=<cert-id>`
      endpoints.  Publishes the canonical SignedBundle wire bytes
      (per the codec post-#329) and decodes the relay's JSON-array
      response into SignedBundle objects, filtering by recipient
      cert id defensively.  Network errors trigger exponential
      backoff with reconnect.  Tests inject a mocked Dio so the
      seam is verified without standing up a real relay.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/shard_proxy_client.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/mesh/shard_proxy_client_test.dart
      - core/protocol-types/src/overlay/shard-proxy-client.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-6 Phase 2.  The relay's wire shape is
      a substrate concern — different operator deployments can plug
      in different relay implementations (bitcoin-shard-proxy with
      an HTTP front, a tenant-owned Semantos Brain serving as a relay,
      etc.).  The Dart client speaks the minimal HTTP contract:
      bundles in, bundles out, addressed by recipient cert id.

  - id: mesh-transport-fallback
    canonical: HTTP-REPL fallback transport
    aliases:
      - HttpReplFallbackTransport
      - mesh fallback path
    short: |
      Backward-compat mobile transport for environments without
      shard-proxy reachability.  Routes by SignedBundle.payload_type
      to the existing per-kind uploaders (DioAttachmentUploader,
      VoiceExtractFlushUploader) and the ReplClient.  Receive stream
      is empty — incoming live-updates ride the existing WSS path.
    definition: |
      The *HTTP-REPL fallback transport* is the second backend
      `MeshTransport` ships, at `mesh_transport.dart` →
      `HttpReplFallbackTransport`.  Switches on the bundle's
      payload_type to dispatch to the existing per-kind uploaders
      (`oddjobz.attachment.create` →
      `DioAttachmentUploader.upload`; `oddjobz.voice-extract` →
      `VoiceExtractFlushUploader.upload`; `oddjobz.cell.create` →
      `ReplClient.send`) so the helm UI keeps working when the
      shard-proxy is unreachable or unconfigured.  `incoming()`
      returns `Stream.empty()` because HTTP-REPL doesn't have a
      native receive stream — incoming live-updates ride the
      existing WSS path.  The factory selects this backend when the
      shard-proxy reachability probe fails or the [mesh] section is
      absent in the brain's tenant manifest.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/mesh/mesh_transport.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/mesh/mesh_transport_test.dart
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-6 Phase 2.  The brief is explicit
      that this fallback path is preserved for environments without
      shard-proxy reachability — the mesh transport is opt-in per
      deployment, and the fallback ensures the helm UI keeps
      working in restricted networks (operator deploys without a
      [mesh] section, mobile shell behind a corporate proxy that
      blocks long-poll, etc.).

  - id: info-endpoint
    canonical: /api/v1/info endpoint
    aliases:
      - info endpoint
      - GET /api/v1/info
      - brain info endpoint
    short: |
      Bearer-gated GET endpoint mobile + federation peers fetch
      post-pairing to discover the brain's mesh substrate config:
      shard-proxy URL (or null), shard group id, brain pin cert +
      pubkey, server version.  Drives the MeshTransportFactory
      decision.
    definition: |
      The */api/v1/info endpoint* is the discovery seam mobile +
      federation peers use to learn the brain's mesh substrate
      configuration.  `GET /api/v1/info` (bearer-gated) returns a
      JSON envelope with `shard_proxy_endpoint` (string URL or
      `null` when [mesh] is absent in the tenant manifest),
      `shard_group_id`, `brain_pin_cert_id`, `brain_pin_pubkey`,
      and `server_version`.  Mobile fetches this once post-pairing
      and caches it in ChildCertStore; the MeshTransportFactory
      reads the cached endpoint to decide whether to construct a
      ShardProxyMeshTransport or fall back to HttpReplFallback.  The
      brain pin fields surface the operator's root cert id +
      pubkey so the helm "verify your brain" view can re-assert the
      TOFU pin out-of-band.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/info_http.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/info_http_test.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5m.followup-6 Phase 2.  Bearer-gated by design:
      a casual scanner shouldn't be able to enumerate shard-proxy
      URLs.  When the [mesh] section is absent in the manifest,
      `shard_proxy_endpoint` is JSON null + `shard_group_id` is
      empty — mobile sees this and skips the mesh path,
      structurally indistinguishable from "operator hasn't
      enabled mesh sync yet."

  - id: secure-signing-key-mobile
    canonical: secure-signing-key-mobile
    aliases:
      - secure-signing-key-mobile
      - secure-signing-key
      - secure key handle
      - SecureSigningKeyAdapter
    short: |
      Adapter abstraction for the device's signing priv that wraps
      iOS Keychain (with biometric-gated `SecAccessControl`) on
      iOS and `EncryptedSharedPreferences` on Android.  Replaces
      the raw 64-hex priv slot in flutter_secure_storage; the
      legacy slot stays present for backward compatibility.
    definition: |
      The *secure-signing-key-mobile* surface is the
      `SecureSigningKeyAdapter` interface in
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/identity/secure_signing_key.dart`
      with two implementations: the
      `PlatformSecureSigningKeyAdapter` (production, dispatches to
      native iOS Swift / Android Kotlin via the
      `semantos.oddjobz/secure_signing_key` MethodChannel) and the
      `InMemorySecureSigningKeyAdapter` (pure-Dart, used by the
      unit-test suite + as a degraded fallback when the native
      handler isn't wired in).  The adapter exposes
      `generateNew(label) → {keyHandle, publicKey}`,
      `sign(keyHandle, message) → 64-byte (r||s) signature`,
      `delete(keyHandle)`, and `exists(keyHandle)`; the priv bytes
      are written to the platform secure store at generate time
      and not returned across the channel.  D-O5m.followup-2.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/identity/secure_signing_key.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/identity/platform_secure_signing_key_adapter.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Runner/SecureSigningKey.swift
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/app/src/main/kotlin/info/oddjobtodd/oddjobz_mobile/SecureSigningKey.kt
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/identity/secure_signing_key_test.dart
      - docs/operator-runbooks/secure-signing-key-migration.md
    notes: |
      Honest scope (mirrored in the runbook): secp256k1 is NOT a
      Secure Enclave-supported curve (SE only does NIST P-256) and
      AndroidKeyStore EC keys are restricted to NIST curves
      (P-256/P-384/P-521).  So the priv DOES briefly enter process
      memory during sign operations — both natively (Keychain → Data
      blob → libsecp256k1 in userspace) and in the InMemoryAdapter
      fallback (Uint8List → pointycastle).  The migration adds
      at-rest encryption + biometric gating + key revocation but
      is NOT a true "key never leaves enclave" implementation;
      that's a future revision (D-O5m.followup-2-bis) requiring
      either a curve change or a JNI/CMake-built libsecp256k1
      running in a secure context.  The wire shape of a
      Keychain-backed signature is identical to a raw-priv
      signature (64-byte r||s, low-s normalised) — the brain-side
      verifier accepts both unchanged because both paths produce
      ECDSA-secp256k1-sha256 signatures over the same canonical
      preimage.

  - id: keychain-backed-priv
    canonical: keychain-backed-priv
    aliases:
      - keychain-backed-priv
      - keychain-backed signing key
      - iOS Keychain priv handle
    short: |
      iOS-side implementation of the `SecureSigningKeyAdapter`
      contract.  Stores the 32-byte secp256k1 priv as a
      `kSecClassGenericPassword` Keychain item with
      `kSecAttrAccessibleAfterFirstUnlockThisDeviceOnly` +
      `SecAccessControl(.userPresence)` requiring a fresh
      Face ID / Touch ID / passcode prompt on every read.
    definition: |
      The *keychain-backed-priv* surface is the iOS implementation
      of `secure-signing-key-mobile` in
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Runner/SecureSigningKey.swift`.  Key
      generation uses GigaBitcoin's
      `secp256k1.swift` library (vendored via CocoaPods,
      `pod 'secp256k1.swift'`).  The Keychain entry is namespaced
      under `kSecAttrService =
      info.oddjobtodd.oddjobz_mobile.secure_signing_key` and
      `kSecAttrAccount = d-o5m.followup-2.secure_signing_key.<handle>`
      so the Keychain query surface stays scoped to the
      app's own slot.  Sign operations call
      `SecKeyCopyMatching` (which fires the biometric prompt) and
      then `secp256k1.swift.Signing.PrivateKey.signature(for:)` to
      produce a 64-byte compact (r||s) signature.  D-O5m.followup-2.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Runner/SecureSigningKey.swift
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Podfile
    notes: |
      The priv enters process memory during sign — see the
      honest-scope note in `secure-signing-key-mobile`.  The
      Keychain layer's value is at-rest encryption (the entry is
      wrapped by a key that lives in Secure Enclave on devices
      that have one) + per-read biometric gating, NOT
      enclave-resident signing.  A future revision moves to
      `kSecAttrTokenIDSecureEnclave` + `SecKeyCreateSignature`,
      which would require switching to a P-256 cell signer or
      adding a P-256 cert track alongside secp256k1.

  - id: androidkeystore-backed-priv
    canonical: androidkeystore-backed-priv
    aliases:
      - androidkeystore-backed-priv
      - AndroidKeyStore-backed signing key
      - Android EncryptedSharedPreferences priv
    short: |
      Android-side implementation of the
      `SecureSigningKeyAdapter` contract.  Stores the 32-byte
      secp256k1 priv inside `EncryptedSharedPreferences` (with an
      AndroidKeyStore-derived AES-256-GCM master key that has
      `setUserAuthenticationRequired(true)`) and signs via
      BouncyCastle.
    definition: |
      The *androidkeystore-backed-priv* surface is the Android
      implementation of `secure-signing-key-mobile` in
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/app/src/main/kotlin/info/oddjobtodd/oddjobz_mobile/SecureSigningKey.kt`.
      Key generation uses BouncyCastle's `ECKeyPairGenerator`
      with the `SECNamedCurves.secp256k1` domain; the priv is
      hex-encoded and stored in an `EncryptedSharedPreferences`
      file (`info.oddjobtodd.oddjobz_mobile.secure_signing_key`)
      whose master key is obtained via
      `MasterKey.Builder.setUserAuthenticationRequired(true, 0)`
      so reads require a fresh BiometricPrompt success.  Signing
      uses `ECDSASigner(HMacDSAKCalculator(SHA256Digest()))` to
      produce RFC 6979 deterministic-k signatures, low-s normalised
      to 64-byte compact (r||s).  AndroidKeyStore native EC keys
      are restricted to NIST P-256/P-384/P-521 — secp256k1 has to
      be done in userspace.  D-O5m.followup-2.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/app/src/main/kotlin/info/oddjobtodd/oddjobz_mobile/SecureSigningKey.kt
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/app/build.gradle.kts
    notes: |
      Three Gradle deps land with this entry:
      `org.bouncycastle:bcprov-jdk18on` (secp256k1 primitives),
      `androidx.security:security-crypto`
      (EncryptedSharedPreferences + AndroidKeyStore master key),
      and `androidx.biometric:biometric` (BiometricPrompt for
      the explicit Settings → Migrate-now prompt).  StrongBox
      backing is opportunistic — `setRequestStrongBoxBacked(true)`
      isn't currently set on the master key spec; it could be
      added in a future revision after we measure the device-class
      compatibility hit.

  - id: biometric-gated-signing
    canonical: biometric-gated-signing
    aliases:
      - biometric-gated-signing
      - biometric-gated cell signature
      - per-sign biometric prompt
    short: |
      Property of the secure-signing-key-mobile surface: every
      `sign(keyHandle, message)` call triggers a fresh OS
      biometric prompt (Face ID / Touch ID on iOS, fingerprint /
      face on Android).  Falls back to device passcode when no
      biometrics are enrolled.
    definition: |
      *Biometric-gated signing* is the user-experience property of
      the `secure-signing-key-mobile` surface that requires a
      fresh OS biometric (or device-passcode) authentication on
      every cell signature.  iOS path: the Keychain entry's
      `SecAccessControl` is created with `.userPresence` flags so
      the read fires `LocalAuthentication`'s biometric prompt
      (with the operation prompt "Authorize signing for the
      oddjobz operator device.") before returning the priv blob.
      Android path: the `EncryptedSharedPreferences` master key
      is built with
      `setUserAuthenticationRequired(true, /*durationSeconds=*/0)`
      — auth-per-use mode — so the master key unlock requires a
      `BiometricPrompt` success and there is no validity-window
      cache.  D-O5m.followup-2.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/ios/Runner/SecureSigningKey.swift
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/app/src/main/kotlin/info/oddjobtodd/oddjobz_mobile/SecureSigningKey.kt
      - docs/operator-runbooks/secure-signing-key-migration.md
    notes: |
      Operators on kiosk-style devices (e.g. a tablet at a job
      site shared by multiple tradies) may want to disable the
      per-sign prompt to reduce friction.  Today this is achieved
      by NOT wiring the SecureSigningKeyAdapter at app boot —
      pairing falls through to the legacy raw-priv path and there
      is no biometric prompt.  A future revision exposes a
      Settings toggle that switches the access-control flags
      between `.userPresence` and `.devicePasscode`-only without
      a re-pair.

  - id: site-config-resource
    canonical: site_config dispatcher resource
    aliases:
      - site-config-resource
      - site_config.read
      - site_config.write
      - whole-blob site config handler
    short: |
      Dispatcher resource at `runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/
      site_config_handler.zig` that exposes `read` + `write`
      commands for `<sites_dir>/<domain>/site.json` as a single
      atomic blob.  Cap-gated on `cap.brain.admin`; the `write`
      path validates via `site_config.parseJson` before doing a
      write-to-temp + rename so a rejected payload never
      replaces the on-disk file.  Sits alongside
      `sites-dispatcher-resource` (which ships targeted edits
      like route_add / set_listen_port) — the whole-blob
      handler exists specifically so the helm SPA editor can
      Save the entire JSON in one round-trip without losing
      operator whitespace + ordering.
    definition: |
      *site_config dispatcher resource* is the brain-side seam
      introduced by D-O5.followup-5 for the helm SPA's site
      config editor view.  Two commands:
      `read {domain}` returns `{domain, json, size, mtime_unix}`
      where `json` is the raw on-disk site.json bytes verbatim;
      the handler round-trips through `site_config.parseJson`
      first so a corrupt-on-disk file surfaces as
      `validation_failed` rather than handing garbage to the
      editor.  `write {domain, json, dry_run?}` validates via
      the same parser and, when `dry_run` is unset, atomically
      replaces the file via the same write-to-temp + rename
      dance `sites_handler` uses (mirrored bit-for-bit so
      atomicity behaviour is identical across both handlers).
      `dry_run:true` runs validation only and returns
      `{ok:true, dry_run:true}` so the editor's "Validate"
      button can pre-flight a draft.  Read is classified as
      audit-skippable via `is_read_fn` for future opt-out;
      writes always emit the dispatcher's begin/complete pair.
      The handler is registered in `cmdRepl` (REPL operators
      get `site config show / set / validate` verbs) and
      `cmdServe` with `--enable-repl` (helm SPA hits the same
      dispatcher seam via `/api/v1/repl`).
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/resources/site_config_handler.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/site_config_handler_conformance.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/repl.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/cli.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-5 (2026-05-02).  Reuses
      `cap.brain.admin` rather than minting a new `cap.helm.admin`
      — the existing root authority cap is the canonical
      operator-root marker.  The handler's mutex serialises
      writes within ONE brain process; cross-process serialisation
      remains the same TODO `sites_handler` carries (flock(2) on
      a sibling lock file), pending a real concurrency case.
      Companion view: site-config-editor-helm.

  - id: site-config-editor-helm
    canonical: helm site config editor view
    aliases:
      - site-config-editor-helm
      - SiteConfigEditor.svelte
      - helm site config editor
    short: |
      Operator-root Svelte view (`apps/loom-svelte/src/views/
      SiteConfigEditor.svelte`) that loads the on-disk site.json
      via `site_config.read`, lets the operator hand-edit the
      JSON in a textarea, and atomically saves via
      `site_config.write`.  Side panel renders a parsed routes
      list; clicking a row jumps the textarea selection to the
      matching path.
    definition: |
      *helm site config editor view* is the operator-facing
      surface of the D-O5.followup-5 site config editor.  Loads
      `<sites_dir>/<domain>/site.json` on mount via
      `loadSiteConfig` (lib/site-config-store.ts), populates a
      monospace textarea, and tracks dirty state so Save +
      Discard light up only when the buffer has changed.  Save
      pre-validates the JSON locally (no network call when the
      operator left a stray comma), then dispatches
      `saveSiteConfig` which minifies the buffer, sends
      `site config set <domain> <minified>` over the bearer-
      gated REPL endpoint, and renders the brain's
      `written_at` timestamp in the status row.  Validate runs
      the same pipeline with `dry_run:true` so the operator can
      confirm a draft parses without committing.  The side
      panel renders a route summary (path / type / auth) sniffed
      from the editor's current text — re-derives on every
      keystroke so the operator sees their edits reflected in
      the parsed view.  Clicking a route row jumps the
      textarea's selection range to the matching path string,
      best-effort find-and-highlight without a full code-editor
      dependency.  Wired as a tab in App.svelte alongside Jobs
      / Customers / etc.; visibility is not gated client-side
      (the brain's cap.brain.admin requirement surfaces via the
      typed error UX when a non-admin caller tries to Load /
      Save).
    sources:
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/views/SiteConfigEditor.svelte
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/site-config-store.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/App.svelte
      - apps/loom-svelte/tests/site-config-editor.test.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-5 (2026-05-02).  The textarea is
      plain-text — picking up monaco-editor or codemirror was
      considered but rejected for v0.1: a tenant operator
      editing 5–20 routes by hand doesn't need IntelliSense;
      the brain-side parser is the canonical validator and its
      typed errors are surfaced inline.  A future revision
      could swap the textarea for a code editor with JSON
      schema awareness — the Save / Validate pipeline is
      decoupled from the editor backing so the swap is a
      view-only churn.

  - id: tenant-theme-config
    canonical: tenant theme config (`[theme]` block)
    aliases:
      - tenant-theme-config
      - manifest theme block
      - "[theme]"
    short: |
      Optional `[theme]` section in the tenant manifest carrying
      operator-set primary color, accent color, logo URL, font
      family, and dark/light mode preference.  Both helms (loom-
      svelte desktop + oddjobz-mobile Flutter) read the resolved
      values via `GET /api/v1/info`; defaults are substituted
      inline when the block is absent.
    definition: |
      *tenant theme config* is a per-tenant branding declaration
      that lives next to `[branding]` / `[mesh]` / etc. in the
      tenant manifest (`runtime/semantos-brain/src/tenant_manifest.zig`).
      Five string fields:
        • `primary_hex` — operator's primary brand color (`#RRGGBB`).
        • `accent_hex` — accent / success color (`#RRGGBB`).
        • `logo_url` — optional, ≤ 500 chars, `/`-rooted or
          `https://`.  `http://` is rejected so a logo never
          downgrades an HTTPS helm.
        • `font_family` — `system` | `serif` | `mono` | a free-
          form CSS font-stack ≤ 200 chars.
        • `mode` — `light` | `dark` | `auto`.
      All fields are optional; an absent block yields the
      canonical defaults (indigo-600 primary, emerald-500 accent,
      no logo, system font, auto mode) which the brain
      substitutes inline at the `/api/v1/info` seam so no client
      ships its own.  See theme-default-fallback for the
      defaults' single-source-of-truth model.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/tenant_manifest.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/tenant_manifest_conformance.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-6 (2026-05-02).  Validation is
      strict on the colors (7-char `#RRGGBB`, 3-char shorthand
      rejected so the wire shape has a single canonical form)
      and on `mode` (enum); `font_family` is a length-bounded
      free-form string.  The encoder round-trips the block on
      manifest archive write so the operator-supplied values
      survive `/etc/semantos/tenants/<domain>.toml` re-write.

  - id: theme-store-helm
    canonical: helm theme store (loom-svelte)
    aliases:
      - theme-store-helm
      - loom-svelte theme-store
      - theme-store.ts
    short: |
      Svelte writable + initialiser at `apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/
      theme-store.ts`.  Fetches `/api/v1/info` post-auth, applies
      the resolved theme via CSS custom properties on `:root`
      (`--color-primary`, `--color-accent`, `--theme-font-family`),
      and toggles `data-mode` on `<html>` based on the operator's
      mode preference + `prefers-color-scheme`.
    definition: |
      *helm theme store* is loom-svelte's runtime adapter for
      the `tenant-theme-config`.  On mount, App.svelte calls
      `loadTheme(brainBaseUrl, bearer)` which GETs
      `/api/v1/info`, parses the `theme` block via
      `parseInfoThemeBlock` (tolerant of missing fields →
      `DEFAULT_THEME`), and pushes the result through:
        1. `applyThemeToDocument` — writes
           `--color-primary`, `--color-accent`,
           `--theme-font-family` CSS custom properties on
           `:root`.  Migrated stylesheet rules
           (`nav button.active { color: var(--color-primary) }`,
           `a { color: var(--color-accent) }`,
           `body { font: 14px/1.5 var(--theme-font-family) }`,
           `.brand-logo { … }`) read these vars so the load-
           bearing surfaces (top nav active button, links,
           font, logo placement) re-render under the operator's
           palette.
        2. `data-mode` attribute on `<html>` — `light` /
           `dark` / `auto` (auto follows the OS via
           `matchMedia('(prefers-color-scheme: dark)')`).  The
           CSS has a `html[data-mode="light"]` ladder for the
           load-bearing surfaces only; the dark palette stays
           the default.
      The store exposes a Svelte `Readable<Theme>` so views can
      reactively bind to `$theme.logoUrl` (rendered in the nav
      header when set).  Network failures + 401s leave the
      store at its current value (initially `DEFAULT_THEME`)
      and rethrow — App.svelte's onMount swallows the error so
      a transient network blip never blanks the SPA.
    sources:
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/theme-store.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/App.svelte
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/app.css
      - apps/loom-svelte/tests/theme-store.test.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-6 (2026-05-02).  CSS migration is
      scoped to top nav + primary buttons + links + logo
      placement per the brief — the rest of the existing dark
      palette stays hard-coded so this PR doesn't churn unrelated
      styling.  A future revision could migrate every color to
      CSS custom properties (the migration plan is "find-replace
      hex literals with `var(--…)`" once the operator-facing
      design tokens are stable).

  - id: tenant-theme-mobile
    canonical: tenant theme service (oddjobz-mobile Flutter)
    aliases:
      - tenant-theme-mobile
      - theme_service.dart
      - oddjobz-mobile theme service
    short: |
      Flutter ThemeService at `apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/theme/
      theme_service.dart` (pure-Dart core) +
      `theme_service_flutter.dart` (Flutter glue).  Fetches
      `/api/v1/info` post-pairing, caches the resolved theme in
      SecureStore, and exposes a `ValueNotifier<TenantTheme>`
      that MaterialApp's `ValueListenableBuilder` rebuilds on.
    definition: |
      *tenant theme service (mobile)* is the oddjobz-mobile
      runtime adapter for the `tenant-theme-config`.  Split
      into a flutter-free pure-Dart core (`ThemeServiceCore`,
      `TenantTheme`, `parseTenantTheme`) so unit tests run
      under `dart test` without the Flutter SDK loaded, plus a
      thin Flutter wrapper that adapts the core's
      `Stream<TenantTheme>` to a `ValueNotifier<TenantTheme>`
      and projects `TenantTheme` to `ThemeData` /
      `ThemeMode` for MaterialApp.
      Lifecycle:
        1. App boot — `themeService.warmFromCache()` reads the
           SecureStore-persisted theme into the notifier so the
           first MaterialApp render uses the operator's brand
           even before the first network call.  Fresh installs
           render with `TenantTheme.defaults`.
        2. Post-auth — AuthRouter calls
           `themeService.fetch()` which GETs `/api/v1/info`
           with the persisted bearer, parses the `theme` block,
           and (a) updates the notifier (MaterialApp rebuilds)
           and (b) persists the JSON-encoded theme to
           SecureStore for the next launch.
        3. Network failures fall back to `cached()` (or
           defaults if the cache is empty) — theme is cosmetic;
           an unreachable brain never blocks job filing.
      The `font_family` shorthand maps to Flutter's `fontFamily`
      slot (`system` → null/platform default, `serif` →
      `'serif'`, `mono` → `'monospace'`, custom → free-form
      stack passed verbatim).  `mode = auto` resolves to
      `ThemeMode.system` so Flutter follows the OS preference.
    sources:
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/theme/theme_service.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/theme/theme_service_flutter.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/main.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/app.dart
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/test/theme/theme_service_test.dart
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-6 (2026-05-02).  The pure-Dart
      / Flutter split mirrors the rest of the codebase
      (push_handlers / push_notification_router; secure_signing_key
      / platform_secure_signing_key_adapter): pure-Dart core
      where the load-bearing logic lives, Flutter wrapper where
      the SDK is genuinely required.  SecureStore caching uses
      the namespaced `d-o5.followup-6.v1.tenant_theme` slot so
      a future schema rev can migrate without colliding.

  - id: theme-default-fallback
    canonical: theme default fallback
    aliases:
      - theme-default-fallback
      - canonical theme defaults
      - THEME_DEFAULT_*
    short: |
      Single-source-of-truth theme defaults
      (`#4F46E5` primary, `#10B981` accent, no logo, `system`
      font, `auto` mode) declared as constants in
      `tenant_manifest.zig` and substituted inline by
      `/api/v1/info` when the operator hasn't configured a
      `[theme]` block.  Helms read what they're handed; they
      do not ship their own copies of the defaults.
    definition: |
      *theme default fallback* is the contract that says the
      brain — never the helm — owns the canonical theme
      defaults.  When `[theme]` is absent in the tenant
      manifest, every field on `info_http.Acceptor.theme` is
      empty; the handler substitutes
      `tenant_manifest.THEME_DEFAULT_PRIMARY` /
      `THEME_DEFAULT_ACCENT` / `THEME_DEFAULT_FONT_FAMILY` /
      `THEME_DEFAULT_MODE` inline so the wire-shape `theme`
      block always carries valid values.  `logo_url` is the
      only field that surfaces JSON `null` (no canonical
      default logo exists).  Helms render whatever the brain
      sends; they do hold their own initial-render defaults
      (`DEFAULT_THEME` in theme-store.ts, `TenantTheme.defaults`
      in theme_service.dart) but those exist only so the first
      paint before the first fetch isn't blank — they are kept
      in sync with the brain constants by deliberate code-
      review hygiene, not by build-time generation.  A future
      `pnpm/dart codegen` step could derive both from the Zig
      constants if drift becomes a real risk.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/tenant_manifest.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/info_http.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/info_http_test.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-6 (2026-05-02).  The `defaults
      inline` rule is the same as `[mesh]`'s
      `shard_proxy_endpoint = null` semantics — both make the
      brain the single point where the operator's choice gets
      resolved against the canonical contract.

  - id: multi-hat-helm-sessions
    canonical: multi-hat helm sessions
    aliases:
      - multi-hat-helm-sessions
      - hat-sessions store
      - helm.hat-sessions.v1
    short: |
      Multi-bearer session store for the loom-svelte helm
      (`apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/hat-sessions.ts`).  Replaces
      the single-bearer `helm.bearer` localStorage key from
      D-O5.followup-2 with a typed list of `HatSession`
      records (one per paired hat) plus an `activeId` pointer.
      ReplClient reads the active session on every `send` so
      hat switches take effect immediately.
    definition: |
      *multi-hat helm sessions* is the operator-side seam that
      lets one helm SPA hold bearer tokens for multiple hats
      simultaneously (e.g. a tradie hat + a PM hat per the
      D-O11 federation work).  Persisted as a single JSON
      object under `localStorage["helm.hat-sessions.v1"]`.
      Each `HatSession` carries `id` (client-generated UUIDv4),
      `hatId` (from cert.context_tag namespace), `hatName`
      (operator-friendly display name), `certId` (32-hex —
      empty until D-O11 wires bearer→cert linkage), `bearer`
      (64-hex), `brainBaseUrl` (per-tenant override),
      `colorHex` (per-hat tint for the App.svelte top-nav
      strip), `loggedInAt`, and `lastUsedAt` (bumped by
      ReplClient on every send).  Public API:
      `loadSessions()` (with one-time migration of legacy
      `helm.bearer` into a Default session), `addSession`,
      `removeSession` (active-id reassigns to most-recently-
      used remaining session), `setActive`, `getActiveSession`,
      `bumpLastUsed`, `updateSession`.  Backward compat:
      ReplClient's existing explicit `bearer` callback still
      wins over the active session, so legacy callers keep
      working.  401 responses auto-remove the active session
      so the operator isn't trapped in a "bearer rejected"
      loop.  Companion components: hat-switcher-component,
      hat-info-endpoint-extension.
    sources:
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/hat-sessions.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/repl-client.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/tests/hat-sessions.test.ts
      - apps/loom-svelte/tests/repl-client-multi-hat.test.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-8 (2026-05-02).  Mobile shell
      stays single-hat for now (different UX constraints —
      tab switching is less natural on a phone).  The
      `activeId` re-assignment on remove uses
      most-recently-used (highest `lastUsedAt`) rather than
      first/last in list order so a busy "PM hat" doesn't get
      ousted by a long-idle "Ops hat" the operator only paired
      once.

  - id: hat-switcher-component
    canonical: HatSwitcher component (Svelte)
    aliases:
      - hat-switcher-component
      - HatSwitcher.svelte
      - top-nav hat switcher
    short: |
      Top-right Svelte dropdown
      (`apps/loom-svelte/src/components/HatSwitcher.svelte`)
      that renders the active hat's name + color avatar, lists
      every paired hat with Switch/Remove actions, and exposes
      a "Pair another hat" CTA at the bottom.  Switches fire a
      `hat-switched` CustomEvent on `document` so App.svelte
      can re-load the per-tenant theme for the new context.
    definition: |
      *HatSwitcher component* is the visible UI surface for
      the multi-hat-helm-sessions store.  Pure view — never
      mutates the store except via `setActive` /
      `removeSession`.  Each row in the dropdown shows the
      hat name (bold), the cert/hat-id tail (last 6 chars,
      monospace, dim) when populated, and the relative
      lastUsedAt time.  The active row is highlighted; its
      Switch button is hidden (you can't switch to the
      already-active hat).  The "Pair another hat" CTA opens
      the wallet origin in a new tab with `?return_to=` set to
      the helm URL so the auth-callback redirect lands the
      operator back on the helm with a fresh hat session
      imported into the same store.  After every switch the
      component dispatches `new CustomEvent("hat-switched",
      { detail: { activeId } })` on `document`; App.svelte
      listens for this event and re-runs `loadTheme` so the
      visual context refreshes immediately.
    sources:
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/components/HatSwitcher.svelte
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/App.svelte
      - apps/loom-svelte/src/lib/hat-sessions.ts
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-8 (2026-05-02).  The per-hat
      color avatar uses `colorHex` from the session record
      with a `var(--color-primary)` fallback so a brand-new
      paired hat (no operator-picked color yet) still
      renders a visible swatch.  The same color flows into
      App.svelte's top-of-page indicator strip via the
      `activeHatColor` derived; both surfaces re-render
      reactively when the operator sets a per-hat color.

  - id: hat-info-endpoint-extension
    canonical: /api/v1/info hat block extension
    aliases:
      - hat-info-endpoint-extension
      - info_http hat block
      - /api/v1/info hat block
    short: |
      `hat` block added to the `GET /api/v1/info` response
      (runtime/semantos-brain/src/info_http.zig) carrying the calling
      bearer's id + label + cert id.  Lets the helm-side
      HatSwitcher populate `hatName` / `hatId` / `certId` on
      first add instead of stubbing the legacy migration
      values.
    definition: |
      *hat-info-endpoint-extension* is the brain-side
      counterpart to multi-hat-helm-sessions.  When a bearer
      authenticates against `/api/v1/info`, the handler
      resolves the bearer's TokenRecord via
      `bearer_tokens.verifyHex` and emits
      `"hat":{"id":"<32-hex>","name":"<label>","cert_id":""}`
      alongside the existing `theme` / `shard_proxy_endpoint`
      / pin blocks.  `id` is the bearer's TokenRecord id
      (stable across helm restarts); `name` is the operator-
      supplied label from `brain bearer issue --label` (e.g.
      "Todd (tradie)"); `cert_id` is empty for today's
      bearer-only path because the bearer→cert linkage waits
      on D-O11 federation work, but the field is on the wire
      so a future PR can populate it without a schema rev.
      The 401 path (no bearer / bad bearer) carries no hat
      block — the helm interprets that as "this bearer is
      revoked, drop the session" via the auto-remove logic in
      ReplClient.
    sources:
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/info_http.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/tests/info_http_test.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/bearer_tokens.zig
    notes: |
      Introduced D-O5.followup-8 (2026-05-02).  Three brain
      tests assert: hat block populated for known bearer,
      operator-supplied bearer label round-trips through the
      response, 401 carries no hat block.  Future work
      (D-O11): plumb the cert id this bearer was minted under
      through the TokenRecord (or a parallel
      bearer→cert linkage map) so `cert_id` populates.  The
      empty-string contract for "no cert linkage yet" is
      deliberate — distinguishes from a missing field a
      future schema rev might add.

  - id: mobile-build-android-script
    canonical: mobile-build-android-script
    aliases:
      - mobile-build-android-script
      - scripts/build-android-libs.sh
      - build-android-libs
    short: |
      Bash driver at `scripts/build-android-libs.sh` that cross-
      compiles `libsemantos.a` for the three Android ABIs the
      Flutter FFI plugin links against (arm64-v8a, armeabi-v7a,
      x86_64) and stages them under
      `platforms/flutter/semantos_ffi/build/android/<abi>/` where
      the plugin's CMakeLists.txt expects them.
    definition: |
      *mobile-build-android-script* is the Zig cross-compile front-
      end that fills the gap between `flutter build apk` and the
      kernel.  It iterates the three ABIs, runs `zig build static
      -Dtarget=<abi-target> -Doptimize=ReleaseSafe` against
      `src/ffi/`, smoke-checks each output for the load-bearing
      FFI exports (`semantos_init`, `semantos_version`,
      `semantos_execute_script`) via `nm`, and writes a
      `CHANGES.txt` marker that
      `scripts/smoke-test-mobile.sh` reads to skip rebuilds that
      already happened in the last 30 minutes.  Verbs:
      `--abi <one>` builds a single ABI; `--clean` removes staged
      libs + the Zig cache; `--release` swaps to ReleaseFast;
      `--release-safe` is the default and `--debug` is also
      available.  The Android build needs two NDK-compatibility
      flags applied on the Zig module — `single_threaded = true`
      and `stack_check = false` — wired into `src/ffi/build.zig`
      conditional on `target.result.abi.isAndroid()`.  Without
      them the resulting `.a` carries unresolved
      `__tls_get_addr` + `__zig_probe_stack` references that
      break the SHARED `libsemantos.so` wrapper the FFI plugin's
      CMakeLists builds.
    sources:
      - scripts/build-android-libs.sh
      - src/ffi/build.zig
      - platforms/flutter/semantos_ffi/android/CMakeLists.txt
      - docs/operator-runbooks/mobile-build-and-pair.md
    notes: |
      Introduced D-OPS.mobile-smoke-test (2026-05-02).  The Flutter
      FFI plugin's android/CMakeLists.txt got a SHARED-library shim
      in the same PR — the static archive on its own is not
      packageable in an APK because Dart FFI's
      `DynamicLibrary.open('libsemantos.so')` lookup expects a
      shared object, not a `.a`.  The shim wraps the static via a
      `--whole-archive` link block + a one-line `stub.c` so all
      kernel exports are preserved + re-exported through the .so.
      iOS keeps its XCFramework path (`scripts/build-ios.sh`); only
      Android needs the static-to-shared shim.

  - id: mobile-pair-and-smoke
    canonical: mobile-pair-and-smoke
    aliases:
      - mobile-pair-and-smoke
      - mobile-build-and-pair-runbook
      - docs/operator-runbooks/mobile-build-and-pair.md
    short: |
      End-to-end operator runbook at
      `docs/operator-runbooks/mobile-build-and-pair.md` that walks
      from "phone in hand" to "voice command produces a signed
      cell that lands in brain".  Three smoke tests assert the data
      flow: REPL pull-to-refresh, WSS live-tick, and the full
      voice → STT → SIR → 2-PDA → outbox loop.
    definition: |
      *mobile-pair-and-smoke* is the human-readable companion to
      `scripts/build-android-libs.sh` + `scripts/smoke-test-mobile
      .sh`.  Sections B1-B11 cover prerequisites, one-time phone
      setup (USB debugging + adb authorisation), brain build,
      native-libs build, HTTPS configuration (cloudflared as the
      recommended zero-config option; mkcert + Android trust
      import as the offline alternative because device-pair v2's
      `https://`/`wss://` enforcement refuses cleartext brain
      endpoints), brain start, pair-token generation via
      `brain device pair`, APK build/install, the pair flow, the
      three smoke-test scenarios, and a troubleshooting matrix.
      Push notifications are explicitly OUT OF SCOPE — the
      Firebase placeholder from D-O5m.followup-9 (#328) is
      graceful (init wrapped in try/catch) and the sovereign-push
      refactor (D-O5m.followup-9 Phase D) ships in a follow-up
      PR; the runbook documents both the placeholder behaviour
      and the planned replacement so operators don't waste time
      debugging push during the smoke test.
    sources:
      - docs/operator-runbooks/mobile-build-and-pair.md
      - scripts/build-android-libs.sh
      - scripts/smoke-test-mobile.sh
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/README.md
    notes: |
      Introduced D-OPS.mobile-smoke-test (2026-05-02).  The
      runbook is macOS-first because that's the dev environment
      the substrate ships against today; Linux notes are inline
      where the install commands diverge.  Windows is a separate
      followup runbook (no immediate consumer).  The runbook also
      documents the pre-existing pubspec resolver bug
      (`record 5.x` vs. `record_platform_interface 1.5.0`) plus
      the core-library-desugaring + bouncycastle/jspecify META-INF
      conflicts the same PR resolves in
      `apps/oddjobz-mobile/android/app/build.gradle.kts`, so an
      operator hitting any of those during their first
      `flutter build apk` has a self-service fix path.

  - id: unifiedpush
    title: UnifiedPush (libre push protocol)
    summary: |
      A vendor-neutral push protocol where the operator's device picks
      a *distributor app* (ntfy, NextPush, Conversations, …); the
      distributor mints a per-instance HTTPS endpoint URL; the brain
      POSTs the wake envelope directly to that URL with no auth, no
      provider wrapping, no key signing — the URL itself is the
      capability.  Phase D.3 of the sovereign-push refactor adds it as
      a third backend behind the brain's PushPlatform enum, alongside
      `apns` (iOS) and `fcm` (Android Firebase).  Android operators who
      install a distributor (and optionally self-host one) can run the
      entire wake loop off Google services; iOS operators stay on APNs
      because the Apple sandbox bans alternative wake mechanisms.
    sources:
      - https://unifiedpush.org/spec/server/
      - https://unifiedpush.org/users/distributors/
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/unifiedpush_dispatcher.zig
      - runtime/semantos-brain/src/identity_certs.zig
      - apps/oddjobz-mobile/lib/src/push/unified_push_adapter.dart
      - docs/operator-runbooks/push-architecture.md
    notes: |
      Introduced sovereign-push D.3 (PR 3 of 3 in the sovereign-push
      refactor).  D.1 made push payloads wake-only (no operator
      content), D.2 shipped the device-side silent handler, D.3 closes
      the Android sovereignty gap.  The `unifiedpush` Flutter plugin
      (^6.2.0) auto-registers the
      `org.unifiedpush.android.connector.PUSH_EVENT` service via its
      manifest merger — no manual AndroidManifest.xml edits.  Cross-
      language wire-name MUST be exactly `"unifiedpush"` (lower case);
      both the Zig PushPlatform serializer and the Dart enum name spell
      it that way so the brain's parsePostBody picks it up cleanly.

```
